Title:    ------------------------------------------------------------------------
Title:                                     Preface
Title:  
Title:     MOST of the adventures recorded in this book really occurred; one or two
Title:  were experiences of my own, the rest those of boys who were schoolmates of
Title:  mine. Huck Finn is drawn from life; Tom Sawyer also, but not from an
Title:  individual -- he is a combination of the characteristics of three boys whom
Title:  I knew, and therefore belongs to the composite order of architecture.
Title:  
Title:     The odd superstitions touched upon were all prevalent among children and
Title:  slaves in the West at the period of this story -- that is to say, thirty or
Title:  forty years ago.
Title:  
Title:     Although my book is intended mainly for the entertainment of boys and
Title:  girls, I hope it will not be shunned by men and women on that account, for
Title:  
Title:  part of my plan has been to try to pleasantly remind adults of what they
Title:  once were themselves, and of how they felt and thought and talked, and what
Title:  queer enterprises they sometimes engaged in.
Title:  
Title:     THE AUTHOR.
Title:  
Title:     HARTFORD, 1876.
Title:  
Title:                     --------------------------------------
Title:    ------------------------------------------------------------------------
Title:  
Title:                                    Chapter I
Title:  
Title:     "TOM!"
Title:  
Title:     No answer.
Title:  
Title:      "TOM!"
Title:  
Title:     No answer.
Title:  
Title:     "What's gone with that boy, I wonder? You TOM!"
Title:  
Title:     No answer.
Title:  
Title:     The old lady pulled her spectacles down and looked over them about the
Title:  room; then she put them up and looked out under them. She seldom or never
Title:  looked through them for so small a thing as a boy; they were her state pair,
Title:  the pride of her heart, and were built for "style," not service -- she could
Title:  have seen through a pair of stove-lids just as well. She looked perplexed
Title:  for a moment, and then said, not fiercely, but still loud enough for the
Title:  furniture to hear:
Title:  
Title:     "Well, I lay if I get hold of you I'll -- "
Title:  
Title:     She did not finish, for by this time she was bending down and punching
Title:  under the bed with the broom, and so she needed breath to punctuate the
Title:  punches with. She resurrected nothing but the cat.
Title:  
Title:     "I never did see the beat of that boy!"
Title:  
Title:     She went to the open door and stood in it and looked out among the tomato
Title:  vines and "jimpson" weeds that constituted the garden. No Tom. So she lifted
Title:  up her voice at an angle calculated for distance and shouted:
Title:  
Title:     "Y-o-u-u Tom!"
Title:  
Title:     There was a slight noise behind her and she turned just in time to seize
Title:  a small boy by the slack of his roundabout and arrest his flight.
Title:  
Title:     "There! I might 'a' thought of that closet. What you been doing in
Title:  there?"
Title:  
Title:     "Nothing."
Title:  
Title:     "Nothing! Look at your hands. And look at your mouth. What is that
Title:  truck?"
Title:  
Title:      "I don't know, aunt."
Title:  
Title:     "Well, I know. It's jam -- that's what it is. Forty times I've said if
Title:  you didn't let that jam alone I'd skin you. Hand me that switch."
Title:  
Title:     The switch hovered in the air -- the peril was desperate --
Title:  
Title:     "My! Look behind you, aunt!"
Title:  
Title:     The old lady whirled round, and snatched her skirts out of danger. The
Title:  lad fled on the instant, scrambled up the high board-fence, and disappeared
Title:  over it.
Title:  
Title:     His aunt Polly stood surprised a moment, and then broke into a gentle
Title:  laugh.
Title:  
Title:     "Hang the boy, can't I never learn anything? Ain't he played me tricks
Title:  enough like that for me to be looking out for him by this time? But old
Title:  fools is the biggest fools there is. Can't learn an old dog new tricks, as the
Title:  saying is. But my goodness, he never plays them alike, two days, and how is
Title:  a body to know what's coming? He 'pears to know just how long he can torment
Title:  me before I get my dander up, and he knows if he can make out to put me off
Title:  for a minute or make me laugh, it's all down again and I can't hit him a
Title:  lick. I ain't doing my duty by that boy, and that's the Lord's truth,
Title:  goodness knows. Spare the rod and spile the child, as the Good Book says.
Title:  I'm a laying up sin and suffering for us both, I know. He's full of the Old
Title:  Scratch, but laws-a-me! he's my own dead sister's boy, poor thing, and I
Title:  ain't got the heart to lash him, somehow. Every time I let him off, my
Title:  conscience does hurt me so, and every time I hit him my old heart most
Title:  breaks. Well-a-well, man that is born of woman is of few days and full of
Title:  trouble, as the Scripture says, and I reckon it's so. He'll play hookey this
Title:  evening, * and [* Southwestern for "afternoon"] I'll just be obleeged to
Title:  make him work, to-morrow, to punish him. It's mighty hard to make him work
Title:  Saturdays, when all the boys is having holiday, but he hates work more than
Title:  he hates anything else, and I've got to do some of my duty by him, or I'll
Title:  be the ruination of the child."
Title:  
Title:     Tom did play hookey, and he had a very good time. He got back home barely
Title:  in season to help Jim, the small colored boy, saw next-day's wood
Title:  and split the kindlings before supper -- at least he was there in time to
Title:  tell his adventures to Jim while Jim did three-fourths of the work. Tom's
Title:  younger brother (or rather half-brother) Sid was already through with his
Title:  part of the work (picking up chips), for he was a quiet boy, and had no
Title:  adventurous, troublesome ways.
Title:  
Title:     While Tom was eating his supper, and stealing sugar as opportunity
Title:  offered, Aunt Polly asked him questions that were full of guile, and very
Title:  deep -- for she wanted to trap him into damaging revealments. Like many
Title:  other simple-hearted souls, it was her pet vanity to believe she was endowed
Title:  with a talent for dark and mysterious diplomacy, and she loved to
Title:  contemplate her most transparent devices as marvels of low cunning. Said
Title:  she:
Title:  
Title:     "Tom, it was middling warm in school, warn't it?"
Title:  
Title:     "Yes'm."
Title:  
Title:     "Powerful warm, warn't it?"
Title:  
Title:     "Yes'm."
Title:  
Title:     "Didn't you want to go in a-swimming, Tom?"
Title:  
Title:     A bit of a scare shot through Tom -- a touch of uncomfortable suspicion.
Title:  He searched Aunt Polly's face, but it told him nothing. So he said:
Title:  
Title:     "No'm -- well, not very much."
Title:  
Title:     The old lady reached out her hand and felt Tom's shirt, and said:
Title:  
Title:     "But you ain't too warm now, though." And it flattered her to reflect
Title:  that she had discovered that the shirt was dry without anybody knowing that
Title:  that was what she had in her mind. But in spite of her, Tom knew where
Title:  the wind lay, now. So he forestalled what might be the next move:
Title:  
Title:     "Some of us pumped on our heads -- mine's damp yet. See?"
Title:  
Title:     Aunt Polly was vexed to think she had overlooked that bit of
Title:  circumstantial evidence, and missed a trick. Then she had a new inspiration:
Title:  
Title:     "Tom, you didn't have to undo your shirt collar where I sewed it, to pump
Title:  on your head, did you? Unbutton your jacket!"
Title:  
Title:     The trouble vanished out of Tom's face. He opened his jacket. His shirt
Title:  collar was securely sewed.
Title:  
Title:     "Bother! Well, go 'long with you. I'd made sure you'd played hookey and
Title:  been a-swimming. But I forgive ye, Tom. I reckon you're a kind of a singed
Title:  cat, as the saying is -- better'n you look. This time."
Title:  
Title:     She was half sorry her sagacity had miscarried, and half glad that Tom
Title:  had stumbled into obedient conduct for once.
Title:  
Title:     But Sidney said:
Title:  
Title:     "Well, now, if I didn't think you sewed his collar with white thread, but
Title:  it's black."
Title:  
Title:     "Why, I did sew it with white! Tom!"
Title:  
Title:     But Tom did not wait for the rest. As he went out at the door he said:
Title:  
Title:     "Siddy, I'll lick you for that."
Title:  
Title:     In a safe place Tom examined two large needles which were thrust into the
Title:  lapels of his jacket, and had thread bound about them -- one needle carried
Title:  white thread and the other black. He said:
Title:  
Title:     "She'd never noticed if it hadn't been for Sid. Confound it! sometimes
Title:  she sews it with white, and sometimes she sews it with black. I wish to
Title:  geeminy she'd stick to one or t'other -- I can't keep the run of 'em. But I
Title:  bet you I'll lam Sid for that. I'll learn him!"
Title:  
Title:     He was not the Model Boy of the village. He knew the model boy very well
Title:  though -- and loathed him.
Title:  
Title:     Within two minutes, or even less, he had forgotten all his troubles. Not
Title:  because his troubles were one whit less heavy and bitter to him than a man's
Title:  are to a man, but because a new and powerful interest bore them down and
Title:  drove them out of his mind for the time -- just as men's misfortunes are
Title:  forgotten in the excitement of new enterprises. This new interest was a
Title:  valued novelty in whistling, which he had just acquired from a negro, and he
Title:  was suffering to practise it undisturbed. It consisted in a peculiar
Title:  bird-like turn, a sort of liquid warble, produced by touching the tongue to
Title:  the roof of the mouth at short intervals in the midst of the music -- the
Title:  reader probably remembers how to do it, if he has ever been a boy. Diligence
Title:  and attention soon gave him the knack of it, and he strode down the street
Title:  with his mouth full of harmony
Title:  and his soul full of gratitude. He felt much as an astronomer feels who has
Title:  discovered a new planet -- no doubt, as far as strong, deep, unalloyed
Title:  pleasure is concerned, the advantage was with the boy, not the astronomer.
Title:  
Title:     The summer evenings were long. It was not dark, yet. Presently Tom
Title:  checked his whistle. A stranger was before him -- a boy a shade larger than
Title:  himself. A new-comer of any age or either sex was an impressive curiosity in
Title:  the poor little shabby village of St. Petersburg. This boy was well dressed,
Title:  too -- well dressed on a week-day. This was simply astounding. His cap was a
Title:  dainty thing, his close-buttoned blue cloth roundabout was new and natty,
Title:  and so were his pantaloons. He had shoes on -- and it was only Friday. He
Title:  even wore a necktie, a bright bit of ribbon. He had a citified air about him
Title:  that ate into Tom's vitals. The more Tom stared at the splendid marvel, the
Title:  higher he turned up his nose at his finery and the shabbier and shabbier his
Title:  own outfit seemed to him to grow. Neither boy spoke. If one moved, the other
Title:  moved -- but only sidewise, in a circle; they kept face to face and eye to
Title:  eye all the time. Finally Tom said:
Title:  
Title:     "I can lick you!"
Title:  
Title:     "I'd like to see you try it."
Title:  
Title:     "Well, I can do it."
Title:  
Title:     "No you can't, either."
Title:  
Title:     "Yes I can."
Title:  
Title:     "No you can't."
Title:  
Title:     "I can."
Title:  
Title:     "You can't."
Title:  
Title:     "Can!"
Title:  
Title:     "Can't!"
Title:  
Title:     An uncomfortable pause. Then Tom said:
Title:  
Title:     "What's your name?"
Title:  
Title:     "'Tisn't any of your business, maybe."
Title:  
Title:     "Well I 'low I'll make it my business."
Title:  
Title:     "Well why don't you?"
Title:  
Title:     "If you say much, I will."
Title:  
Title:     "Much -- much -- much. There now."
Title:  
Title:     "Oh, you think you're mighty smart, don't you? I could lick you with one
Title:  hand tied behind me, if I wanted to."
Title:  
Title:     "Well why don't you do it? You say you can do it."
Title:  
Title:     "Well I will , if you fool with me."
Title:  
Title:     "Oh yes -- I've seen whole families in the same fix."
Title:  
Title:     "Smarty! You think you're some , now, don't you? Oh, what a hat!"
Title:  
Title:     "You can lump that hat if you don't like it. I dare you to knock it off
Title:  -- and anybody that'll take a dare will suck eggs."
Title:  
Title:     "You're a liar!"
Title:  
Title:     "You're another."
Title:  
Title:     "You're a fighting liar and dasn't take it up."
Title:  
Title:     "Aw -- take a walk!"
Title:  
Title:     "Say -- if you give me much more of your sass I'll take and bounce a rock
Title:  off'n your head."
Title:  
Title:     "Oh, of course you will."
Title:  
Title:     "Well I will ."
Title:  
Title:     "Well why don't you do it then? What do you keep saying you will for? Why
Title:  don't you do it? It's because you're afraid."
Title:  
Title:     "I ain't afraid."
Title:  
Title:     "You are."
Title:  
Title:     "I ain't."
Title:  
Title:     "You are."
Title:  
Title:     Another pause, and more eying and sidling around each other. Presently
Title:  they were shoulder to shoulder. Tom said:
Title:  
Title:     "Get away from here!"
Title:  
Title:     "Go away yourself!"
Title:  
Title:     "I won't."
Title:  
Title:     "I won't either."
Title:  
Title:     So they stood, each with a foot placed at an angle as a brace, and both
Title:  shoving with might and main, and glowering at each other with hate. But
Title:  neither could get an advantage. After struggling till both were hot and
Title:  flushed, each relaxed his strain with watchful caution, and Tom said:
Title:  
Title:     "You're a coward and a pup. I'll tell my big brother on you, and he can
Title:  thrash you with his little finger, and I'll make him do it, too."
Title:  
Title:     "What do I care for your big brother? I've got a brother that's bigger
Title:  than he is -- and what's more, he can throw him over that fence, too." [Both
Title:  brothers were imaginary.]
Title:  
Title:     "That's a lie."
Title:  
Title:     "Your saying so don't make it so."
Title:  
Title:     Tom drew a line in the dust with his big toe, and said:
Title:  
Title:     "I dare you to step over that, and I'll lick you till you can't stand up.
Title:  Anybody that'll take a dare will steal sheep."
Title:  
Title:     The new boy stepped over promptly, and said:
Title:  
Title:     "Now you said you'd do it, now let's see you do it."
Title:  
Title:     "Don't you crowd me now; you better look out."
Title:  
Title:     "Well, you said you'd do it -- why don't you do it?"
Title:  
Title:     "By jingo! for two cents I will do it."
Title:  
Title:     The new boy took two broad coppers out of his pocket and held them out
Title:  with derision. Tom struck them to the ground. In an instant both boys were
Title:  rolling and tumbling in the dirt, gripped together like cats; and for the
Title:  space of a minute they tugged and tore at each other's hair and clothes,
Title:  punched and scratched each other's nose, and covered themselves with dust
Title:  and glory. Presently the confusion took form, and through the fog of battle
Title:  Tom appeared, seated astride the new boy, and pounding him with his fists.
Title:  "Holler 'nuff!" said he.
Title:  
Title:     The boy only struggled to free himself. He was crying -- mainly from
Title:  rage.
Title:  
Title:     "Holler 'nuff!" -- and the pounding went on.
Title:  
Title:     At last the stranger got out a smothered "'Nuff!" and Tom let him up and
Title:  said: "Now that'll learn you. Better look out who you're fooling with next
Title:  time."
Title:  
Title:     The new boy went off brushing the dust from his clothes, sobbing,
Title:  snuffling, and occasionally looking back and shaking his head and
Title:  threatening what he would do to Tom the "next time he caught him out." To
Title:  which Tom responded with jeers, and started off in high feather, and as soon
Title:  as his back was turned the new boy snatched up a stone, threw it and hit him
Title:  between the shoulders and then turned tail and ran like an antelope. Tom
Title:  chased the traitor home, and thus found out where he lived. He then held a
Title:  position at the gate for some time, daring the enemy to come outside, but
Title:  the enemy only made faces at him through the window and declined. At last
Title:  the enemy's mother appeared, and called Tom a bad, vicious, vulgar child,
Title:  and ordered him away. So he went away; but he said he "'lowed" to "lay" for
Title:  that boy.
Title:  
Title:     He got home pretty late that night, and when he climbed cautiously in at
Title:  the window, he uncovered an ambuscade, in the person of his aunt; and when
Title:  she saw the state his clothes were in her resolution to turn his Saturday
Title:  holiday into captivity at hard labor became adamantine in its firmness.
Title:  
Title:    ------------------------------------------------------------------------
Title:  
Title:                                   Chapter II
Title:  
Title:     SATURDAY morning was come, and all the summer world was bright and fresh,
Title:  and brimming with life. There was a song in every heart; and if the heart
Title:  was young the music issued at the lips. There was cheer in every face and a
Title:  spring in every step. The locust-trees were in bloom and the fragrance of
Title:  the blossoms filled the air. Cardiff Hill, beyond the village and above it,
Title:  was green with vegetation and it lay just far enough away to seem a
Title:  Delectable Land, dreamy, reposeful, and inviting.
Title:  
Title:     Tom appeared on the sidewalk with a bucket of whitewash and a
Title:  long-handled brush. He surveyed the fence, and all gladness left him and a
Title:  deep melancholy settled down upon his spirit. Thirty yards of board fence
Title:  nine feet high. Life to him seemed hollow, and existence but a burden.
Title:  Sighing, he dipped his brush and passed it along the topmost plank; repeated
Title:  the operation; did it again; compared the insignificant whitewashed streak
Title:  with the far-reaching continent of unwhitewashed fence, and sat down on a
Title:  tree-box discouraged. Jim came skipping out at the gate with
Title:  a tin pail, and singing Buffalo Gals. Bringing water from the town pump had
Title:  always been hateful work in Tom's eyes, before, but now it did not strike
Title:  him so. He remembered that there was company at the pump. White, mulatto,
Title:  and negro boys and girls were always there waiting their turns, resting,
Title:  trading playthings, quarrelling, fighting, skylarking. And he remembered
Title:  that although the pump was only a hundred and fifty yards off, Jim never got
Title:  back with a bucket of water under an hour -- and even then somebody
Title:  generally had to go after him. Tom said:
Title:  
Title:     "Say, Jim, I'll fetch the water if you'll whitewash some."
Title:  
Title:     Jim shook his head and said:
Title:  
Title:     "Can't, Mars Tom. Ole missis, she tole me I got to go an' git dis water
Title:  an' not stop foolin' roun' wid anybody. She say she spec' Mars Tom gwine to
Title:  ax me to whitewash, an' so she tole me go 'long an' 'tend to my own business
Title:  -- she 'lowed she'd 'tend to de whitewashin'."
Title:  
Title:     "Oh, never you mind what she said, Jim. That's the way she always talks.
Title:  Gimme the bucket -- I won't be gone only a a minute. She won't ever know."
Title:  
Title:     "Oh, I dasn't, Mars Tom. Ole missis she'd take an' tar de head off'n me.
Title:  'Deed she would."
Title:  
Title:     " She! She never licks anybody -- whacks 'em over the head with her
Title:  thimble -- and who cares for that, I'd like to know. She talks awful, but
Title:  don't hurt -- anyways it don't if she don't cry. Jim, I'll give you a marvel.
Title:  I'll give you a white alley!"
Title:  
Title:     Jim began to waver.
Title:  
Title:     "White alley, Jim! And it's a bully taw."
Title:  
Title:     "My! Dat's a mighty gay marvel, I tell you! But Mars Tom I's powerful
Title:  'fraid ole missis -- "
Title:  
Title:     "And besides, if you will I'll show you my sore toe."
Title:  
Title:     Jim was only human -- this attraction was too much for him. He put down
Title:  his pail, took the white alley, and bent over the toe with absorbing
Title:  interest while the bandage was being unwound. In another moment he was
Title:  flying down the street with his pail and a tingling rear, Tom was
Title:  whitewashing with vigor, and Aunt Polly was retiring from the field with a
Title:  slipper in her hand and triumph in her eye. But Tom's energy did not last.
Title:  He began to think of the fun he had planned for this day, and his sorrows
Title:  multiplied. Soon the free boys would come tripping along on all sorts of
Title:  delicious expeditions, and they would make a world of fun of him for having
Title:  to work -- the very thought of it burnt him like fire. He got out his
Title:  worldly wealth and examined it -- bits of toys, marbles, and trash; enough
Title:  to buy an exchange of work, maybe, but not half enough to buy so much as
Title:  half an hour of pure freedom. So he returned his straitened means to his
Title:  pocket, and gave up the idea of trying
Title:  to buy the boys. At this dark and hopeless moment an inspiration burst upon
Title:  him! Nothing less than a great, magnificent inspiration.
Title:  
Title:     He took up his brush and went tranquilly to work. Ben Rogers hove in
Title:  sight presently -- the very boy, of all boys, whose ridicule he had been
Title:  dreading. Ben's gait was the hop-skip-and-jump -- proof enough that his
Title:  heart was light and his anticipations high. He was eating an apple, and
Title:  giving a long, melodious whoop, at intervals, followed by a deep-toned
Title:  ding-dong-dong, ding-dong-dong, for he was personating a steamboat. As he
Title:  drew near, he slackened speed, took the middle of the street, leaned far
Title:  over to star-board and rounded to ponderously and with laborious pomp and
Title:  circumstance -- for he was personating the Big Missouri, and considered
Title:  himself to be drawing nine feet of water. He was boat and captain and
Title:  engine-bells combined, so he had to imagine himself standing on his own
Title:  hurricane-deck giving the orders and executing them:
Title:  
Title:     "Stop her, sir! Ting-a-ling-ling!" The headway ran almost out, and he
Title:  drew up slowly toward the sidewalk.
Title:  
Title:     "Ship up to back! Ting-a-ling-ling!" His arms straightened and stiffened
Title:  down his sides.
Title:  
Title:     "Set her back on the stabboard! Ting-a-ling-ling! Chow! ch-chow-wow!
Title:  Chow!" His right hand, meantime, describing stately circles -- for it was
Title:  representing a forty-foot wheel.
Title:  
Title:     "Let her go back on the labboard! Ting-a-ling-ling! Chow-ch-chow-chow!"
Title:  The left hand began to describe circles.
Title:  
Title:     "Stop the stabboard! Ting-a-ling-ling! Stop the labboard! Come ahead on
Title:  the stabboard! Stop her! Let your outside turn over slow! Ting-a-ling-ling!
Title:  Chow-ow-ow! Get out that head-line! Lively now! Come -- out with your
Title:  spring-line -- what're you about there! Take a turn round that stump with
Title:  the bight of it! Stand by that stage, now -- let her go! Done with the
Title:  engines, sir! Ting-a-ling-ling! Sh't! s'h't! sh't!" (trying the
Title:  gauge-cocks).
Title:  
Title:     Tom went on whitewashing -- paid no attention to the steamboat. Ben
Title:  stared a moment and then said: "Hi- yi ! You're up a stump, ain't you!"
Title:  
Title:     No answer. Tom surveyed his last touch with the eye of an artist, then he
Title:  gave his brush another gentle sweep and surveyed the result, as before. Ben
Title:  ranged up alongside of him. Tom's mouth watered for the apple, but he stuck
Title:  to his work. Ben said:
Title:  
Title:     "Hello, old chap, you got to work, hey?"
Title:  
Title:     Tom wheeled suddenly and said:
Title:  
Title:     "Why, it's you, Ben! I warn't noticing."
Title:  
Title:     "Say -- I'm going in a-swimming, I am. Don't you wish you could? But of
Title:  course you'd druther work -- wouldn't you? Course you would!"
Title:  
Title:     Tom contemplated the boy a bit, and said:
Title:  
Title:     "What do you call work?"
Title:  
Title:     "Why, ain't that work?"
Title:  
Title:     Tom resumed his whitewashing, and answered carelessly:
Title:  
Title:     "Well, maybe it is, and maybe it ain't. All I know, is, it suits Tom
Title:  Sawyer."
Title:  
Title:     "Oh come, now, you don't mean to let on that you like it?"
Title:  
Title:     The brush continued to move.
Title:  
Title:     "Like it? Well, I don't see why I oughtn't to like it. Does a boy get a
Title:  chance to whitewash a fence every day?"
Title:  
Title:     That put the thing in a new light. Ben stopped nibbling his apple. Tom
Title:  swept his brush daintily back and forth -- stepped back to note the effect
Title:  -- added a touch here and there -- criticised the effect again -- Ben
Title:  watching every move and getting more and more interested, more and more
Title:  absorbed. Presently he said:
Title:  
Title:     "Say, Tom, let me whitewash a little."
Title:  
Title:     Tom considered, was about to consent; but he altered his mind:
Title:  
Title:     "No -- no -- I reckon it wouldn't hardly do, Ben. You see, Aunt Polly's
Title:  awful particular about this fence -- right here on the street, you know --
Title:  but if it was the back fence I wouldn't mind and she wouldn't. Yes, she's
Title:  awful particular about this fence; it's got to be done very careful; I
Title:  reckon there ain't one boy in a thousand, maybe two thousand, that can do it
Title:  the way it's got to be done."
Title:  
Title:     "No -- is that so? Oh come, now -- lemme
Title:  just try. Only just a little -- I'd let you, if you was me, Tom."
Title:  
Title:     "Ben, I'd like to, honest injun; but Aunt Polly -- well, Jim wanted to do
Title:  it, but she wouldn't let him; Sid wanted to do it, and she wouldn't let Sid.
Title:  Now don't you see how I'm fixed? If you was to tackle this fence and
Title:  anything was to happen to it -- "
Title:  
Title:     "Oh, shucks, I'll be just as careful. Now lemme try. Say -- I'll give you
Title:  the core of my apple."
Title:  
Title:     "Well, here -- No, Ben, now don't. I'm afeard -- "
Title:  
Title:     "I'll give you all of it!"
Title:  
Title:     Tom gave up the brush with reluctance in his face, but alacrity in his
Title:  heart. And while the late steamer Big Missouri worked and sweated in the
Title:  sun, the retired artist sat on a barrel in the shade close by, dangled his
Title:  legs, munched his apple, and planned the slaughter of more innocents. There
Title:  was no lack of material; boys happened along every little while; they came
Title:  to jeer, but remained to whitewash. By the time Ben was fagged out, Tom had
Title:  traded the next chance to Billy Fisher for a kite, in good repair; and when
Title:  he played out, Johnny Miller bought in for a dead rat and a string to swing
Title:  it with -- and so on, and so on, hour after hour. And when the middle of the
Title:  afternoon came, from being a poor poverty-stricken boy in the morning, Tom
Title:  was literally rolling in wealth. He had besides the things before mentioned,
Title:  twelve marbles,
Title:  part of a jews-harp, a piece of blue bottle-glass to look through, a spool
Title:  cannon, a key that wouldn't unlock anything, a fragment of chalk, a glass
Title:  stopper of a decanter, a tin soldier, a couple of tadpoles, six
Title:  fire-crackers, a kitten with only one eye, a brass door-knob, a dog-collar
Title:  -- but no dog -- the handle of a knife, four pieces of orange-peel, and a
Title:  dilapidated old window sash.
Title:  
Title:     He had had a nice, good, idle time all the while -- plenty of company --
Title:  and the fence had three coats of whitewash on it! If he hadn't run out of
Title:  whitewash he would have bankrupted every boy in the village.
Title:  
Title:     Tom said to himself that it was not such a hollow world, after all. He
Title:  had discovered a great law of human action, without knowing it -- namely,
Title:  that in order to make a man or a boy covet a thing, it is only necessary to
Title:  make the thing difficult to attain. If he had been a great and wise
Title:  philosopher, like the writer of this book, he would now have comprehended
Title:  that Work consists of whatever a body is obliged to do, and that Play
Title:  consists of whatever a body is not obliged to do. And this would help him to
Title:  understand why constructing artificial flowers or performing on a tread-mill
Title:  is work, while rolling ten-pins or climbing Mont Blanc is only amusement.
Title:  There are wealthy gentlemen in England who drive four-horse
Title:  passenger-coaches twenty or thirty miles on a daily line, in the summer,
Title:  because the privilege costs them considerable money; but if they were
Title:  offered wages for the service, that would turn it into work and then they
Title:  would resign.
Title:  
Title:     The boy mused awhile over the substantial change which had taken place in
Title:  his worldly circumstances, and then wended toward headquarters to report.
Title:  
Title:    ------------------------------------------------------------------------
Title:  
Title:                                   Chapter III
Title:  
Title:     TOM presented himself before Aunt Polly, who was sitting by an open
Title:  window in a pleasant rearward apartment, which was bedroom, breakfast-room,
Title:  dining-room, and library, combined. The balmy summer air, the restful quiet,
Title:  the odor of the flowers, and the drowsing murmur of the bees had had their
Title:  effect, and she was nodding over her knitting -- for she had no company but
Title:  the cat, and it was asleep in her lap. Her spectacles were propped up on her
Title:  gray head for safety. She had thought that of course Tom had deserted long
Title:  ago, and she wondered at seeing him place himself in her power again in this
Title:  intrepid way. He said: "Mayn't I go and play now, aunt?"
Title:  
Title:     "What, a'ready? How much have you done?"
Title:  
Title:     "It's all done, aunt."
Title:  
Title:     "Tom, don't lie to me -- I can't bear it."
Title:  
Title:     "I ain't, aunt; it is all done."
Title:  
Title:     Aunt Polly placed small trust in such evidence. She went out to see for
Title:  herself; and she would have been content to find twenty per cent. of Tom's
Title:  statement true. When she found the entire fence whitewashed, and not only
Title:  white-washed but elaborately coated and recoated, and even a streak added
Title:  to the ground, her astonishment was almost unspeakable. She said:
Title:  
Title:     "Well, I never! There's no getting round it, you can work when you're a
Title:  mind to, Tom." And then she diluted the compliment by adding, "But it's
Title:  powerful seldom you're a mind to, I'm bound to say. Well, go 'long and play;
Title:  but mind you get back some time in a week, or I'll tan you."
Title:  
Title:     She was so overcome by the splendor of his achievement that she took him
Title:  into the closet and selected a choice apple and delivered it to him, along
Title:  with an improving lecture upon the added value and flavor a treat took to
Title:  itself when it came without sin through virtuous effort. And while she
Title:  closed with a happy Scriptural flourish, he "hooked" a doughnut.
Title:  
Title:     Then he skipped out, and saw Sid just starting up the outside stairway
Title:  that led to the back rooms on the second floor. Clods were handy and the air
Title:  was full of them in a twinkling. They raged around Sid like a hail-storm;
Title:  and before Aunt Polly could collect her surprised faculties and sally to the
Title:  rescue, six or seven clods had taken personal effect, and Tom was over the
Title:  fence and gone. There was a gate, but as a general thing he was too crowded
Title:  for time to make use of it. His soul was at peace, now that he had settled
Title:  with Sid for calling attention to his black thread and getting him into
Title:  trouble.
Title:  
Title:     Tom skirted the block, and came round into a muddy alley that led by the
Title:  back of his aunt's cow-stable. He presently got safely beyond the reach of
Title:  capture and punishment, and hastened toward the public square of the
Title:  village, where two "military" companies of boys had met for conflict,
Title:  according to previous appointment. Tom was General of one of these armies,
Title:  Joe Harper (a bosom friend) General of the other. These two great commanders
Title:  did not condescend to fight in person -- that being better suited to the
Title:  still smaller fry -- but sat together on an eminence and conducted the field
Title:  operations by orders delivered through aides-de-camp. Tom's army won a great
Title:  victory, after a long and hard-fought battle. Then the dead were counted,
Title:  prisoners exchanged, the terms of the next disagreement agreed upon, and the
Title:  day for the necessary battle appointed; after which the armies fell into
Title:  line and marched away, and Tom turned homeward alone.
Title:  
Title:     As he was passing by the house where Jeff Thatcher lived, he saw a new
Title:  girl in the garden -- a lovely little blue-eyed creature with yellow hair
Title:  plaited into two long-tails, white summer frock and embroidered pantalettes.
Title:  The fresh-crowned hero fell without firing a shot. A certain Amy Lawrence
Title:  vanished out of his heart and left not even a memory of herself behind. He
Title:  had thought he loved her to distraction; he had regarded his passion as
Title:  adoration; and behold it was only a poor little evanescent partiality. He
Title:  had been months winning her; she
Title:  had confessed hardly a week ago; he had been the happiest and the proudest
Title:  boy in the world only seven short days, and here in one instant of time she
Title:  had gone out of his heart like a casual stranger whose visit is done.
Title:  
Title:     He worshipped this new angel with furtive eye, till he saw that she had
Title:  discovered him; then he pretended he did not know she was present, and began
Title:  to "show off" in all sorts of absurd boyish ways, in order to win her
Title:  admiration. He kept up this grotesque foolishness for some time; but
Title:  by-and-by, while he was in the midst of some dangerous gymnastic
Title:  performances, he glanced aside and saw that the little girl was wending her
Title:  way toward the house. Tom came up to the fence and leaned on it, grieving,
Title:  and hoping she would tarry yet awhile longer. She halted a moment on the
Title:  steps and then moved toward the door. Tom heaved a great sigh as she put her
Title:  foot on the threshold. But his face lit up, right away, for she tossed a
Title:  pansy over the fence a moment before she disappeared.
Title:  
Title:     The boy ran around and stopped within a foot or two of the flower, and
Title:  then shaded his eyes with his hand and began to look down street as if he
Title:  had discovered something of interest going on in that direction. Presently
Title:  he picked up a straw and began trying to balance it on his nose, with his
Title:  head tilted far back; and as he moved from side to side, in his efforts, he
Title:  edged nearer and nearer toward the pansy; finally his bare foot rested upon
Title:  it, his pliant
Title:  toes closed upon it, and he hopped away with the treasure and disappeared
Title:  round the corner. But only for a minute -- only while he could button the
Title:  flower inside his jacket, next his heart -- or next his stomach, possibly,
Title:  for he was not much posted in anatomy, and not hypercritical, anyway.
Title:  
Title:     He returned, now, and hung about the fence till nightfall, "showing off,"
Title:  as before; but the girl never exhibited herself again, though Tom comforted
Title:  himself a little with the hope that she had been near some window, meantime,
Title:  and been aware of his attentions. Finally he strode home reluctantly, with
Title:  his poor head full of visions.
Title:  
Title:     All through supper his spirits were so high that his aunt wondered "what
Title:  had got into the child." He took a good scolding about clodding Sid, and did
Title:  not seem to mind it in the least. He tried to steal sugar under his aunt's
Title:  very nose, and got his knuckles rapped for it. He said:
Title:  
Title:     "Aunt, you don't whack Sid when he takes it."
Title:  
Title:     "Well, Sid don't torment a body the way you do. You'd be always into that
Title:  sugar if I warn't watching you."
Title:  
Title:     Presently she stepped into the kitchen, and Sid, happy in his immunity,
Title:  reached for the sugar-bowl -- a sort of glorying over Tom which was wellnigh
Title:  unbearable. But Sid's fingers slipped and the bowl dropped and broke. Tom
Title:  was in ecstasies. In such ecstasies that he even controlled his tongue and
Title:  was silent. He said to himself that he would
Title:  not speak a word, even when his aunt came in, but would sit perfectly still
Title:  till she asked who did the mischief; and then he would tell, and there would
Title:  be nothing so good in the world as to see that pet model "catch it." He was
Title:  so brimful of exultation that he could hardly hold himself when the old lady
Title:  came back and stood above the wreck discharging lightnings of wrath from
Title:  over her spectacles. He said to himself, "Now it's coming!" And the next
Title:  instant he was sprawling on the floor! The potent palm was uplifted to
Title:  strike again when Tom cried out:
Title:  
Title:     "Hold on, now, what 'er you belting me for? -- Sid broke it!"
Title:  
Title:     Aunt Polly paused, perplexed, and Tom looked for healing pity. But when
Title:  she got her tongue again, she only said:
Title:  
Title:     "Umf! Well, you didn't get a lick amiss, I reckon. You been into some
Title:  other audacious mischief when I wasn't around, like enough."
Title:  
Title:     Then her conscience reproached her, and she yearned to say something kind
Title:  and loving; but she judged that this would be construed into a confession
Title:  that she had been in the wrong, and discipline forbade that. So she kept
Title:  silence, and went about her affairs with a troubled heart. Tom sulked in a
Title:  corner and exalted his woes. He knew that in her heart his aunt was on her
Title:  knees to him, and he was morosely gratified by the consciousness of it. He
Title:  would hang out no signals, he would take notice
Title:  of none. He knew that a yearning glance fell upon him, now and then, through
Title:  a film of tears, but he refused recognition of it. He pictured himself lying
Title:  sick unto death and his aunt bending over him beseeching one little
Title:  forgiving word, but he would turn his face to the wall, and die with that
Title:  word unsaid. Ah, how would she feel then? And he pictured himself brought
Title:  home from the river, dead, with his curls all wet, and his sore heart at
Title:  rest. How she would throw herself upon him, and how her tears would fall
Title:  like rain, and her lips pray God to give her back her boy and she would
Title:  never, never abuse him any more! But he would lie there cold and white and
Title:  make no sign -- a poor little sufferer, whose griefs were at an end. He so
Title:  worked upon his feelings with the pathos of these dreams, that he had to
Title:  keep swallowing, he was so like to choke; and his eyes swam in a blur of
Title:  water, which overflowed when he winked, and ran down and trickled from the
Title:  end of his nose. And such a luxury to him was this petting of his sorrows,
Title:  that he could not bear to have any worldly cheeriness or any grating delight
Title:  intrude upon it; it was too sacred for such contact; and so, presently, when
Title:  his cousin Mary danced in, all alive with the joy of seeing home again after
Title:  an age-long visit of one week to the country, he got up and moved in clouds
Title:  and darkness out at one door as she brought song and sunshine in at the
Title:  other.
Title:  
Title:     He wandered far from the accustomed haunts of
Title:  boys, and sought desolate places that were in harmony with his spirit. A log
Title:  raft in the river invited him, and he seated himself on its outer edge and
Title:  contemplated the dreary vastness of the stream, wishing, the while, that he
Title:  could only be drowned, all at once and unconsciously, without undergoing the
Title:  uncomfortable routine devised by nature. Then he thought of his flower. He
Title:  got it out, rumpled and wilted, and it mightily increased his dismal
Title:  felicity. He wondered if she would pity him if she knew? Would she cry, and
Title:  wish that she had a right to put her arms around his neck and comfort him?
Title:  Or would she turn coldly away like all the hollow world? This picture
Title:  brought such an agony of pleasurable suffering that he worked it over and
Title:  over again in his mind and set it up in new and varied lights, till he wore
Title:  it threadbare. At last he rose up sighing and departed in the darkness.
Title:  
Title:     About half-past nine or ten o'clock he came along the deserted street to
Title:  where the Adored Unknown lived; he paused a moment; no sound fell upon his
Title:  listening ear; a candle was casting a dull glow upon the curtain of a
Title:  second-story window. Was the sacred presence there? He climbed the fence,
Title:  threaded his stealthy way through the plants, till he stood under that
Title:  window; he looked up at it long, and with emotion; then he laid him down on
Title:  the ground under it, disposing himself upon his back, with his hands clasped
Title:  upon his breast and holding his poor wilted flower. And thus he would
Title:  die -- out in the cold world, with no shelter over his homeless head, no
Title:  friendly hand to wipe the death-damps from his brow, no loving face to bend
Title:  pityingly over him when the great agony came. And thus she would see him
Title:  when she looked out upon the glad morning, and oh! would she drop one little
Title:  tear upon his poor, lifeless form, would she heave one little sigh to see a
Title:  bright young life so rudely blighted, so untimely cut down?
Title:  
Title:     The window went up, a maid-servant's discordant voice profaned the holy
Title:  calm, and a deluge of water drenched the prone martyr's remains!
Title:  
Title:     The strangling hero sprang up with a relieving snort. There was a whiz as
Title:  of a missile in the air, mingled with the murmur of a curse, a sound as of
Title:  shivering glass followed, and a small, vague form went over the fence and
Title:  shot away in the gloom.
Title:  
Title:     Not long after, as Tom, all undressed for bed, was surveying his drenched
Title:  garments by the light of a tallow dip, Sid woke up; but if he had any dim
Title:  idea of making any "references to allusions," he thought better of it and
Title:  held his peace, for there was danger in Tom's eye.
Title:  
Title:     Tom turned in without the added vexation of prayers, and Sid made mental
Title:  note of the omission.
Title:  
Title:    ------------------------------------------------------------------------
Title:  
Title:                                   Chapter IV
Title:  
Title:     THE sun rose upon a tranquil world, and beamed down upon the peaceful
Title:  village like a benediction. Breakfast over, Aunt Polly had family worship:
Title:  it began with a prayer built from the ground up of solid courses of
Title:  Scriptural quotations, welded together with a thin mortar of originality;
Title:  and from the summit of this she delivered a grim chapter of the Mosaic Law,
Title:  as from Sinai.
Title:  
Title:     Then Tom girded up his loins, so to speak, and went to work to "get his
Title:  verses." Sid had learned his lesson days before. Tom bent all his energies
Title:  to the memorizing of five verses, and he chose part of the Sermon on the
Title:  Mount, because he could find no verses that were shorter. At the end of half
Title:  an hour Tom had a vague general idea of his lesson, but no more, for his
Title:  mind was traversing the whole field of human thought, and his hands were
Title:  busy with distracting recreations. Mary took his book to hear him recite,
Title:  and he tried to find his way through the fog:
Title:  
Title:     "Blessed are the -- a -- a -- "
Title:  
Title:     "Poor" --
Title:  
Title:     "Yes -- poor; blessed are the poor -- a -- a -- "
Title:  
Title:     "In spirit -- "
Title:  
Title:     "In spirit; blessed are the poor in spirit, for they -- they -- "
Title:  
Title:     "Theirs -- "
Title:  
Title:     "For theirs . Blessed are the poor in spirit, for theirs is the kingdom
Title:  of heaven. Blessed are they that mourn, for they -- they -- "
Title:  
Title:     "Sh -- "
Title:  
Title:     "For they -- a -- "
Title:  
Title:     "S, H, A -- "
Title:  
Title:     "For they S, H -- Oh, I don't know what it is!"
Title:  
Title:     "Shall!"
Title:  
Title:     "Oh, shall! for they shall -- for they shall -- a -- a -- shall mourn --
Title:  a -- a -- blessed are they that shall -- they that -- a -- they that shall
Title:  mourn, for they shall -- a -- shall what? Why don't you tell me, Mary? --
Title:  what do you want to be so mean for?"
Title:  
Title:     "Oh, Tom, you poor thick-headed thing, I'm not teasing you. I wouldn't do
Title:  that. You must go and learn it again. Don't you be discouraged, Tom, you'll
Title:  manage it -- and if you do, I'll give you something ever so nice. There,
Title:  now, that's a good boy."
Title:  
Title:     "All right! What is it, Mary, tell me what it is."
Title:  
Title:     "Never you mind, Tom. You know if I say it's nice, it is nice."
Title:  
Title:     "You bet you that's so, Mary. All right, I'll tackle it again."
Title:  
Title:     And he did "tackle it again" -- and under the
Title:  double pressure of curiosity and prospective gain he did it with such spirit
Title:  that he accomplished a shining success. Mary gave him a brand-new "Barlow"
Title:  knife worth twelve and a half cents; and the convulsion of delight that
Title:  swept his system shook him to his foundations. True, the knife would not cut
Title:  anything, but it was a "sure-enough" Barlow, and there was inconceivable
Title:  grandeur in that -- though where the Western boys ever got the idea that
Title:  such a weapon could possibly be counterfeited to its injury is an imposing
Title:  mystery and will always remain so, perhaps. Tom contrived to scarify the
Title:  cupboard with it, and was arranging to begin on the bureau, when he was
Title:  called off to dress for Sunday-school.
Title:  
Title:     Mary gave him a tin basin of water and a piece of soap, and he went
Title:  outside the door and set the basin on a little bench there; then he dipped
Title:  the soap in the water and laid it down; turned up his sleeves; poured out
Title:  the water on the ground, gently, and then entered the kitchen and began to
Title:  wipe his face diligently on the towel behind the door. But Mary removed the
Title:  towel and said:
Title:  
Title:     "Now ain't you ashamed, Tom. You mustn't be so bad. Water won't hurt
Title:  you."
Title:  
Title:     Tom was a trifle disconcerted. The basin was refilled, and this time he
Title:  stood over it a little while, gathering resolution; took in a big breath and
Title:  began. When he entered the kitchen presently, with both eyes shut and
Title:  groping for the towel with
Title:  his hands, an honorable testimony of suds and water was dripping from his
Title:  face. But when he emerged from the towel, he was not yet satisfactory, for
Title:  the clean territory stopped short at his chin and his jaws, like a mask;
Title:  below and beyond this line there was a dark expanse of unirrigated soil that
Title:  spread downward in front and backward around his neck. Mary took him in
Title:  hand, and when she was done with him he was a man and a brother, without
Title:  distinction of color, and his saturated hair was neatly brushed, and its
Title:  short curls wrought into a dainty and symmetrical general effect. [He
Title:  privately smoothed out the curls, with labor and difficulty, and plastered
Title:  his hair close down to his head; for he held curls to be effeminate, and his
Title:  own filled his life with bitterness.] Then Mary got out a suit of his
Title:  clothing that had been used only on Sundays during two years -- they were
Title:  simply called his "other clothes" -- and so by that we know the size of his
Title:  wardrobe. The girl "put him to rights" after he had dressed himself; she
Title:  buttoned his neat roundabout up to his chin, turned his vast shirt collar
Title:  down over his shoulders, brushed him off and crowned him with his speckled
Title:  straw hat. He now looked exceedingly improved and uncomfortable. He was
Title:  fully as uncomfortable as he looked; for there was a restraint about whole
Title:  clothes and cleanliness that galled him. He hoped that Mary would forget his
Title:  shoes, but the hope was blighted; she coated them thoroughly with tallow, as
Title:  was the
Title:  custom, and brought them out. He lost his temper and said he was always
Title:  being made to do everything he didn't want to do. But Mary said,
Title:  persuasively:
Title:  
Title:     "Please, Tom -- that's a good boy."
Title:  
Title:     So he got into the shoes snarling. Mary was soon ready, and the three
Title:  children set out for Sunday-school -- a place that Tom hated with his whole
Title:  heart; but Sid and Mary were fond of it.
Title:  
Title:     Sabbath-school hours were from nine to half-past ten; and then church
Title:  service. Two of the children always remained for the sermon voluntarily, and
Title:  the other always remained too -- for stronger reasons. The church's
Title:  high-backed, uncushioned pews would seat about three hundred persons; the
Title:  edifice was but a small, plain affair, with a sort of pine board tree-box on
Title:  top of it for a steeple. At the door Tom dropped back a step and accosted a
Title:  Sunday-dressed comrade:
Title:  
Title:     "Say, Billy, got a yaller ticket?"
Title:  
Title:     "Yes."
Title:  
Title:     "What'll you take for her?"
Title:  
Title:     "What'll you give?"
Title:  
Title:     "Piece of lickrish and a fish-hook."
Title:  
Title:     "Less see 'em."
Title:  
Title:     Tom exhibited. They were satisfactory, and the property changed hands.
Title:  Then Tom traded a couple of white alleys for three red tickets, and some
Title:  small trifle or other for a couple of blue ones. He waylaid other boys as
Title:  they came, and went on buying tickets of various colors ten or fifteen
Title:  minutes longer. He entered the church, now, with a swarm of clean and noisy
Title:  boys and
Title:  girls, proceeded to his seat and started a quarrel with the first boy that
Title:  came handy. The teacher, a grave, elderly man, interfered; then turned his
Title:  back a moment and Tom pulled a boy's hair in the next bench, and was
Title:  absorbed in his book when the boy turned around; stuck a pin in another boy,
Title:  presently, in order to hear him say "Ouch!" and got a new reprimand from his
Title:  teacher. Tom's whole class were of a pattern -- restless, noisy, and
Title:  troublesome. When they came to recite their lessons, not one of them knew
Title:  his verses perfectly, but had to be prompted all along. However, they
Title:  worried through, and each got his reward -- in small blue tickets, each with
Title:  a passage of Scripture on it; each blue ticket was pay for two verses of the
Title:  recitation. Ten blue tickets equalled a red one, and could be exchanged for
Title:  it; ten red tickets equalled a yellow one; for ten yellow tickets the
Title:  superintendent gave a very plainly bound Bible (worth forty cents in those
Title:  easy times) to the pupil. How many of my readers would have the industry and
Title:  application to memorize two thousand verses, even for a Dore Bible? And yet
Title:  Mary had acquired two Bibles in this way -- it was the patient work of two
Title:  years -- and a boy of German parentage had won four or five. He once recited
Title:  three thousand verses without stopping; but the strain upon his mental
Title:  faculties was too great, and he was little better than an idiot from that
Title:  day forth -- a grievous misfortune for the school, for on great occasions,
Title:  before company, the superintendent (as Tom expressed it) had always made
Title:  this boy come out and "spread himself." Only the older pupils managed to
Title:  keep their tickets and stick to their tedious work long enough to get a
Title:  Bible, and so the delivery of one of these prizes was a rare and noteworthy
Title:  circumstance; the successful pupil was so great and conspicuous for that day
Title:  that on the spot every scholar's heart was fired with a fresh ambition that
Title:  often lasted a couple of weeks. It is possible that Tom's mental stomach had
Title:  never really hungered for one of those prizes, but unquestionably his entire
Title:  being had for many a day longed for the glory and the eclat that came with
Title:  it.
Title:  
Title:     In due course the superintendent stood up in front of the pulpit, with a
Title:  closed hymn-book in his hand and his forefinger inserted between its leaves,
Title:  and commanded attention. When a Sunday-school superintendent makes his
Title:  customary little speech, a hymn-book in the hand is as necessary as is the
Title:  inevitable sheet of music in the hand of a singer who stands forward on the
Title:  platform and sings a solo at a concert -- though why, is a mystery: for
Title:  neither the hymn-book nor the sheet of music is ever referred to by the
Title:  sufferer. This superintendent was a slim creature of thirty-five, with a
Title:  sandy goatee and short sandy hair; he wore a stiff standing-collar whose
Title:  upper edge almost reached his ears and whose sharp points curved forward
Title:  abreast the
Title:  corners of his mouth -- a fence that compelled a straight lookout ahead, and
Title:  a turning of the whole body when a side view was required; his chin was
Title:  propped on a spreading cravat which was as broad and as long as a bank-note,
Title:  and had fringed ends; his boot toes were turned sharply up, in the fashion
Title:  of the day, like sleigh-runners -- an effect patiently and laboriously
Title:  produced by the young men by sitting with their toes pressed against a wall
Title:  for hours together. Mr. Walters was very earnest of mien, and very sincere
Title:  and honest at heart; and he held sacred things and places in such reverence,
Title:  and so separated them from worldly matters, that unconsciously to himself
Title:  his Sunday-school voice had acquired a peculiar intonation which was wholly
Title:  absent on week-days. He began after this fashion:
Title:  
Title:     "Now, children, I want you all to sit up just as straight and pretty as
Title:  you can and give me all your attention for a minute or two. There -- that is
Title:  it. That is the way good little boys and girls should do. I see one little
Title:  girl who is looking out of the window -- I am afraid she thinks I am out
Title:  there somewhere -- perhaps up in one of the trees making a speech to the
Title:  little birds. [Applausive titter.] I want to tell you how good it makes me
Title:  feel to see so many bright, clean little faces assembled in a place like
Title:  this, learning to do right and be good." And so forth and so on. It is not
Title:  necessary to set down the rest of the oration. It was of a pattern which
Title:  does not vary, and so it is familiar to us all.
Title:  
Title:     The latter third of the speech was marred by the resumption of fights and
Title:  other recreations among certain of the bad boys, and by fidgetings and
Title:  whisperings that extended far and wide, washing even to the bases of
Title:  isolated and incorruptible rocks like Sid and Mary. But now every sound
Title:  ceased suddenly, with the subsidence of Mr. Walters' voice, and the
Title:  conclusion of the speech was received with a burst of silent gratitude.
Title:  
Title:     A good part of the whispering had been occasioned by an event which was
Title:  more or less rare -- the entrance of visitors: lawyer Thatcher, accompanied
Title:  by a very feeble and aged man; a fine, portly, middle-aged gentleman with
Title:  iron-gray hair; and a dignified lady who was doubtless the latter's wife.
Title:  The lady was leading a child. Tom had been restless and full of chafings and
Title:  repinings; conscience-smitten, too -- he could not meet Amy Lawrence's eye,
Title:  he could not brook her loving gaze. But when he saw this small new-comer his
Title:  soul was all ablaze with bliss in a moment. The next moment he was "showing
Title:  off" with all his might -- cuffing boys, pulling hair, making faces -- in a
Title:  word, using every art that seemed likely to fascinate a girl and win her
Title:  applause. His exaltation had but one alloy -- the memory of his humiliation
Title:  in this angel's garden -- and that record in sand was fast washing out,
Title:  under the waves of happiness that were sweeping over it now.
Title:  
Title:     The visitors were given the highest seat of honor,
Title:  and as soon as Mr. Walters' speech was finished, he introduced them to the
Title:  school. The middle-aged man turned out to be a prodigious personage -- no
Title:  less a one than the county judge -- altogether the most august creation
Title:  these children had ever looked upon -- and they wondered what kind of
Title:  material he was made of -- and they half wanted to hear him roar, and were
Title:  half afraid he might, too. He was from Constantinople, twelve miles away --
Title:  so he had travelled, and seen the world -- these very eyes had looked upon
Title:  the county court-house -- which was said to have a tin roof. The awe which
Title:  these reflections inspired was attested by the impressive silence and the
Title:  ranks of staring eyes. This was the great Judge Thatcher, brother of their
Title:  own lawyer. Jeff Thatcher immediately went forward, to be familiar with the
Title:  great man and be envied by the school. It would have been music to his soul
Title:  to hear the whisperings:
Title:  
Title:     "Look at him, Jim! He's a going up there. Say -- look! he's a going to
Title:  shake hands with him -- he is shaking hands with him! By jings, don't you
Title:  wish you was Jeff?"
Title:  
Title:     Mr. Walters fell to "showing off," with all sorts of official bustlings
Title:  and activities, giving orders, delivering judgments, discharging directions
Title:  here, there, everywhere that he could find a target. The librarian "showed
Title:  off" -- running hither and thither with his arms full of books and making a
Title:  deal of the splutter and fuss that insect authority delights in.
Title:  The young lady teachers "showed off" -- bending sweetly over pupils that
Title:  were lately being boxed, lifting pretty warning fingers at bad little boys
Title:  and patting good ones lovingly. The young gentlemen teachers "showed off"
Title:  with small scoldings and other little displays of authority and fine
Title:  attention to discipline -- and most of the teachers, of both sexes, found
Title:  business up at the library, by the pulpit; and it was business that
Title:  frequently had to be done over again two or three times (with much seeming
Title:  vexation). The little girls "showed off" in various ways, and the little
Title:  boys "showed off" with such diligence that the air was thick with paper wads
Title:  and the murmur of scufflings. And above it all the great man sat and beamed
Title:  a majestic judicial smile upon all the house, and warmed himself in the sun
Title:  of his own grandeur -- for he was "showing off," too.
Title:  
Title:     There was only one thing wanting to make Mr. Walters' ecstasy complete,
Title:  and that was a chance to deliver a Bible-prize and exhibit a prodigy.
Title:  Several pupils had a few yellow tickets, but none had enough -- he had been
Title:  around among the star pupils inquiring. He would have given worlds, now, to
Title:  have that German lad back again with a sound mind.
Title:  
Title:     And now at this moment, when hope was dead, Tom Sawyer came forward with
Title:  nine yellow tickets, nine red tickets, and ten blue ones, and demanded a
Title:  Bible. This was a thunderbolt out of a clear sky. Walters was not expecting
Title:  an application from this source for the next ten years. But there was no
Title:  getting around it -- here were the certified checks, and they were good for
Title:  their face. Tom was therefore elevated to a place with the Judge and the
Title:  other elect, and the great news was announced from head-quarters. It was the
Title:  most stunning surprise of the decade, and so profound was the sensation that
Title:  it lifted the new hero up to the judicial one's altitude, and the school had
Title:  two marvels to gaze upon in place of one. The boys were all eaten up with
Title:  envy -- but those that suffered the bitterest pangs were those who perceived
Title:  too late that they themselves had contributed to this hated splendor by
Title:  trading tickets to Tom for the wealth he had amassed in selling whitewashing
Title:  privileges. These despised themselves, as being the dupes of a wily fraud, a
Title:  guileful snake in the grass.
Title:  
Title:     The prize was delivered to Tom with as much effusion as the
Title:  superintendent could pump up under the circumstances; but it lacked somewhat
Title:  of the true gush, for the poor fellow's instinct taught him that there was a
Title:  mystery here that could not well bear the light, perhaps; it was simply
Title:  preposterous that this boy had warehoused two thousand sheaves of Scriptural
Title:  wisdom on his premises -- a dozen would strain his capacity, without a
Title:  doubt.
Title:  
Title:     Amy Lawrence was proud and glad, and she tried to make Tom see it in her
Title:  face -- but he wouldn't look. She wondered; then she was just a grain
Title:  troubled; next a dim suspicion came and went -- came again; she watched; a
Title:  furtive glance told her
Title:  worlds -- and then her heart broke, and she was jealous, and angry, and the
Title:  tears came and she hated everybody. Tom most of all (she thought).
Title:  
Title:     Tom was introduced to the Judge; but his tongue was tied, his breath
Title:  would hardly come, his heart quaked -- partly because of the awful greatness
Title:  of the man, but mainly because he was her parent. He would have liked to
Title:  fall down and worship him, if it were in the dark. The Judge put his hand on
Title:  Tom's head and called him a fine little man, and asked him what his name
Title:  was. The boy stammered, gasped, and got it out:
Title:  
Title:     "Tom."
Title:  
Title:     "Oh, no, not Tom -- it is -- "
Title:  
Title:     "Thomas."
Title:  
Title:     "Ah, that's it. I thought there was more to it, maybe. That's very well.
Title:  But you've another one I daresay, and you'll tell it to me, won't you?"
Title:  
Title:     "Tell the gentleman your other name, Thomas," said Walters, "and say sir
Title:  . You mustn't forget your manners."
Title:  
Title:     "Thomas Sawyer -- sir."
Title:  
Title:     "That's it! That's a good boy. Fine boy. Fine, manly little fellow. Two
Title:  thousand verses is a great many -- very, very great many. And you never can
Title:  be sorry for the trouble you took to learn them; for knowledge is worth more
Title:  than anything there is in the world; it's what makes great men and good men;
Title:  you'll
Title:  be a great man and a good man yourself, some day, Thomas, and then you'll
Title:  look back and say, It's all owing to the precious Sunday-school privileges
Title:  of my boyhood -- it's all owing to my dear teachers that taught me to learn
Title:  -- it's all owing to the good superintendent, who encouraged me, and watched
Title:  over me, and gave me a beautiful Bible -- a splendid elegant Bible -- to
Title:  keep and have it all for my own, always -- it's all owing to right bringing
Title:  up! That is what you will say, Thomas -- and you wouldn't take any money for
Title:  those two thousand verses -- no indeed you wouldn't. And now you wouldn't
Title:  mind telling me and this lady some of the things you've learned -- no, I
Title:  know you wouldn't -- for we are proud of little boys that learn. Now, no
Title:  doubt you know the names of all the twelve disciples. Won't you tell us the
Title:  names of the first two that were appointed?"
Title:  
Title:     Tom was tugging at a button-hole and looking sheepish. He blushed, now,
Title:  and his eyes fell. Mr. Walters' heart sank within him. He said to himself,
Title:  it is not possible that the boy can answer the simplest question -- why did
Title:  the Judge ask him? Yet he felt obliged to speak up and say:
Title:  
Title:     "Answer the gentleman, Thomas -- don't be afraid."
Title:  
Title:     Tom still hung fire.
Title:  
Title:     "Now I know you'll tell me," said the lady. "The names of the first two
Title:  disciples were -- "
Title:  
Title:     "DAVID AND GOLIAH!"
Title:  
Title:     Let us draw the curtain of charity over the rest of the scene.
Title:  
Title:    ------------------------------------------------------------------------
Title:  
Title:                                    Chapter V
Title:  
Title:     ABOUT half-past ten the cracked bell of the small church began to ring,
Title:  and presently the people began to gather for the morning sermon. The
Title:  Sunday-school children distributed themselves about the house and occupied
Title:  pews with their parents, so as to be under supervision. Aunt Polly came, and
Title:  Tom and Sid and Mary sat with her -- Tom being placed next the aisle, in
Title:  order that he might be as far away from the open window and the seductive
Title:  outside summer scenes as possible. The crowd filed up the aisles: the aged
Title:  and needy postmaster, who had seen better days; the mayor and his wife --
Title:  for they had a mayor there, among other unnecessaries; the justice of the
Title:  peace; the widow Douglass, fair, smart, and forty, a generous, good-hearted
Title:  soul and well-to-do, her hill mansion the only palace in the town, and the
Title:  most hospitable and much the most lavish in the matter of festivities that
Title:  St. Petersburg could boast; the bent and venerable Major and Mrs. Ward;
Title:  lawyer Riverson, the new notable from a distance; next the belle of the
Title:  village, followed by a troop of lawn-clad and ribbon-decked young
Title:  heart-breakers; then all the young clerks in town in a
Title:  body -- for they had stood in the vestibule sucking their cane-heads, a
Title:  circling wall of oiled and simpering admirers, till the last girl had run
Title:  their gantlet; and last of all came the Model Boy, Willie Mufferson, taking
Title:  as heedful care of his mother as if she were cut glass. He always brought
Title:  his mother to church, and was the pride of all the matrons. The boys all
Title:  hated him, he was so good. And besides, he had been "thrown up to them" so
Title:  much. His white handkerchief was hanging out of his pocket behind, as usual
Title:  on Sundays -- accidentally. Tom had no handkerchief, and he looked upon boys
Title:  who had as snobs.
Title:  
Title:     The congregation being fully assembled, now, the bell rang once more, to
Title:  warn laggards and stragglers, and then a solemn hush fell upon the church
Title:  which was only broken by the tittering and whispering of the choir in the
Title:  gallery. The choir always tittered and whispered all through service. There
Title:  was once a church choir that was not ill-bred, but I have forgotten where it
Title:  was, now. It was a great many years ago, and I can scarcely remember
Title:  anything about it, but I think it was in some foreign country.
Title:  
Title:     The minister gave out the hymn, and read it through with a relish, in a
Title:  peculiar style which was much admired in that part of the country. His voice
Title:  began on a medium key and climbed steadily up till it reached a certain
Title:  point, where it bore with strong emphasis upon the topmost word and then
Title:  plunged down as if from a spring-board:
Title:  
Title:  Shall I be car-ri-ed toe the skies, on flow'ry beds
Title:  of ease,
Title:  Whilst others fight to win the prize, and sail thro' blood
Title:  -y seas?
Title:  
Title:     He was regarded as a wonderful reader. At church "sociables" he was
Title:  always called upon to read poetry; and when he was through, the ladies would
Title:  lift up their hands and let them fall helplessly in their laps, and "wall"
Title:  their eyes, and shake their heads, as much as to say, "Words cannot express
Title:  it; it is too beautiful, too beautiful for this mortal earth."
Title:  
Title:     After the hymn had been sung, the Rev. Mr. Sprague turned himself into a
Title:  bulletin-board, and read off "notices" of meetings and societies and things
Title:  till it seemed that the list would stretch out to the crack of doom -- a
Title:  queer custom which is still kept up in America, even in cities, away here in
Title:  this age of abundant newspapers. Often, the less there is to justify a
Title:  traditional custom, the harder it is to get rid of it.
Title:  
Title:     And now the minister prayed. A good, generous prayer it was, and went
Title:  into details: it pleaded for the church, and the little children of the
Title:  church; for the other churches of the village; for the village itself; for
Title:  the county; for the State; for the State officers; for the United States;
Title:  for the churches of the United States; for Congress; for the President; for
Title:  the officers of the Government; for poor sailors, tossed by stormy seas; for
Title:  the oppressed millions
Title:  groaning under the heel of European monarchies and Oriental despotisms; for
Title:  such as have the light and the good tidings, and yet have not eyes to see
Title:  nor ears to hear withal; for the heathen in the far islands of the sea; and
Title:  closed with a supplication that the words he was about to speak might find
Title:  grace and favor, and be as seed sown in fertile ground, yielding in time a
Title:  grateful harvest of good. Amen.
Title:  
Title:     There was a rustling of dresses, and the standing congregation sat down.
Title:  The boy whose history this book relates did not enjoy the prayer, he only
Title:  endured it -- if he even did that much. He was restive all through it; he
Title:  kept tally of the details of the prayer, unconsciously -- for he was not
Title:  listening, but he knew the ground of old, and the clergyman's regular route
Title:  over it -- and when a little trifle of new matter was interlarded, his ear
Title:  detected it and his whole nature resented it; he considered additions
Title:  unfair, and scoundrelly. In the midst of the prayer a fly had lit on the
Title:  back of the pew in front of him and tortured his spirit by calmly rubbing
Title:  its hands together, embracing its head with its arms, and polishing it so
Title:  vigorously that it seemed to almost part company with the body, and the
Title:  slender thread of a neck was exposed to view; scraping its wings with its
Title:  hind legs and smoothing them to its body as if they had been coat-tails;
Title:  going through its whole toilet as tranquilly as if it knew it was perfectly
Title:  safe. As indeed it was; for as sorely as Tom's hands
Title:  itched to grab for it they did not dare -- he believed his soul would be
Title:  instantly destroyed if he did such a thing while the prayer was going on.
Title:  But with the closing sentence his hand began to curve and steal forward; and
Title:  the instant the "Amen" was out the fly was a prisoner of war. His aunt
Title:  detected the act and made him let it go.
Title:  
Title:     The minister gave out his text and droned along monotonously through an
Title:  argument that was so prosy that many a head by and by began to nod -- and
Title:  yet it was an argument that dealt in limitless fire and brimstone and
Title:  thinned the predestined elect down to a company so small as to be hardly
Title:  worth the saving. Tom counted the pages of the sermon; after church he
Title:  always knew how many pages there had been, but he seldom knew anything else
Title:  about the discourse. However, this time he was really interested for a
Title:  little while. The minister made a grand and moving picture of the assembling
Title:  together of the world's hosts at the millennium when the lion and the lamb
Title:  should lie down together and a little child should lead them. But the
Title:  pathos, the lesson, the moral of the great spectacle were lost upon the boy;
Title:  he only thought of the conspicuousness of the principal character before the
Title:  on-looking nations; his face lit with the thought, and he said to himself
Title:  that he wished he could be that child, if it was a tame lion.
Title:  
Title:     Now he lapsed into suffering again, as the dry argument was resumed.
Title:  Presently he bethought
Title:  him of a treasure he had and got it out. It was a large black beetle with
Title:  formidable jaws -- a "pinchbug," he called it. It was in a percussion-cap
Title:  box. The first thing the beetle did was to take him by the finger. A natural
Title:  fillip followed, the beetle went floundering into the aisle and lit on its
Title:  back, and the hurt finger went into the boy's mouth. The beetle lay there
Title:  working its helpless legs, unable to turn over. Tom eyed it, and longed for
Title:  it; but it was safe out of his reach. Other people uninterested in the
Title:  sermon found relief in the beetle, and they eyed it too. Presently a vagrant
Title:  poodle dog came idling along, sad at heart, lazy with the summer softness
Title:  and the quiet, weary of captivity, sighing for change. He spied the beetle;
Title:  the drooping tail lifted and wagged. He surveyed the prize; walked around
Title:  it; smelt at it from a safe distance; walked around it again; grew bolder,
Title:  and took a closer smell; then lifted his lip and made a gingerly snatch at
Title:  it, just missing it; made another, and another; began to enjoy the
Title:  diversion; subsided to his stomach with the beetle between his paws, and
Title:  continued his experiments; grew weary at last, and then indifferent and
Title:  absent-minded. His head nodded, and little by little his chin descended and
Title:  touched the enemy, who seized it. There was a sharp yelp, a flirt of the
Title:  poodle's head, and the beetle fell a couple of yards away, and lit on its
Title:  back once more. The neighboring spectators shook with a gentle inward joy,
Title:  several faces went behind
Title:  fans and handkerchiefs, and Tomwas entirely happy. The dog looked foolish,
Title:  and probably felt so; but there was resentment in his heart, too, and a
Title:  craving for revenge. So he went to the beetle and began a wary attack on it
Title:  again; jumping at it from every point of a circle, lighting with his
Title:  fore-paws within an inch of the creature, making even closer snatches at it
Title:  with his teeth, and jerking his head till his ears flapped again. But he
Title:  grew tired once more, after a while; tried to amuse himself with a fly but
Title:  found no relief; followed an ant around, with his nose close to the floor,
Title:  and quickly wearied of that; yawned, sighed, forgot the beetle entirely, and
Title:  sat down on it. Then there was a wild yelp of agony and the poodle went
Title:  sailing up the aisle; the yelps continued, and so did the dog; he crossed
Title:  the house in front of the altar; he flew down the other aisle; he crossed
Title:  before the doors; he clamored up the home-stretch; his anguish grew with his
Title:  progress, till presently he was but a woolly comet moving in its orbit with
Title:  the gleam and the speed of light. At last the frantic sufferer sheered from
Title:  its course, and sprang into its master's lap; he flung it out of the window,
Title:  and the voice of distress quickly thinned away and died in the distance.
Title:  
Title:     By this time the whole church was red-faced and suffocating with
Title:  suppressed laughter, and the sermon had come to a dead standstill. The
Title:  discourse was resumed presently, but it went lame and halting, all
Title:  possibility of impressiveness being at an end; for even
Title:  the gravest sentiments were constantly being received with a smothered burst
Title:  of unholy mirth, under cover of some remote pew-back, as if the poor parson
Title:  had said a rarely facetious thing. It was a genuine relief to the whole
Title:  congregation when the ordeal was over and the benediction pronounced.
Title:  
Title:     Tom Sawyer went home quite cheerful, thinking to himself that there was
Title:  some satisfaction about divine service when there was a bit of variety in
Title:  it. He had but one marring thought; he was willing that the dog should play
Title:  with his pinchbug, but he did not think it was upright in him to carry it
Title:  off.
Title:  
Title:    ------------------------------------------------------------------------
Title:  
Title:                                   Chapter VI
Title:  
Title:     MONDAY morning found Tom Sawyer miserable. Monday morning always found
Title:  him so -- because it began another week's slow suffering in school. He
Title:  generally began that day with wishing he had had no intervening holiday, it
Title:  made the going into captivity and fetters again so much more odious.
Title:  
Title:     Tom lay thinking. Presently it occurred to him that he wished he was
Title:  sick; then he could stay home from school. Here was a vague possibility. He
Title:  canvassed his system. No ailment was found, and he investigated again. This
Title:  time he thought he could detect colicky symptoms, and he began to encourage
Title:  them with considerable hope. But they soon grew feeble, and presently died
Title:  wholly away. He reflected further. Suddenly he discovered something. One of
Title:  his upper front teeth was loose. This was lucky; he was about to begin to
Title:  groan, as a "starter," as he called it, when it occurred to him that if he
Title:  came into court with that argument, his aunt would pull it out, and that
Title:  would hurt. So he thought he would hold the tooth in reserve for the
