Title:  present, and seek further. Nothing offered for some little time, and then he
Title:  remembered hearing the
Title:  doctor tell about a certain thing that laid up a patient for two or three
Title:  weeks and threatened to make him lose a finger. So the boy eagerly drew his
Title:  sore toe from under the sheet and held it up for inspection. But now he did
Title:  not know the necessary symptoms. However, it seemed well worth while to
Title:  chance it, so he fell to groaning with considerable spirit.
Title:  
Title:     But Sid slept on unconscious.
Title:  
Title:     Tom groaned louder, and fancied that he began to feel pain in the toe.
Title:  
Title:     No result from Sid.
Title:  
Title:     Tom was panting with his exertions by this time. He took a rest and then
Title:  swelled himself up and fetched a succession of admirable groans.
Title:  
Title:     Sid snored on.
Title:  
Title:     Tom was aggravated. He said, "Sid, Sid!" and shook him. This course
Title:  worked well, and Tom began to groan again. Sid yawned, stretched, then
Title:  brought himself up on his elbow with a snort, and began to stare at Tom. Tom
Title:  went on groaning. Sid said:
Title:  
Title:     "Tom! Say, Tom!" [No response.] "Here, Tom! Tom! What is the matter,
Title:  Tom?" And he shook him and looked in his face anxiously.
Title:  
Title:     Tom moaned out:
Title:  
Title:     "Oh, don't, Sid. Don't joggle me."
Title:  
Title:     "Why, what's the matter, Tom? I must call auntie."
Title:  
Title:     "No -- never mind. It'll be over by and by, maybe. Don't call anybody."
Title:  
Title:     "But I must! Don't groan so, Tom, it's awful. How long you been this
Title:  way?"
Title:  
Title:     "Hours. Ouch! Oh, don't stir so, Sid, you'll kill me."
Title:  
Title:     "Tom, why didn't you wake me sooner ? Oh, Tom, don't ! It makes my flesh
Title:  crawl to hear you. Tom, what is the matter?"
Title:  
Title:     "I forgive you everything, Sid. [Groan.] Everything you've ever done to
Title:  me. When I'm gone -- "
Title:  
Title:     "Oh, Tom, you ain't dying, are you? Don't, Tom -- oh, don't. Maybe -- "
Title:  
Title:     "I forgive everybody, Sid. [Groan.] Tell 'em so, Sid. And Sid, you give
Title:  my window-sash and my cat with one eye to that new girl that's come to town,
Title:  and tell her -- "
Title:  
Title:     But Sid had snatched his clothes and gone. Tom was suffering in reality,
Title:  now, so handsomely was his imagination working, and so his groans had
Title:  gathered quite a genuine tone.
Title:  
Title:     Sid flew down-stairs and said:
Title:  
Title:     "Oh, Aunt Polly, come! Tom's dying!"
Title:  
Title:     "Dying!"
Title:  
Title:     "Yes'm. Don't wait -- come quick!"
Title:  
Title:     "Rubbage! I don't believe it!"
Title:  
Title:     But she fled up-stairs, nevertheless, with Sid and Mary at her heels. And
Title:  her face grew white, too, and her lip trembled. When she reached the
Title:  bed-side she gasped out:
Title:  
Title:     "You, Tom! Tom, what's the matter with you?"
Title:  
Title:     "Oh, auntie, I'm -- "
Title:  
Title:     "What's the matter with you -- what is the matter with you, child?"
Title:  
Title:     "Oh, auntie, my sore toe's mortified!"
Title:  
Title:     The old lady sank down into a chair and laughed a little, then cried a
Title:  little, then did both together. This restored her and she said:
Title:  
Title:     "Tom, what a turn you did give me. Now you shut up that nonsense and
Title:  climb out of this."
Title:  
Title:     The groans ceased and the pain vanished from the toe. The boy felt a
Title:  little foolish, and he said:
Title:  
Title:     "Aunt Polly, it seemed mortified, and it hurt so I never minded my tooth
Title:  at all."
Title:  
Title:     "Your tooth, indeed! What's the matter with your tooth?"
Title:  
Title:     "One of them's loose, and it aches perfectly awful."
Title:  
Title:     "There, there, now, don't begin that groaning again. Open your mouth.
Title:  Well -- your tooth IS loose, but you're not going to die about that. Mary,
Title:  get me a silk thread, and a chunk of fire out of the kitchen."
Title:  
Title:     Tom said:
Title:  
Title:     "Oh, please, auntie, don't pull it out. It don't hurt any more. I wish I
Title:  may never stir if it does. Please don't, auntie. I don't want to stay home
Title:  from school."
Title:  
Title:     "Oh, you don't, don't you? So all this row was because you thought you'd
Title:  get to stay home from school and go a-fishing? Tom, Tom, I love you
Title:  so, and you seem to try every way you can to break my old heart with your
Title:  outrageousness." By this time the dental instruments were ready. The old
Title:  lady made one end of the silk thread fast to Tom's tooth with a loop and
Title:  tied the other to the bedpost. Then she seized the chunk of fire and
Title:  suddenly thrust it almost into the boy's face. The tooth hung dangling by
Title:  the bedpost, now.
Title:  
Title:     But all trials bring their compensations. As Tom wended to school after
Title:  breakfast, he was the envy of every boy he met because the gap in his upper
Title:  row of teeth enabled him to expectorate in a new and admirable way. He
Title:  gathered quite a following of lads interested in the exhibition; and one
Title:  that had cut his finger and had been a centre of fascination and homage up
Title:  to this time, now found himself suddenly without an adherent, and shorn of
Title:  his glory. His heart was heavy, and he said with a disdain which he did not
Title:  feel that it wasn't anything to spit like Tom Sawyer; but another boy said,
Title:  "Sour grapes!" and he wandered away a dismantled hero.
Title:  
Title:     Shortly Tom came upon the juvenile pariah of the village, Huckleberry
Title:  Finn, son of the town drunkard. Huckleberry was cordially hated and dreaded
Title:  by all the mothers of the town, because he was idle and lawless and vulgar
Title:  and bad -- and because all their children admired him so, and delighted in
Title:  his forbidden society, and wished they dared to be like him. Tom was like
Title:  the rest of the respectable boys, in that he envied Huckleberry his
Title:  gaudy outcast condition, and was under strict orders not to play with him.
Title:  So he played with him every time he got a chance. Huckleberry was always
Title:  dressed in the cast-off clothes of full-grown men, and they were in
Title:  perennial bloom and fluttering with rags. His hat was a vast ruin with a
Title:  wide crescent lopped out of its brim; his coat, when he wore one, hung
Title:  nearly to his heels and had the rearward buttons far down the back; but one
Title:  suspender supported his trousers; the seat of the trousers bagged low and
Title:  contained nothing, the fringed legs dragged in the dirt when not rolled up.
Title:  
Title:     Huckleberry came and went, at his own free will. He slept on doorsteps in
Title:  fine weather and in empty hogsheads in wet; he did not have to go to school
Title:  or to church, or call any being master or obey anybody; he could go fishing
Title:  or swimming when and where he chose, and stay as long as it suited him;
Title:  nobody forbade him to fight; he could sit up as late as he pleased; he was
Title:  always the first boy that went barefoot in the spring and the last to resume
Title:  leather in the fall; he never had to wash, nor put on clean clothes; he
Title:  could swear wonderfully. In a word, everything that goes to make life
Title:  precious that boy had. So thought every harassed, hampered, respectable boy
Title:  in St. Petersburg.
Title:  
Title:     Tom hailed the romantic outcast:
Title:  
Title:     "Hello, Huckleberry!"
Title:  
Title:     "Hello yourself, and see how you like it."
Title:  
Title:     "What's that you got?"
Title:  
Title:     "Dead cat."
Title:  
Title:     "Lemme see him, Huck. My, he's pretty stiff. Where'd you get him ?"
Title:  
Title:     "Bought him off'n a boy."
Title:  
Title:     "What did you give?"
Title:  
Title:     "I give a blue ticket and a bladder that I got at the slaughter-house."
Title:  
Title:     "Where'd you get the blue ticket?"
Title:  
Title:     "Bought it off'n Ben Rogers two weeks ago for a hoop-stick."
Title:  
Title:     "Say -- what is dead cats good for, Huck?"
Title:  
Title:     "Good for? Cure warts with."
Title:  
Title:     "No! Is that so? I know something that's better."
Title:  
Title:     "I bet you don't. What is it?"
Title:  
Title:     "Why, spunk-water."
Title:  
Title:     "Spunk-water! I wouldn't give a dern for spunk-water."
Title:  
Title:     "You wouldn't, wouldn't you? D'you ever try it?"
Title:  
Title:     "No, I hain't. But Bob Tanner did."
Title:  
Title:     "Who told you so!"
Title:  
Title:     "Why, he told Jeff Thatcher, and Jeff told Johnny Baker, and Johnny told
Title:  Jim Hollis, and Jim told Ben Rogers, and Ben told a nigger, and the nigger
Title:  told me. There now!"
Title:  
Title:     "Well, what of it? They'll all lie. Leastways all but the nigger. I don't
Title:  know him . But I never see a nigger that wouldn't lie. Shucks! Now you tell
Title:  me how Bob Tanner done it, Huck."
Title:  
Title:     "Why, he took and dipped his hand in a rotten stump where the rain-water
Title:  was."
Title:  
Title:     "In the daytime?"
Title:  
Title:     "Certainly."
Title:  
Title:     "With his face to the stump?"
Title:  
Title:     "Yes. Least I reckon so."
Title:  
Title:     "Did he say anything?"
Title:  
Title:     "I don't reckon he did. I don't know."
Title:  
Title:     "Aha! Talk about trying to cure warts with spunk-water such a blame fool
Title:  way as that! Why, that ain't a-going to do any good. You got to go all by
Title:  yourself, to the middle of the woods, where you know there's a spunk-water
Title:  stump, and just as it's midnight you back up against the stump and jam your
Title:  hand in and say:
Title:  
Title:       'Barley-corn, barley-corn, injun-meal shorts,
Title:       Spunk-water, spunk-water, swaller these warts,'
Title:  
Title:  and then walk away quick, eleven steps, with your eyes shut, and then turn
Title:  around three times and walk home without speaking to anybody. Because if you
Title:  speak the charm's busted."
Title:  
Title:     "Well, that sounds like a good way; but that ain't the way Bob Tanner
Title:  done."
Title:  
Title:     "No, sir, you can bet he didn't, becuz he's the wartiest boy in this
Title:  town; and he wouldn't have a wart on him if he'd knowed how to work
Title:  spunk-water. I've took off thousands of warts off of my hands that way,
Title:  Huck. I play with frogs so much that I've always got considerable many
Title:  warts. Sometimes I take 'em off with a bean."
Title:  
Title:     "Yes, bean's good. I've done that."
Title:  
Title:     "Have you? What's your way?"
Title:  
Title:     "You take and split the bean, and cut the wart so as to get some blood,
Title:  and then you put the blood on one piece of the bean and take and dig a hole
Title:  and bury it 'bout midnight at the crossroads in the dark of the moon, and
Title:  then you burn up the rest of the bean. You see that piece that's got the
Title:  blood on it will keep drawing and drawing, trying to fetch the other piece
Title:  to it, and so that helps the blood to draw the wart, and pretty soon off she
Title:  comes."
Title:  
Title:     "Yes, that's it, Huck -- that's it; though when you're burying it if you
Title:  say 'Down bean; off wart; come no more to bother me!' it's better. That's
Title:  the way Joe Harper does, and he's been nearly to Coonville and most
Title:  everywheres. But say -- how do you cure 'em with dead cats?"
Title:  
Title:     "Why, you take your cat and go and get in the graveyard 'long about
Title:  midnight when somebody that was wicked has been buried; and when it's
Title:  midnight a devil will come, or maybe two or three, but you can't see 'em,
Title:  you can only hear something like the wind, or maybe hear 'em talk; and when
Title:  they're taking that feller away, you heave your cat after 'em and say,
Title:  'Devil follow corpse, cat follow devil, warts follow cat, I'm done with ye!'
Title:  That'll fetch ANY wart."
Title:  
Title:     "Sounds right. D'you ever try it, Huck?"
Title:  
Title:     "No, but old Mother Hopkins told me."
Title:  
Title:     "Well, I reckon it's so, then. Becuz they say she's a witch."
Title:  
Title:     "Say! Why, Tom, I know she is. She witched pap. Pap says so his own self.
Title:  He come along one day, and he see she was a-witching him, so he took up a
Title:  rock, and if she hadn't dodged, he'd a got her. Well, that very night he
Title:  rolled off'n a shed wher' he was a layin drunk, and broke his arm."
Title:  
Title:     "Why, that's awful. How did he know she was a-witching him?"
Title:  
Title:     "Lord, pap can tell, easy. Pap says when they keep looking at you right
Title:  stiddy, they're a-witching you. Specially if they mumble. Becuz when they
Title:  mumble they're saying the Lord's Prayer backards."
Title:  
Title:     "Say, Hucky, when you going to try the cat?"
Title:  
Title:     "To-night. I reckon they'll come after old Hoss Williams to-night."
Title:  
Title:     "But they buried him Saturday. Didn't they get him Saturday night?"
Title:  
Title:     "Why, how you talk! How could their charms work till midnight? -- and
Title:  then it's Sunday. Devils don't slosh around much of a Sunday, I don't
Title:  reckon."
Title:  
Title:     "I never thought of that. That's so. Lemme go with you?"
Title:  
Title:     "Of course -- if you ain't afeard."
Title:  
Title:     "Afeard! 'Tain't likely. Will you meow?"
Title:  
Title:     "Yes -- and you meow back, if you get a chance. Last time, you kep' me
Title:  a-meowing around till old
Title:  Hays went to throwing rocks at me and says 'Dern that cat!' and so I hove a
Title:  brick through his window -- but don't you tell."
Title:  
Title:     "I won't. I couldn't meow that night, becuz auntie was watching me, but
Title:  I'll meow this time. Say -- what's that?"
Title:  
Title:     "Nothing but a tick."
Title:  
Title:     "Where'd you get him?"
Title:  
Title:     "Out in the woods."
Title:  
Title:     "What'll you take for him?"
Title:  
Title:     "I don't know. I don't want to sell him."
Title:  
Title:     "All right. It's a mighty small tick, anyway."
Title:  
Title:     "Oh, anybody can run a tick down that don't belong to them. I'm satisfied
Title:  with it. It's a good enough tick for me."
Title:  
Title:     "Sho, there's ticks a plenty. I could have a thousand of 'em if I wanted
Title:  to."
Title:  
Title:     "Well, why don't you? Becuz you know mighty well you can't. This is a
Title:  pretty early tick, I reckon. It's the first one I've seen this year."
Title:  
Title:     "Say, Huck -- I'll give you my tooth for him."
Title:  
Title:     "Less see it."
Title:  
Title:     Tom got out a bit of paper and carefully unrolled it. Huckleberry viewed
Title:  it wistfully. The temptation was very strong. At last he said:
Title:  
Title:     "Is it genuwyne?"
Title:  
Title:     Tom lifted his lip and showed the vacancy.
Title:  
Title:     "Well, all right," said Huckleberry, "it's a trade."
Title:  
Title:     Tom enclosed the tick in the percussion-cap box
Title:  that had lately been the pinchbug's prison, and the boys separated, each
Title:  feeling wealthier than before.
Title:  
Title:     When Tom reached the little isolated frame school-house, he strode in
Title:  briskly, with the manner of one who had come with all honest speed. He hung
Title:  his hat on a peg and flung himself into his seat with business-like
Title:  alacrity. The master, throned on high in his great splint-bottom arm-chair,
Title:  was dozing, lulled by the drowsy hum of study. The interruption roused him.
Title:  
Title:     "Thomas Sawyer!"
Title:  
Title:     Tom knew that when his name was pronounced in full, it meant trouble.
Title:  
Title:     "Sir!"
Title:  
Title:     "Come up here. Now, sir, why are you late again, as usual?"
Title:  
Title:     Tom was about to take refuge in a lie, when he saw two long tails of
Title:  yellow hair hanging down a back that he recognized by the electric sympathy
Title:  of love; and by that form was the only vacant place on the girls' side of
Title:  the school-house. He instantly said:
Title:  
Title:     "I STOPPED TO TALK WITH HUCKLEBERRY FINN!"
Title:  
Title:     The master's pulse stood still, and he stared helplessly. The buzz of
Title:  study ceased. The pupils wondered if this foolhardy boy had lost his mind.
Title:  The master said:
Title:  
Title:     "You -- you did what?"
Title:  
Title:     "Stopped to talk with Huckleberry Finn."
Title:  
Title:     There was no mistaking the words.
Title:  
Title:     "Thomas Sawyer, this is the most astounding confession I have ever
Title:  listened to. No mere ferule will answer for this offence. Take off your
Title:  jacket."
Title:  
Title:     The master's arm performed until it was tired and the stock of switches
Title:  notably diminished. Then the order followed:
Title:  
Title:     "Now, sir, go and sit with the girls! And let this be a warning to you."
Title:  
Title:     The titter that rippled around the room appeared to abash the boy, but in
Title:  reality that result was caused rather more by his worshipful awe of his
Title:  unknown idol and the dread pleasure that lay in his high good fortune. He
Title:  sat down upon the end of the pine bench and the girl hitched herself away
Title:  from him with a toss of her head. Nudges and winks and whispers traversed
Title:  the room, but Tom sat still, with his arms upon the long, low desk before
Title:  him, and seemed to study his book.
Title:  
Title:     By and by attention ceased from him, and the accustomed school murmur
Title:  rose upon the dull air once more. Presently the boy began to steal furtive
Title:  glances at the girl. She observed it, "made a mouth" at him and gave him the
Title:  back of her head for the space of a minute. When she cautiously faced around
Title:  again, a peach lay before her. She thrust it away. Tom gently put it back.
Title:  She thrust it away again, but with less animosity. Tom patiently returned it
Title:  to its place. Then she let it remain. Tom scrawled on his slate, "Please
Title:  take
Title:  it -- I got more." The girl glanced at the words, but made no sign. Now the
Title:  boy began to draw something on the slate, hiding his work with his left
Title:  hand. For a time the girl refused to notice; but her human curiosity
Title:  presently began to manifest itself by hardly perceptible signs. The boy
Title:  worked on, apparently unconscious. The girl made a sort of non-committal
Title:  attempt to see, but the boy did not betray that he was aware of it. At last
Title:  she gave in and hesitatingly whispered:
Title:  
Title:     "Let me see it."
Title:  
Title:     Tom partly uncovered a dismal caricature of a house with two gable ends
Title:  to it and a corkscrew of smoke issuing from the chimney. Then the girl's
Title:  interest began to fasten itself upon the work and she forgot everything
Title:  else. When it was finished, she gazed a moment, then whispered:
Title:  
Title:     "It's nice -- make a man."
Title:  
Title:     The artist erected a man in the front yard, that resembled a derrick. He
Title:  could have stepped over the house; but the girl was not hypercritical; she
Title:  was satisfied with the monster, and whispered:
Title:  
Title:     "It's a beautiful man -- now make me coming along."
Title:  
Title:     Tom drew an hour-glass with a full moon and straw limbs to it and armed
Title:  the spreading fingers with a portentous fan. The girl said:
Title:  
Title:     "It's ever so nice -- I wish I could draw."
Title:  
Title:     "It's easy," whispered Tom, "I'll learn you."
Title:  
Title:     "Oh, will you? When"
Title:  
Title:     "At noon. Do you go home to dinner?"
Title:  
Title:     "I'll stay if you will."
Title:  
Title:     "Good -- that's a whack. What's your name?"
Title:  
Title:     "Becky Thatcher. What's yours? Oh, I know. It's Thomas Sawyer."
Title:  
Title:     "That's the name they lick me by. I'm Tom when I'm good. You call me Tom,
Title:  will you?"
Title:  
Title:     "Yes."
Title:  
Title:     Now Tom began to scrawl something on the slate, hiding the words from the
Title:  girl. But she was not backward this time. She begged to see. Tom said:
Title:  
Title:     "Oh, it ain't anything."
Title:  
Title:     "Yes it is."
Title:  
Title:     "No it ain't. You don't want to see."
Title:  
Title:     "Yes I do, indeed I do. Please let me."
Title:  
Title:     "You'll tell."
Title:  
Title:     "No I won't -- deed and deed and double deed won't."
Title:  
Title:     "You won't tell anybody at all? Ever, as long as you live?"
Title:  
Title:     "No, I won't ever tell anybody. Now let me."
Title:  
Title:     "Oh, you don't want to see!"
Title:  
Title:     "Now that you treat me so, I will see." And she put her small hand upon
Title:  his and a little scuffle ensued, Tom pretending to resist in earnest but
Title:  letting his hand slip by degrees till these words were revealed: "I LOVE
Title:  YOU."
Title:  
Title:     "Oh, you bad thing!" And she hit his hand a smart rap, but reddened and
Title:  looked pleased, nevertheless.
Title:  
Title:     Just at this juncture the boy felt a slow, fateful grip closing on his
Title:  ear, and a steady lifting impulse. In that vise he was borne across the
Title:  house and deposited in his own seat, under a peppering fire of giggles from
Title:  the whole school. Then the master stood over him during a few awful moments,
Title:  and finally moved away to his throne without saying a word. But although
Title:  Tom's ear tingled, his heart was jubilant.
Title:  
Title:     As the school quieted down Tom made an honest effort to study, but the
Title:  turmoil within him was too great. In turn he took his place in the reading
Title:  class and made a botch of it; then in the geography class and turned lakes
Title:  into mountains, mountains into rivers, and rivers into continents, till
Title:  chaos was come again; then in the spelling class, and got "turned down," by
Title:  a succession of mere baby words, till he brought up at the foot and yielded
Title:  up the pewter medal which he had worn with ostentation for months.
Title:  
Title:    ------------------------------------------------------------------------
Title:  
Title:                                   Chapter VII
Title:  
Title:     THE harder Tom tried to fasten his mind on his book, the more his ideas
Title:  wandered. So at last, with a sigh and a yawn, he gave it up. It seemed to
Title:  him that the noon recess would never come. The air was utterly dead. There
Title:  was not a breath stirring. It was the sleepiest of sleepy days. The drowsing
Title:  murmur of the five and twenty studying scholars soothed the soul like the
Title:  spell that is in the murmur of bees. Away off in the flaming sunshine,
Title:  Cardiff Hill lifted its soft green sides through a shimmering veil of heat,
Title:  tinted with the purple of distance; a few birds floated on lazy wing high in
Title:  the air; no other living thing was visible but some cows, and they were
Title:  asleep. Tom's heart ached to be free, or else to have something of interest
Title:  to do to pass the dreary time. His hand wandered into his pocket and his
Title:  face lit up with a glow of gratitude that was prayer, though he did not know
Title:  it. Then furtively the percussion-cap box came out. He released the tick and
Title:  put him on the long flat desk. The creature probably glowed with a gratitude
Title:  that amounted to prayer, too, at this moment, but it was premature: for when
Title:  he started
Title:  thankfully to travel off, Tom turned him aside with a pin and made him take
Title:  a new direction.
Title:  
Title:     Tom's bosom friend sat next him, suffering just as Tom had been, and now
Title:  he was deeply and gratefully interested in this entertainment in an instant.
Title:  This bosom friend was Joe Harper. The two boys were sworn friends all the
Title:  week, and embattled enemies on Saturdays. Joe took a pin out of his lapel
Title:  and began to assist in exercising the prisoner. The sport grew in interest
Title:  momently. Soon Tom said that they were interfering with each other, and
Title:  neither getting the fullest benefit of the tick. So he put Joe's slate on
Title:  the desk and drew a line down the middle of it from top to bottom.
Title:  
Title:     "Now," said he, "as long as he is on your side you can stir him up and
Title:  I'll let him alone; but if you let him get away and get on my side, you're
Title:  to leave him alone as long as I can keep him from crossing over."
Title:  
Title:     "All right, go ahead; start him up."
Title:  
Title:     The tick escaped from Tom, presently, and crossed the equator. Joe
Title:  harassed him awhile, and then he got away and crossed back again. This
Title:  change of base occurred often. While one boy was worrying the tick with
Title:  absorbing interest, the other would look on with interest as strong, the two
Title:  heads bowed together over the slate, and the two souls dead to all things
Title:  else. At last luck seemed to settle and abide with Joe. The tick tried this,
Title:  that, and the other course, and got as excited and as
Title:  anxious as the boys themselves, but time and again just as he would have
Title:  victory in his very grasp, so to speak, and Tom's fingers would be twitching
Title:  to begin, Joe's pin would deftly head him off, and keep possession. At last
Title:  Tom could stand it no longer. The temptation was too strong. So he reached
Title:  out and lent a hand with his pin. Joe was angry in a moment. Said he:
Title:  
Title:     "Tom, you let him alone."
Title:  
Title:     "I only just want to stir him up a little, Joe."
Title:  
Title:     "No, sir, it ain't fair; you just let him alone."
Title:  
Title:     "Blame it, I ain't going to stir him much."
Title:  
Title:     "Let him alone, I tell you."
Title:  
Title:     "I won't!"
Title:  
Title:     "You shall -- he's on my side of the line."
Title:  
Title:     "Look here, Joe Harper, whose is that tick?"
Title:  
Title:     " I don't care whose tick he is -- he's on my side of the line, and you
Title:  sha'n't touch him."
Title:  
Title:     "Well, I'll just bet I will, though. He's my tick and I'll do what I
Title:  blame please with him, or die!"
Title:  
Title:     A tremendous whack came down on Tom's shoulders, and its duplicate on
Title:  Joe's; and for the space of two minutes the dust continued to fly from the
Title:  two jackets and the whole school to enjoy it. The boys had been too absorbed
Title:  to notice the hush that had stolen upon the school awhile before when the
Title:  master came tiptoeing down the room and stood over them. He had contemplated
Title:  a good part of the performance before he contributed his bit of variety to
Title:  it.
Title:  
Title:     When school broke up at noon, Tom flew to Becky Thatcher, and whispered
Title:  in her ear:
Title:  
Title:     "Put on your bonnet and let on you're going home; and when you get to the
Title:  corner, give the rest of 'em the slip, and turn down through the lane and
Title:  come back. I'll go the other way and come it over 'em the same way."
Title:  
Title:     So the one went off with one group of scholars, and the other with
Title:  another. In a little while the two met at the bottom of the lane, and when
Title:  they reached the school they had it all to themselves. Then they sat
Title:  together, with a slate before them, and Tom gave Becky the pencil and held
Title:  her hand in his, guiding it, and so created another surprising house. When
Title:  the interest in art began to wane, the two fell to talking. Tom was swimming
Title:  in bliss. He said:
Title:  
Title:     "Do you love rats?"
Title:  
Title:     "No! I hate them!"
Title:  
Title:     "Well, I do, too -- live ones. But I mean dead ones, to swing round your
Title:  head with a string."
Title:  
Title:     "No, I don't care for rats much, anyway. What I like is chewing-gum."
Title:  
Title:     "Oh, I should say so! I wish I had some now."
Title:  
Title:     "Do you? I've got some. I'll let you chew it awhile, but you must give it
Title:  back to me."
Title:  
Title:     That was agreeable, so they chewed it turn about, and dangled their legs
Title:  against the bench in excess of contentment.
Title:  
Title:     "Was you ever at a circus?" said Tom.
Title:  
Title:     "Yes, and my pa's going to take me again some time, if I'm good."
Title:  
Title:     "I been to the circus three or four times -- lots of times. Church ain't
Title:  shucks to a circus. There's things going on at a circus all the time. I'm
Title:  going to be a clown in a circus when I grow up."
Title:  
Title:     "Oh, are you! That will be nice. They're so lovely, all spotted up."
Title:  
Title:     "Yes, that's so. And they get slathers of money -- most a dollar a day,
Title:  Ben Rogers says. Say, Becky, was you ever engaged?"
Title:  
Title:     "What's that?"
Title:  
Title:     "Why, engaged to be married."
Title:  
Title:     "No."
Title:  
Title:     "Would you like to?"
Title:  
Title:     "I reckon so. I don't know. What is it like?"
Title:  
Title:     "Like? Why it ain't like anything. You only just tell a boy you won't
Title:  ever have anybody but him, ever ever ever, and then you kiss and that's all.
Title:  Anybody can do it."
Title:  
Title:     "Kiss? What do you kiss for?"
Title:  
Title:     "Why, that, you know, is to -- well, they always do that."
Title:  
Title:     "Everybody?"
Title:  
Title:     "Why, yes, everybody that's in love with each other. Do you remember what
Title:  I wrote on the slate?"
Title:  
Title:     "Ye -- yes."
Title:  
Title:     "What was it?"
Title:  
Title:     "I sha'n't tell you."
Title:  
Title:     "Shall I tell you?"
Title:  
Title:     "Ye -- yes -- but some other time."
Title:  
Title:     "No, now."
Title:  
Title:     "No, not now -- to-morrow."
Title:  
Title:     "Oh, no, now. Please, Becky -- I'll whisper it, I'll whisper it ever so
Title:  easy."
Title:  
Title:     Becky hesitating, Tom took silence for consent, and passed his arm about
Title:  her waist and whispered the tale ever so softly, with his mouth close to her
Title:  ear. And then he added:
Title:  
Title:     "Now you whisper it to me -- just the same."
Title:  
Title:     She resisted, for a while, and then said:
Title:  
Title:     "You turn your face away so you can't see, and then I will. But you
Title:  mustn't ever tell anybody -- will you, Tom? Now you won't, will you?"
Title:  
Title:     "No, indeed, indeed I won't. Now, Becky."
Title:  
Title:     He turned his face away. She bent timidly around till her breath stirred
Title:  his curls and whispered, "I -- love -- you!"
Title:  
Title:     Then she sprang away and ran around and around the desks and benches,
Title:  with Tom after her, and took refuge in a corner at last, with her little
Title:  white apron to her face. Tom clasped her about her neck and pleaded:
Title:  
Title:     "Now, Becky, it's all done -- all over but the kiss. Don't you be afraid
Title:  of that -- it ain't anything at all. Please, Becky." And he tugged at her
Title:  apron and the hands.
Title:  
Title:     By and by she gave up, and let her hands drop;
Title:  her face, all glowing with the struggle, came up and submitted. Tom kissed
Title:  the red lips and said:
Title:  
Title:     "Now it's all done, Becky. And always after this, you know, you ain't
Title:  ever to love anybody but me, and you ain't ever to marry anybody but me,
Title:  ever never and forever. Will you?"
Title:  
Title:     "No, I'll never love anybody but you, Tom, and I'll never marry anybody
Title:  but you -- and you ain't to ever marry anybody but me, either."
Title:  
Title:     "Certainly. Of course. That's part of it. And always coming to school or
Title:  when we're going home, you're to walk with me, when there ain't anybody
Title:  looking -- and you choose me and I choose you at parties, because that's the
Title:  way you do when you're engaged."
Title:  
Title:     "It's so nice. I never heard of it before."
Title:  
Title:     "Oh, it's ever so gay! Why, me and Amy Lawrence -- "
Title:  
Title:     The big eyes told Tom his blunder and he stopped, confused.
Title:  
Title:     "Oh, Tom! Then I ain't the first you've ever been engaged to!"
Title:  
Title:     The child began to cry. Tom said:
Title:  
Title:     "Oh, don't cry, Becky, I don't care for her any more."
Title:  
Title:     "Yes, you do, Tom -- you know you do."
Title:  
Title:     Tom tried to put his arm about her neck, but she pushed him away and
Title:  turned her face to the wall, and went on crying. Tom tried again, with
Title:  soothing words in his mouth, and was repulsed again.
Title:  Then his pride was up, and he strode away and went outside. He stood about,
Title:  restless and uneasy, for a while, glancing at the door, every now and then,
Title:  hoping she would repent and come to find him. But she did not. Then he began
Title:  to feel badly and fear that he was in the wrong. It was a hard struggle with
Title:  him to make new advances, now, but he nerved himself to it and entered. She
Title:  was still standing back there in the corner, sobbing, with her face to the
Title:  wall. Tom's heart smote him. He went to her and stood a moment, not knowing
Title:  exactly how to proceed. Then he said hesitatingly:
Title:  
Title:     "Becky, I -- I don't care for anybody but you."
Title:  
Title:     No reply -- but sobs.
Title:  
Title:     "Becky" -- pleadingly. "Becky, won't you say something?"
Title:  
Title:     More sobs.
Title:  
Title:     Tom got out his chiefest jewel, a brass knob from the top of an andiron,
Title:  and passed it around her so that she could see it, and said:
Title:  
Title:     "Please, Becky, won't you take it?"
Title:  
Title:     She struck it to the floor. Then Tom marched out of the house and over
Title:  the hills and far away, to return to school no more that day. Presently
Title:  Becky began to suspect. She ran to the door; he was not in sight; she flew
Title:  around to the play-yard; he was not there. Then she called:
Title:  
Title:     "Tom! Come back, Tom!"
Title:  
Title:     She listened intently, but there was no answer. She had no companions but
Title:  silence and loneliness.
Title:  So she sat down to cry again and upbraid herself; and by this time the
Title:  scholars began to gather again, and she had to hide her griefs and still her
Title:  broken heart and take up the cross of a long, dreary, aching afternoon, with
Title:  none among the strangers about her to exchange sorrows with.
Title:  
Title:    ------------------------------------------------------------------------
Title:  
Title:                                  Chapter VIII
Title:  
Title:     TOM dodged hither and thither through lanes until he was well out of the
Title:  track of returning scholars, and then fell into a moody jog. He crossed a
Title:  small "branch" two or three times, because of a prevailing juvenile
Title:  superstition that to cross water baffled pursuit. Half an hour later he was
Title:  disappearing behind the Douglas mansion on the summit of Cardiff Hill, and
Title:  the school-house was hardly distinguishable away off in the valley behind
Title:  him. He entered a dense wood, picked his pathless way to the centre of it,
Title:  and sat down on a mossy spot under a spreading oak. There was not even a
Title:  zephyr stirring; the dead noonday heat had even stilled the songs of the
Title:  birds; nature lay in a trance that was broken by no sound but the occasional
Title:  far-off hammering of a wood-pecker, and this seemed to render the pervading
Title:  silence and sense of loneliness the more profound. The boy's soul was
Title:  steeped in melancholy; his feelings were in happy accord with his
Title:  surroundings. He sat long with his elbows on his knees and his chin in his
Title:  hands, meditating. It seemed to him that life was but a trouble, at best,
Title:  and he more than half envied Jimmy Hodges, so lately released; it must be
Title:  very peaceful, he thought, to lie and slumber and dream forever and ever,
Title:  with the wind whispering through the trees and caressing the grass and the
Title:  flowers over the grave, and nothing to bother and grieve about, ever any
Title:  more. If he only had a clean Sunday-school record he could be willing to go,
Title:  and be done with it all. Now as to this girl. What had he done? Nothing. He
Title:  had meant the best in the world, and been treated like a dog -- like a very
Title:  dog. She would be sorry some day -- maybe when it was too late. Ah, if he
Title:  could only die temporarily!
Title:  
Title:     But the elastic heart of youth cannot be compressed into one constrained
Title:  shape long at a time. Tom presently began to drift insensibly back into the
Title:  concerns of this life again. What if he turned his back, now, and
Title:  disappeared mysteriously? What if he went away -- ever so far away, into
Title:  unknown countries beyond the seas -- and never came back any more! How would
Title:  she feel then! The idea of being a clown recurred to him now, only to fill
Title:  him with disgust. For frivolity and jokes and spotted tights were an
Title:  offense, when they intruded themselves upon a spirit that was exalted into
Title:  the vague august realm of the romantic. No, he would be a soldier, and
Title:  return after long years, all war-worn and illustrious. No -- better still,
Title:  he would join the Indians, and hunt buffaloes and go on the warpath in the
Title:  mountain ranges and the trackless great plains of
Title:  the Far West, and away in the future come back a great chief, bristling with
Title:  feathers, hideous with paint, and prance into Sunday-school, some drowsy
Title:  summer morning, with a blood-curdling war-whoop, and sear the eyeballs of
Title:  all his companions with unappeasable envy. But no, there was something
Title:  gaudier even than this. He would be a pirate! That was it! Now his future
Title:  lay plain before him, and glowing with unimaginable splendor. How his name
Title:  would fill the world, and make people shudder! How gloriously he would go
Title:  plowing the dancing seas, in his long, low, black-hulled racer, the Spirit
Title:  of the Storm, with his grisly flag flying at the fore! And at the zenith of
Title:  his fame, how he would suddenly appear at the old village and stalk into
Title:  church, brown and weather-beaten, in his black velvet doublet and trunks,
Title:  his great jack-boots, his crimson sash, his belt bristling with
Title:  horse-pistols, his crime-rusted cutlass at his side, his slouch hat with
Title:  waving plumes, his black flag unfurled, with the skull and crossbones on it,
Title:  and hear with swelling ecstasy the whisperings, "It's Tom Sawyer the Pirate!
Title:  -- the Black Avenger of the Spanish Main!"
Title:  
Title:     Yes, it was settled; his career was determined. He would run away from
Title:  home and enter upon it. He would start the very next morning. Therefore he
Title:  must now begin to get ready. He would collect his resources together. He
Title:  went to a rotten log near at hand and began to dig under one end of it with
Title:  his Barlow knife. He soon struck wood that
Title:  sounded hollow. He put his hand there and uttered this incantation
Title:  impressively:
Title:  
Title:     "What hasn't come here, come! What's here, stay here!"
Title:  
Title:     Then he scraped away the dirt, and exposed a pine shingle. He took it up
Title:  and disclosed a shapely little treasure-house whose bottom and sides were of
Title:  shingles. In it lay a marble. Tom's astonishment was boundless! He scratched
Title:  his head with a perplexed air, and said:
Title:  
Title:     "Well, that beats anything!"
Title:  
Title:     Then he tossed the marble away pettishly, and stood cogitating. The truth
Title:  was, that a superstition of his had failed, here, which he and all his
Title:  comrades had always looked upon as infallible. If you buried a marble with
Title:  certain necessary incantations, and left it alone a fortnight, and then
Title:  opened the place with the incantation he had just used, you would find that
Title:  all the marbles you had ever lost had gathered themselves together there,
Title:  meantime, no matter how widely they had been separated. But now, this thing
Title:  had actually and unquestionably failed. Tom's whole structure of faith was
Title:  shaken to its foundations. He had many a time heard of this thing succeeding
Title:  but never of its failing before. It did not occur to him that he had tried
Title:  it several times before, himself, but could never find the hiding-places
Title:  afterward. He puzzled over the matter some time, and finally decided that
Title:  some witch had interfered and broken the charm. He thought he would satisfy
Title:  himself on that point; so he searched around till he found a small sandy
Title:  spot with a little funnel-shaped depression in it. He laid himself down and
Title:  put his mouth close to this depression and called --
Title:  
Title:     "Doodle-bug, doodle-bug, tell me what I want to know! Doodle-bug,
Title:  doodle-bug, tell me what I want to know!"
Title:  
Title:     The sand began to work, and presently a small black bug appeared for a
Title:  second and then darted under again in a fright.
Title:  
Title:     "He dasn't tell! So it was a witch that done it. I just knowed it."
Title:  
Title:     He well knew the futility of trying to contend against witches, so he
Title:  gave up discouraged. But it occurred to him that he might as well have the
Title:  marble he had just thrown away, and therefore he went and made a patient
Title:  search for it. But he could not find it. Now he went back to his
Title:  treasure-house and carefully placed himself just as he had been standing
Title:  when he tossed the marble away; then he took another marble from his pocket
Title:  and tossed it in the same way, saying:
Title:  
Title:     "Brother, go find your brother!"
Title:  
Title:     He watched where it stopped, and went there and looked. But it must have
Title:  fallen short or gone too far; so he tried twice more. The last repetition
Title:  was successful. The two marbles lay within a foot of each other.
Title:  
Title:     Just here the blast of a toy tin trumpet came faintly down the green
Title:  aisles of the forest. Tom
Title:  flung off his jacket and trousers, turned a suspender into a belt, raked
Title:  away some brush behind the rotten log, disclosing a rude bow and arrow, a
Title:  lath sword and a tin trumpet, and in a moment had seized these things and
Title:  bounded away, barelegged, with fluttering shirt. He presently halted under a
Title:  great elm, blew an answering blast, and then began to tiptoe and look warily
Title:  out, this way and that. He said cautiously -- to an imaginary company:
Title:  
Title:     "Hold, my merry men! Keep hid till I blow."
Title:  
Title:     Now appeared Joe Harper, as airily clad and elaborately armed as Tom. Tom
Title:  called:
Title:  
Title:     "Hold! Who comes here into Sherwood Forest without my pass?"
Title:  
Title:     "Guy of Guisborne wants no man's pass. Who art thou that -- that -- "
Title:  
Title:     "Dares to hold such language," said Tom, prompting -- for they talked "by
Title:  the book," from memory.
Title:  
Title:     "Who art thou that dares to hold such language?"
Title:  
Title:     "I, indeed! I am Robin Hood, as thy caitiff carcase soon shall know."
Title:  
Title:     "Then art thou indeed that famous outlaw? Right gladly will I dispute
Title:  with thee the passes of the merry wood. Have at thee!"
Title:  
Title:     They took their lath swords, dumped their other traps on the ground,
Title:  struck a fencing attitude, foot to foot, and began a grave, careful combat,
Title:  "two up and two down." Presently Tom said:
Title:  
Title:     "Now, if you've got the hang, go it lively!"
Title:  
Title:     So they "went it lively," panting and perspiring with the work. By and by
Title:  Tom shouted:
Title:  
Title:     "Fall! fall! Why don't you fall?"
Title:  
Title:     "I sha'n't! Why don't you fall yourself? You're getting the worst of it."
Title:  
Title:     "Why, that ain't anything. I can't fall; that ain't the way it is in the
Title:  book. The book says, 'Then with one back-handed stroke he slew poor Guy of
Title:  Guisborne.' You're to turn around and let me hit you in the back."
Title:  
Title:     There was no getting around the authorities, so Joe turned, received the
Title:  whack and fell.
Title:  
Title:     "Now," said Joe, getting up, "you got to let me kill you. That's fair."
Title:  
Title:     "Why, I can't do that, it ain't in the book."
Title:  
Title:     "Well, it's blamed mean -- that's all."
Title:  
Title:     "Well, say, Joe, you can be Friar Tuck or Much the miller's son, and lam
Title:  me with a quarter-staff; or I'll be the Sheriff of Nottingham and you be
Title:  Robin Hood a little while and kill me."
Title:  
Title:     This was satisfactory, and so these adventures were carried out. Then Tom
Title:  became Robin Hood again, and was allowed by the treacherous nun to bleed his
Title:  strength away through his neglected wound. And at last Joe, representing a
Title:  whole tribe of weeping outlaws, dragged him sadly forth, gave his bow into
Title:  his feeble hands, and Tom said, "Where this arrow falls, there bury poor
Title:  Robin Hood under the greenwood tree." Then he shot the arrow and fell back
Title:  and would have died, but he
Title:  lit on a nettle and sprang up too gaily for a corpse.
Title:  
Title:     The boys dressed themselves, hid their accoutrements, and went off
Title:  grieving that there were no outlaws any more, and wondering what modern
Title:  civilization could claim to have done to compensate for their loss. They
Title:  said they would rather be outlaws a year in Sherwood Forest than President
Title:  of the United States forever.
Title:  
Title:    ------------------------------------------------------------------------
Title:  
Title:                                   Chapter IX
Title:  
Title:     AT half-past nine, that night, Tom and Sid were sent to bed, as usual.
Title:  They said their prayers, and Sid was soon asleep. Tom lay awake and waited,
Title:  in restless impatience. When it seemed to him that it must be nearly
Title:  daylight, he heard the clock strike ten! This was despair. He would have
Title:  tossed and fidgeted, as his nerves demanded, but he was afraid he might wake
Title:  Sid. So he lay still, and stared up into the dark. Everything was dismally
Title:  still. By and by, out of the stillness, little, scarcely perceptible noises
Title:  began to emphasize themselves. The ticking of the clock began to bring
Title:  itself into notice. Old beams began to crack mysteriously. The stairs
Title:  creaked faintly. Evidently spirits were abroad. A measured, muffled snore
Title:  issued from Aunt Polly's chamber. And now the tiresome chirping of a cricket
Title:  that no human ingenuity could locate, began. Next the ghastly ticking of a
Title:  death-watch in the wall at the bed's head made Tom shudder -- it meant that
Title:  somebody's days were numbered. Then the howl of a far-off dog rose on the
Title:  night air, and was answered by a fainter howl from a remoter distance. Tom
Title:  was in an agony. At last he was satisfied that time had ceased and eternity
Title:  begun; he began to doze, in spite of himself; the clock chimed eleven, but
Title:  he did not hear it. And then there came, mingling with his half-formed
Title:  dreams, a most melancholy caterwauling. The raising of a neighboring window
Title:  disturbed him. A cry of "Scat! you devil!" and the crash of an empty bottle
Title:  against the back of his aunt's woodshed brought him wide awake, and a single
Title:  minute later he was dressed and out of the window and creeping along the
Title:  roof of the "ell" on all fours. He "meow'd" with caution once or twice, as
Title:  he went; then jumped to the roof of the woodshed and thence to the ground.
Title:  Huckleberry Finn was there, with his dead cat. The boys moved off and
Title:  disappeared in the gloom. At the end of half an hour they were wading
Title:  through the tall grass of the graveyard.
Title:  
Title:     It was a graveyard of the old-fashioned Western kind. It was on a hill,
Title:  about a mile and a half from the village. It had a crazy board fence around
Title:  it, which leaned inward in places, and outward the rest of the time, but
Title:  stood upright nowhere. Grass and weeds grew rank over the whole cemetery.
Title:  All the old graves were sunken in, there was not a tombstone on the place;
Title:  round-topped, worm-eaten boards staggered over the graves, leaning for
Title:  support and finding none. "Sacred to the memory of" So-
Title:  and-So had been painted on them once, but it could no longer have been read,
Title:  on the most of them, now, even if there had been light.
Title:  
Title:     A faint wind moaned through the trees, and Tom feared it might be the
Title:  spirits of the dead, complaining at being disturbed. The boys talked little,
Title:  and only under their breath, for the time and the place and the pervading
Title:  solemnity and silence oppressed their spirits. They found the sharp new heap
Title:  they were seeking, and ensconced themselves within the protection of three
Title:  great elms that grew in a bunch within a few feet of the grave.
Title:  
Title:     Then they waited in silence for what seemed a long time. The hooting of a
Title:  distant owl was all the sound that troubled the dead stillness. Tom's
Title:  reflections grew oppressive. He must force some talk. So he said in a
Title:  whisper:
Title:  
Title:     "Hucky, do you believe the dead people like it for us to be here?"
Title:  
Title:     Huckleberry whispered:
Title:  
Title:     "I wisht I knowed. It's awful solemn like, ain't it?"
Title:  
Title:     "I bet it is."
Title:  
Title:     There was a considerable pause, while the boys canvassed this matter
Title:  inwardly. Then Tom whispered:
Title:  
Title:     "Say, Hucky -- do you reckon Hoss Williams hears us talking?"
Title:  
Title:     "O' course he does. Least his sperrit does."
Title:  
Title:     Tom, after a pause:
Title:  
Title:     "I wish I'd said Mister Williams. But I never meant any harm. Everybody
Title:  calls him Hoss."
Title:  
Title:     "A body can't be too partic'lar how they talk 'bout these-yer dead
Title:  people, Tom."
Title:  
Title:     This was a damper, and conversation died again.
Title:  
Title:     Presently Tom seized his comrade's arm and said:
Title:  
Title:     "Sh!"
Title:  
Title:     "What is it, Tom?" And the two clung together with beating hearts.
Title:  
Title:     "Sh! There 'tis again! Didn't you hear it?"
Title:  
Title:     "I -- "
Title:  
Title:     "There! Now you hear it."
Title:  
Title:     "Lord, Tom, they're coming! They're coming, sure. What'll we do?"
Title:  
Title:     "I dono. Think they'll see us?"
Title:  
Title:     "Oh, Tom, they can see in the dark, same as cats. I wisht I hadn't come."
Title:  
Title:     "Oh, don't be afeard. I don't believe they'll bother us. We ain't doing
Title:  any harm. If we keep perfectly still, maybe they won't notice us at all."
Title:  
Title:     "I'll try to, Tom, but, Lord, I'm all of a shiver."
Title:  
Title:     "Listen!"
Title:  
Title:     The boys bent their heads together and scarcely breathed. A muffled sound
Title:  of voices floated up from the far end of the graveyard.
Title:  
Title:     "Look! See there!" whispered Tom. "What is it?"
Title:  
Title:     "It's devil-fire. Oh, Tom, this is awful."
Title:  
Title:     Some vague figures approached through the gloom, swinging an
Title:  old-fashioned tin lantern that freckled
Title:  the ground with innumerable little spangles of light. Presently Huckleberry
Title:  whispered with a shudder:
Title:  
Title:     "It's the devils sure enough. Three of 'em! Lordy, Tom, we're goners! Can
Title:  you pray?"
Title:  
Title:     "I'll try, but don't you be afeard. They ain't going to hurt us. 'Now I
Title:  lay me down to sleep, I -- '"
Title:  
Title:     "Sh!"
Title:  
Title:     "What is it, Huck?"
Title:  
Title:     "They're humans! One of 'em is, anyway. One of 'em's old Muff Potter's
Title:  voice."
Title:  
Title:     "No -- 'tain't so, is it?"
Title:  
Title:     "I bet I know it. Don't you stir nor budge. He ain't sharp enough to
Title:  notice us. Drunk, the same as usual, likely -- blamed old rip!"
Title:  
Title:     "All right, I'll keep still. Now they're stuck. Can't find it. Here they
Title:  come again. Now they're hot. Cold again. Hot again. Red hot! They're p'inted
Title:  right, this time. Say, Huck, I know another o' them voices; it's Injun Joe."
Title:  
Title:     "That's so -- that murderin' half-breed! I'd druther they was devils a
Title:  dern sight. What kin they be up to?"
Title:  
Title:     The whisper died wholly out, now, for the three men had reached the grave
Title:  and stood within a few feet of the boys' hiding-place.
Title:  
Title:     "Here it is," said the third voice; and the owner of it held the lantern
Title:  up and revealed the face of young Doctor Robinson.
Title:  
Title:     Potter and Injun Joe were carrying a handbarrow
Title:  with a rope and a couple of shovels on it. They cast down their load and
Title:  began to open the grave. The doctor put the lantern at the head of the grave
Title:  and came and sat down with his back against one of the elm trees. He was so
Title:  close the boys could have touched him.
Title:  
Title:     "Hurry, men!" he said, in a low voice; "the moon might come out at any
Title:  moment."
Title:  
Title:     They growled a response and went on digging. For some time there was no
Title:  noise but the grating sound of the spades discharging their freight of mould
Title:  and gravel. It was very monotonous. Finally a spade struck upon the coffin
Title:  with a dull woody accent, and within another minute or two the men had
Title:  hoisted it out on the ground. They pried off the lid with their shovels, got
Title:  out the body and dumped it rudely on the ground. The moon drifted from
Title:  behind the clouds and exposed the pallid face. The barrow was got ready and
Title:  the corpse placed on it, covered with a blanket, and bound to its place with
Title:  the rope. Potter took out a large spring-knife and cut off the dangling end
Title:  of the rope and then said:
Title:  
Title:     "Now the cussed thing's ready, Sawbones, and you'll just out with another
Title:  five, or here she stays."
Title:  
Title:     "That's the talk!" said Injun Joe.
Title:  
Title:     "Look here, what does this mean?" said the doctor. "You required your pay
Title:  in advance, and I've paid you."
Title:  
Title:     "Yes, and you done more than that," said Injun
Title:  Joe, approaching the doctor, who was now standing. "Five years ago you drove
Title:  me away from your father's kitchen one night, when I come to ask for
Title:  something to eat, and you said I warn't there for any good; and when I swore
Title:  I'd get even with you if it took a hundred years, your father had me jailed
Title:  for a vagrant. Did you think I'd forget? The Injun blood ain't in me for
Title:  nothing. And now I've got you, and you got to settle, you know!"
Title:  
Title:     He was threatening the doctor, with his fist in his face, by this time.
Title:  The doctor struck out suddenly and stretched the ruffian on the ground.
Title:  Potter dropped his knife, and exclaimed:
Title:  
Title:     "Here, now, don't you hit my pard!" and the next moment he had grappled
Title:  with the doctor and the two were struggling with might and main, trampling
Title:  the grass and tearing the ground with their heels. Injun Joe sprang to his
Title:  feet, his eyes flaming with passion, snatched up Potter's knife, and went
Title:  creeping, catlike and stooping, round and round about the combatants,
Title:  seeking an opportunity. All at once the doctor flung himself free, seized
Title:  the heavy headboard of Williams' grave and felled Potter to the earth with
Title:  it -- and in the same instant the half-breed saw his chance and drove the
Title:  knife to the hilt in the young man's breast. He reeled and fell partly upon
Title:  Potter, flooding him with his blood, and in the same moment the clouds
Title:  blotted out the dreadful spectacle and the two frightened boys went speeding
Title:  away in the dark.
Title:  
Title:     Presently, when the moon emerged again, Injun Joe was standing over the
Title:  two forms, contemplating them. The doctor murmured inarticulately, gave a
Title:  long gasp or two and was still. The half-breed muttered:
Title:  
Title:     "That score is settled -- damn you."
Title:  
Title:     Then he robbed the body. After which he put the fatal knife in Potter's
Title:  open right hand, and sat down on the dismantled coffin. Three -- four --
Title:  five minutes passed, and then Potter began to stir and moan. His hand closed
Title:  upon the knife; he raised it, glanced at it, and let it fall, with a
Title:  shudder. Then he sat up, pushing the body from him, and gazed at it, and
Title:  then around him, confusedly. His eyes met Joe's.
Title:  
Title:     "Lord, how is this, Joe?" he said.
Title:  
Title:     "It's a dirty business," said Joe, without moving.
Title:  
Title:     "What did you do it for?"
Title:  
Title:     "I! I never done it!"
Title:  
Title:     "Look here! That kind of talk won't wash."
Title:  
Title:     Potter trembled and grew white.
Title:  
Title:     "I thought I'd got sober. I'd no business to drink to-night. But it's in
Title:  my head yet -- worse'n when we started here. I'm all in a muddle; can't
Title:  recollect anything of it, hardly. Tell me, Joe -- honest, now, old feller --
Title:  did I do it? Joe, I never meant to -- 'pon my soul and honor, I never meant
Title:  to, Joe. Tell me how it was, Joe. Oh, it's awful -- and him so young and
Title:  promising."
Title:  
Title:     "Why, you two was scuffling, and he fetched you
Title:  one with the headboard and you fell flat; and then up you come, all reeling
Title:  and staggering like, and snatched the knife and jammed it into him, just as
Title:  he fetched you another awful clip -- and here you've laid, as dead as a
Title:  wedge til now."
Title:  
Title:     "Oh, I didn't know what I was a-doing. I wish I may die this minute if I
Title:  did. It was all on account of the whiskey and the excitement, I reckon. I
Title:  never used a weepon in my life before, Joe. I've fought, but never with
Title:  weepons. They'll all say that. Joe, don't tell! Say you won't tell, Joe --
Title:  that's a good feller. I always liked you, Joe, and stood up for you, too.
Title:  Don't you remember? You won't tell, will you, Joe?" And the poor creature
Title:  dropped on his knees before the stolid murderer, and clasped his appealing
Title:  hands.
Title:  
Title:     "No, you've always been fair and square with me, Muff Potter, and I won't
Title:  go back on you. There, now, that's as fair as a man can say."
Title:  
Title:     "Oh, Joe, you're an angel. I'll bless you for this the longest day I
Title:  live." And Potter began to cry.
Title:  
Title:     "Come, now, that's enough of that. This ain't any time for blubbering.
Title:  You be off yonder way and I'll go this. Move, now, and don't leave any
Title:  tracks behind you."
Title:  
Title:     Potter started on a trot that quickly increased to a run. The half-breed
Title:  stood looking after him. He muttered:
Title:  
Title:     "If he's as much stunned with the lick and fuddled with the rum as he had
Title:  the look of being, he
Title:  won't think of the knife till he's gone so far he'll be afraid to come back
Title:  after it to such a place by himself -- chicken-heart!"
Title:  
Title:     Two or three minutes later the murdered man, the blanketed corpse, the
Title:  lidless coffin, and the open grave were under no inspection but the moon's.
Title:  The stillness was complete again, too.
Title:  
Title:    ------------------------------------------------------------------------
Title:  
Title:                                    Chapter X
Title:  
Title:     THE two boys flew on and on, toward the village, speechless with horror.
Title:  They glanced backward over their shoulders from time to time,
Title:  apprehensively, as if they feared they might be followed. Every stump that
Title:  started up in their path seemed a man and an enemy, and made them catch
Title:  their breath; and as they sped by some outlying cottages that lay near the
Title:  village, the barking of the aroused watch-dogs seemed to give wings to their
Title:  feet.
Title:  
Title:     "If we can only get to the old tannery before we break down!" whispered
Title:  Tom, in short catches between breaths. "I can't stand it much longer."
Title:  
Title:     Huckleberry's hard pantings were his only reply, and the boys fixed their
Title:  eyes on the goal of their hopes and bent to their work to win it. They
Title:  gained steadily on it, and at last, breast to breast, they burst through the
Title:  open door and fell grateful and exhausted in the sheltering shadows beyond.
Title:  By and by their pulses slowed down, and Tom whispered:
Title:  
Title:     "Huckleberry, what do you reckon'll come of this?"
Title:  
Title:     "If Doctor Robinson dies, I reckon hanging'll come of it."
Title:  
Title:     "Do you though?"
Title:  
Title:     "Why, I know it, Tom."
Title:  
Title:     Tom thought a while, then he said:
Title:  
Title:     "Who'll tell? We?"
Title:  
Title:     "What are you talking about? S'pose something happened and Injun Joe
Title:  didn't hang? Why, he'd kill us some time or other, just as dead sure as
Title:  we're a laying here."
Title:  
Title:     "That's just what I was thinking to myself, Huck."
Title:  
Title:     "If anybody tells, let Muff Potter do it, if he's fool enough. He's
Title:  generally drunk enough."
Title:  
Title:     Tom said nothing -- went on thinking. Presently he whispered:
Title:  
Title:     "Huck, Muff Potter don't know it. How can he tell?"
Title:  
Title:     "What's the reason he don't know it?"
Title:  
Title:     "Because he'd just got that whack when Injun Joe done it. D'you reckon he
Title:  could see anything? D'you reckon he knowed anything?"
Title:  
Title:     "By hokey, that's so, Tom!"
Title:  
Title:     "And besides, look-a-here -- maybe that whack done for him!"
Title:  
Title:     "No, 'taint likely, Tom. He had liquor in him; I could see that; and
Title:  besides, he always has. Well, when pap's full, you might take and belt him
Title:  over the head with a church and you couldn't phase him. He says so, his own
Title:  self. So it's the same with
Title:  Muff Potter, of course. But if a man was dead sober, I reckon maybe that
Title:  whack might fetch him; I dono."
Title:  
Title:     After another reflective silence, Tom said:
Title:  
Title:     "Hucky, you sure you can keep mum?"
Title:  
Title:     "Tom, we got to keep mum. You know that. That Injun devil wouldn't make
Title:  any more of drownding us than a couple of cats, if we was to squeak 'bout
Title:  this and they didn't hang him. Now, look-a-here, Tom, less take and swear to
Title:  one another -- that's what we got to do -- swear to keep mum."
Title:  
Title:     "I'm agreed. It's the best thing. Would you just hold hands and swear
Title:  that we -- "
Title:  
Title:     "Oh no, that wouldn't do for this. That's good enough for little rubbishy
Title:  common things -- specially with gals, cuz they go back on you anyway, and
Title:  blab if they get in a huff -- but there orter be writing 'bout a big thing
Title:  like this. And blood."
Title:  
Title:     Tom's whole being applauded this idea. It was deep, and dark, and awful;
Title:  the hour, the circumstances, the surroundings, were in keeping with it. He
Title:  picked up a clean pine shingle that lay in the moon-light, took a little
Title:  fragment of "red keel" out of his pocket, got the moon on his work, and
Title:  painfully scrawled these lines, emphasizing each slow down-stroke by
Title:  clamping his tongue between his teeth, and letting up the pressure on the
Title:  up-strokes. [See next page.]
Title:  
Title:     Huckleberry was filled with admiration of Tom's facility in writing, and
Title:  the sublimity of his language.
Title:  He at once took a pin from his lapel and was going to prick his flesh, but
Title:  Tom said:
Title:  
Title:     "Hold on! Don't do that. A pin's brass. It might have verdigrease on it."
Title:  
Title:     "What's verdigrease?"
Title:  
Title:     "It's p'ison. That's what it is. You just swaller some of it once --
Title:  you'll see."
Title:  
Title:     So Tom unwound the thread from one of his needles, and each boy pricked
Title:  the ball of his thumb and squeezed out a drop of blood. In time, after many
Title:  squeezes, Tom managed to sign his initials, using
Title:  the ball of his little finger for a pen. Then he showed Huckleberry how to
Title:  make an H and an F, and the oath was complete. They buried the shingle close
Title:  to the wall, with some dismal ceremonies and incantations, and the fetters
Title:  that bound their tongues were considered to be locked and the key thrown
Title:  away.
Title:  
Title:     A figure crept stealthily through a break in the other end of the ruined
Title:  building, now, but they did not notice it.
Title:  
Title:     "Tom," whispered Huckleberry, "does this keep us from ever telling --
Title:  always?"
Title:  
Title:     "Of course it does. It don't make any difference what happens, we got to
Title:  keep mum. We'd drop down dead -- don't you know that?"
Title:  
Title:     "Yes, I reckon that's so."
Title:  
Title:     They continued to whisper for some little time. Presently a dog set up a
Title:  long, lugubrious howl just outside -- within ten feet of them. The boys
Title:  clasped each other suddenly, in an agony of fright.
Title:  
Title:     "Which of us does he mean?" gasped Huckleberry.
Title:  
Title:     "I dono -- peep through the crack. Quick!"
Title:  
Title:     "No, you, Tom!"
Title:  
Title:     "I can't -- I can't do it, Huck!"
Title:  
Title:     "Please, Tom. There 'tis again!"
Title:  
Title:     "Oh, lordy, I'm thankful!" whispered Tom. "I know his voice. It's Bull
Title:  Harbison." *
Title:  
Title:  
Title:  Note: * If Mr. Harbison had owned a slave named Bull, Tom would have spoken
Title:  of him as "Harbison's Bull," but a son or a dog of that name was "Bull
Title:  Harbison."
Title:  
Title:     "Oh, that's good -- I tell you, Tom, I was most scared to death; I'd a
Title:  bet anything it was a stray dog."
Title:  
Title:     The dog howled again. The boys' hearts sank once more.
Title:  
Title:     "Oh, my! that ain't no Bull Harbison!" whispered Huckleberry. " Do ,
Title:  Tom!"
Title:  
Title:     Tom, quaking with fear, yielded, and put his eye to the crack. His
Title:  whisper was hardly audible when he said:
Title:  
Title:     "Oh, Huck, IT'S A STRAY DOG!"
Title:  
Title:     "Quick, Tom, quick! Who does he mean?"
Title:  
Title:     "Huck, he must mean us both -- we're right together."
Title:  
Title:     "Oh, Tom, I reckon we're goners. I reckon there ain't no mistake 'bout
Title:  where I'll go to. I been so wicked."
Title:  
Title:     "Dad fetch it! This comes of playing hookey and doing everything a
Title:  feller's told not to do. I might a been good, like Sid, if I'd a tried --
Title:  but no, I wouldn't, of course. But if ever I get off this time, I lay I'll
Title:  just waller in Sunday-schools!" And Tom began to snuffle a little.
Title:  
Title:     " You bad!" and Huckleberry began to snuffle too. "Consound it, Tom
Title:  Sawyer, you're just old pie, 'longside o' what I am. Oh, lordy , lordy,
Title:  lordy, I wisht I only had half your chance."
Title:  
Title:     Tom choked off and whispered:
Title:  
Title:     "Look, Hucky, look! He's got his BACK to us!"
Title:  
Title:     Hucky looked, with joy in his heart.
Title:  
Title:     "Well, he has, by jingoes! Did he before?"
Title:  
Title:     "Yes, he did. But I, like a fool, never thought. Oh, this is bully, you
Title:  know. Now who can he mean?"
Title:  
Title:     The howling stopped. Tom pricked up his ears.
Title:  
Title:     "Sh! What's that?" he whispered.
Title:  
Title:     "Sounds like -- like hogs grunting. No -- it's somebody snoring, Tom."
Title:  
Title:     "That is it! Where 'bouts is it, Huck?"
Title:  
Title:     "I bleeve it's down at 'tother end. Sounds so, anyway. Pap used to sleep
Title:  there, sometimes, 'long with the hogs, but laws bless you, he just lifts
Title:  things when he snores. Besides, I reckon he ain't ever coming back to this
Title:  town any more."
Title:  
Title:     The spirit of adventure rose in the boys' souls once more.
Title:  
Title:     "Hucky, do you das't to go if I lead?"
Title:  
Title:     "I don't like to, much. Tom, s'pose it's Injun Joe!"
Title:  
Title:     Tom quailed. But presently the temptation rose up strong again and the
Title:  boys agreed to try, with the understanding that they would take to their
Title:  heels if the snoring stopped. So they went tiptoeing stealthily down, the
Title:  one behind the other. When they had got to within five steps of the snorer,
Title:  Tom stepped on a stick, and it broke with a sharp snap. The man moaned,
Title:  writhed a little, and his face came into the moonlight. It was Muff Potter.
Title:  The boys' hearts had stood still, and their hopes too, when the man moved,
Title:  but their fears passed away now. They
Title:  tiptoed out, through the broken weather-boarding, and stopped at a little
Title:  distance to exchange a parting word. That long, lugubrious howl rose on the
Title:  night air again! They turned and saw the strange dog standing within a few
Title:  feet of where Potter was lying, and facing Potter, with his nose pointing
Title:  heavenward.
Title:  
Title:     "Oh, geeminy, it's him!" exclaimed both boys, in a breath.
Title:  
Title:     "Say, Tom -- they say a stray dog come howling around Johnny Miller's
Title:  house, 'bout midnight, as much as two weeks ago; and a whippoorwill come in
Title:  and lit on the banisters and sung, the very same evening; and there ain't
Title:  anybody dead there yet."
Title:  
Title:     "Well, I know that. And suppose there ain't. Didn't Gracie Miller fall in
Title:  the kitchen fire and burn herself terrible the very next Saturday?"
Title:  
Title:     "Yes, but she ain't dead. And what's more, she's getting better, too."
Title:  
Title:     "All right, you wait and see. She's a goner, just as dead sure as Muff
Title:  Potter's a goner. That's what the niggers say, and they know all about these
Title:  kind of things, Huck."
Title:  
Title:     Then they separated, cogitating. When Tom crept in at his bedroom window
Title:  the night was almost spent. He undressed with excessive caution, and fell
Title:  asleep congratulating himself that nobody knew of his escapade. He was not
Title:  aware that the gently-snoring Sid was awake, and had been so for an hour.
Title:  
Title:     When Tom awoke, Sid was dressed and gone.
Title:  There was a late look in the light, a late sense in the atmosphere. He was
Title:  startled. Why had he not been called -- persecuted till he was up, as usual?
Title:  The thought filled him with bodings. Within five minutes he was dressed and
Title:  down-stairs, feeling sore and drowsy. The family were still at table, but
Title:  they had finished breakfast. There was no voice of rebuke; but there were
Title:  averted eyes; there was a silence and an air of solemnity that struck a
Title:  chill to the culprit's heart. He sat down and tried to seem gay, but it was
Title:  up-hill work; it roused no smile, no response, and he lapsed into silence
Title:  and let his heart sink down to the depths.
Title:  
Title:     After breakfast his aunt took him aside, and Tom almost brightened in the
Title:  hope that he was going to be flogged; but it was not so. His aunt wept over
Title:  him and asked him how he could go and break her old heart so; and finally
Title:  told him to go on, and ruin himself and bring her gray hairs with sorrow to
Title:  the grave, for it was no use for her to try any more. This was worse than a
Title:  thousand whippings, and Tom's heart was sorer now than his body. He cried,
Title:  he pleaded for forgiveness, promised to reform over and over again, and then
Title:  received his dismissal, feeling that he had won but an imperfect forgiveness
Title:  and established but a feeble confidence.
Title:  
Title:     He left the presence too miserable to even feel revengeful toward Sid;
Title:  and so the latter's prompt retreat through the back gate was unnecessary. He
Title:  moped to school gloomy and sad, and took his flogging,
Title:  along with Joe Harper, for playing hookey the day before, with the air of
Title:  one whose heart was busy with heavier woes and wholly dead to trifles. Then
Title:  he betook himself to his seat, rested his elbows on his desk and his jaws in
Title:  his hands, and stared at the wall with the stony stare of suffering that has
Title:  reached the limit and can no further go. His elbow was pressing against some
Title:  hard substance. After a long time he slowly and sadly changed his position,
Title:  and took up this object with a sigh. It was in a paper. He unrolled it. A
Title:  long, lingering, colossal sigh followed, and his heart broke. It was his
Title:  brass andiron knob!
Title:  
Title:     This final feather broke the camel's back.
Title:  
Title:    ------------------------------------------------------------------------
Title:  
Title:                                   Chapter XI
Title:  
Title:     CLOSE upon the hour of noon the whole village was suddenly electrified
Title:  with the ghastly news. No need of the as yet undreamed-of telegraph; the
Title:  tale flew from man to man, from group to group, from house to house, with
Title:  little less than telegraphic speed. Of course the schoolmaster gave holiday
Title:  for that afternoon; the town would have thought strangely of him if he had
Title:  not.
Title:  
Title:     A gory knife had been found close to the murdered man, and it had been
Title:  recognized by somebody as belonging to Muff Potter -- so the story ran. And
Title:  it was said that a belated citizen had come upon Potter washing himself in
Title:  the "branch" about one or two o'clock in the morning, and that Potter had at
Title:  once sneaked off -- suspicious circumstances, especially the washing which
Title:  was not a habit with Potter. It was also said that the town had been
Title:  ransacked for this "murderer" (the public are not slow in the matter of
Title:  sifting evidence and arriving at a verdict), but that he could not be found.
Title:  Horsemen had departed down all the roads in every direction, and the Sheriff
Title:  "was confident" that he would be captured before night.
Title:  
Title:     All the town was drifting toward the graveyard. Tom's heartbreak vanished
Title:  and he joined the procession, not because he would not a thousand times
Title:  rather go anywhere else, but because an awful, unaccountable fascination
Title:  drew him on. Arrived at the dreadful place, he wormed his small body through
Title:  the crowd and saw the dismal spectacle. It seemed to him an age since he was
Title:  there before. Somebody pinched his arm. He turned, and his eyes met
Title:  Huckleberry's. Then both looked elsewhere at once, and wondered if anybody
Title:  had noticed anything in their mutual glance. But everybody was talking, and
Title:  intent upon the grisly spectacle before them.
Title:  
Title:     "Poor fellow!" "Poor young fellow!" "This ought to be a lesson to grave
Title:  robbers!" "Muff Potter'll hang for this if they catch him!" This was the
Title:  drift of remark; and the minister said, "It was a judgment; His hand is
Title:  here."
Title:  
Title:     Now Tom shivered from head to heel; for his eye fell upon the stolid face
Title:  of Injun Joe. At this moment the crowd began to sway and struggle, and
Title:  voices shouted, "It's him! it's him! he's coming himself!"
Title:  
Title:     "Who? Who?" from twenty voices.
Title:  
Title:     "Muff Potter!"
Title:  
Title:     "Hallo, he's stopped! -- Look out, he's turning! Don't let him get away!"
Title:  
Title:     People in the branches of the trees over Tom's head said he wasn't trying
Title:  to get away -- he only looked doubtful and perplexed.
Title:  
Title:     "Infernal impudence!" said a bystander; "wanted to come and take a quiet
Title:  look at his work, I reckon -- didn't expect any company."
Title:  
Title:     The crowd fell apart, now, and the Sheriff came through, ostentatiously
Title:  leading Potter by the arm. The poor fellow's face was haggard, and his eyes
Title:  showed the fear that was upon him. When he stood before the murdered man, he
Title:  shook as with a palsy, and he put his face in his hands and burst into
Title:  tears.
Title:  
Title:     "I didn't do it, friends," he sobbed; "'pon my word and honor I never
Title:  done it."
Title:  
Title:     "Who's accused you?" shouted a voice.
Title:  
Title:     This shot seemed to carry home. Potter lifted his face and looked around
Title:  him with a pathetic hopelessness in his eyes. He saw Injun Joe, and
Title:  exclaimed:
Title:  
Title:     "Oh, Injun Joe, you promised me you'd never -- "
Title:  
Title:     "Is that your knife?" and it was thrust before him by the Sheriff.
Title:  
Title:     Potter would have fallen if they had not caught him and eased him to the
Title:  ground. Then he said:
Title:  
Title:     "Something told me 't if I didn't come back and get -- " He shuddered;
Title:  then waved his nerveless hand with a vanquished gesture and said, "Tell 'em,
Title:  Joe, tell 'em -- it ain't any use any more."
Title:  
Title:     Then Huckleberry and Tom stood dumb and staring, and heard the
Title:  stony-hearted liar reel off his serene statement, they expecting every
Title:  moment that the clear sky would deliver God's lightnings upon his head, and
Title:  wondering to see how long the stroke
Title:  was delayed. And when he had finished and still stood alive and whole, their
Title:  wavering impulse to break their oath and save the poor betrayed prisoner's
Title:  life faded and vanished away, for plainly this miscreant had sold himself to
Title:  Satan and it would be fatal to meddle with the property of such a power as
Title:  that.
Title:  
Title:     "Why didn't you leave? What did you want to come here for?" somebody
Title:  said.
Title:  
Title:     "I couldn't help it -- I couldn't help it," Potter moaned. "I wanted to
Title:  run away, but I couldn't seem to come anywhere but here." And he fell to
Title:  sobbing again.
Title:  
Title:     Injun Joe repeated his statement, just as calmly, a few minutes afterward
Title:  on the inquest, under oath; and the boys, seeing that the lightnings were
