Title:  still withheld, were confirmed in their belief that Joe had sold himself to
Title:  the devil. He was now become, to them, the most balefully interesting object
Title:  they had ever looked upon, and they could not take their fascinated eyes
Title:  from his face.
Title:  
Title:     They inwardly resolved to watch him nights, when opportunity should
Title:  offer, in the hope of getting a glimpse of his dread master.
Title:  
Title:     Injun Joe helped to raise the body of the murdered man and put it in a
Title:  wagon for removal; and it was whispered through the shuddering crowd that
Title:  the wound bled a little! The boys thought that this happy circumstance would
Title:  turn suspicion in the right direction; but they were disappointed, for more
Title:  than one villager remarked:
Title:  
Title:     "It was within three feet of Muff Potter when it done it."
Title:  
Title:     Tom's fearful secret and gnawing conscience disturbed his sleep for as
Title:  much as a week after this; and at breakfast one morning Sid said:
Title:  
Title:     "Tom, you pitch around and talk in your sleep so much that you keep me
Title:  awake half the time."
Title:  
Title:     Tom blanched and dropped his eyes.
Title:  
Title:     "It's a bad sign," said Aunt Polly, gravely. "What you got on your mind,
Title:  Tom?"
Title:  
Title:     "Nothing. Nothing 't I know of." But the boy's hand shook so that he
Title:  spilled his coffee.
Title:  
Title:     "And you do talk such stuff," Sid said. "Last night you said, 'It's
Title:  blood, it's blood, that's what it is!' You said that over and over. And you
Title:  said, 'Don't torment me so -- I'll tell!' Tell what? What is it you'll
Title:  tell?"
Title:  
Title:     Everything was swimming before Tom. There is no telling what might have
Title:  happened, now, but luckily the concern passed out of Aunt Polly's face and
Title:  she came to Tom's relief without knowing it. She said:
Title:  
Title:     "Sho! It's that dreadful murder. I dream about it most every night
Title:  myself. Sometimes I dream it's me that done it."
Title:  
Title:     Mary said she had been affected much the same way. Sid seemed satisfied.
Title:  Tom got out of the presence as quick as he plausibly could, and after that
Title:  he complained of toothache for a week, and tied up his jaws every night. He
Title:  never knew that Sid lay
Title:  nightly watching, and frequently slipped the bandage free and then leaned on
Title:  his elbow listening a good while at a time, and afterward slipped the
Title:  bandage back to its place again. Tom's distress of mind wore off gradually
Title:  and the toothache grew irksome and was discarded. If Sid really managed to
Title:  make anything out of Tom's disjointed mutterings, he kept it to himself.
Title:  
Title:     It seemed to Tom that his schoolmates never would get done holding
Title:  inquests on dead cats, and thus keeping his trouble present to his mind. Sid
Title:  noticed that Tom never was coroner at one of these inquiries, though it had
Title:  been his habit to take the lead in all new enterprises; he noticed, too,
Title:  that Tom never acted as a witness -- and that was strange; and Sid did not
Title:  overlook the fact that Tom even showed a marked aversion to these inquests,
Title:  and always avoided them when he could. Sid marvelled, but said nothing.
Title:  However, even inquests went out of vogue at last, and ceased to torture
Title:  Tom's conscience.
Title:  
Title:     Every day or two, during this time of sorrow, Tom watched his opportunity
Title:  and went to the little grated jail-window and smuggled such small comforts
Title:  through to the "murderer" as he could get hold of. The jail was a trifling
Title:  little brick den that stood in a marsh at the edge of the village, and no
Title:  guards were afforded for it; indeed, it was seldom occupied. These offerings
Title:  greatly helped to ease Tom's conscience.
Title:  
Title:     The villagers had a strong desire to tar-and-feather
Title:  Injun Joe and ride him on a rail, for body-snatching, but so formidable was
Title:  his character that nobody could be found who was willing to take the lead in
Title:  the matter, so it was dropped. He had been careful to begin both of his
Title:  inquest-statements with the fight, without confessing the grave-robbery that
Title:  preceded it; therefore it was deemed wisest not to try the case in the
Title:  courts at present.
Title:  
Title:    ------------------------------------------------------------------------
Title:  
Title:                                   Chapter XII
Title:  
Title:     ONE of the reasons why Tom's mind had drifted away from its secret
Title:  troubles was, that it had found a new and weighty matter to interest itself
Title:  about. Becky Thatcher had stopped coming to school. Tom had struggled with
Title:  his pride a few days, and tried to "whistle her down the wind," but failed.
Title:  He began to find himself hanging around her father's house, nights, and
Title:  feeling very miserable. She was ill. What if she should die! There was
Title:  distraction in the thought. He no longer took an interest in war, nor even
Title:  in piracy. The charm of life was gone; there was nothing but dreariness
Title:  left. He put his hoop away, and his bat; there was no joy in them any more.
Title:  His aunt was concerned. She began to try all manner of remedies on him. She
Title:  was one of those people who are infatuated with patent medicines and all
Title:  new-fangled methods of producing health or mending it. She was an inveterate
Title:  experimenter in these things. When something fresh in this line came out she
Title:  was in a fever, right away, to try it; not on herself, for she was never
Title:  ailing, but on anybody else that came handy. She was
Title:  a subscriber for all the "Health" periodicals and phrenological frauds; and
Title:  the solemn ignorance they were inflated with was breath to her nostrils. All
Title:  the "rot" they contained about ventilation, and how to go to bed, and how to
Title:  get up, and what to eat, and what to drink, and how much exercise to take,
Title:  and what frame of mind to keep one's self in, and what sort of clothing to
Title:  wear, was all gospel to her, and she never observed that her health-journals
Title:  of the current month customarily upset everything they had recommended the
Title:  month before. She was as simple-hearted and honest as the day was long, and
Title:  so she was an easy victim. She gathered together her quack periodicals and
Title:  her quack medicines, and thus armed with death, went about on her pale
Title:  horse, metaphorically speaking, with "hell following after." But she never
Title:  suspected that she was not an angel of healing and the balm of Gilead in
Title:  disguise, to the suffering neighbors.
Title:  
Title:     The water treatment was new, now, and Tom's low condition was a windfall
Title:  to her. She had him out at daylight every morning, stood him up in the
Title:  wood-shed and drowned him with a deluge of cold water; then she scrubbed him
Title:  down with a towel like a file, and so brought him to; then she rolled him up
Title:  in a wet sheet and put him away under blankets till she sweated his soul
Title:  clean and "the yellow stains of it came through his pores" -- as Tom said.
Title:  
Title:     Yet notwithstanding all this, the boy grew more and more melancholy and
Title:  pale and dejected. She
Title:  added hot baths, sitz baths, shower baths, and plunges. The boy remained as
Title:  dismal as a hearse. She began to assist the water with a slim oatmeal diet
Title:  and blister-plasters. She calculated his capacity as she would a jug's, and
Title:  filled him up every day with quack cure-alls.
Title:  
Title:     Tom had become indifferent to persecution by this time. This phase filled
Title:  the old lady's heart with consternation. This indifference must be broken up
Title:  at any cost. Now she heard of Pain-killer for the first time. She ordered a
Title:  lot at once. She tasted it and was filled with gratitude. It was simply fire
Title:  in a liquid form. She dropped the water treatment and everything else, and
Title:  pinned her faith to Pain-killer. She gave Tom a teaspoonful and watched with
Title:  the deepest anxiety for the result. Her troubles were instantly at rest, her
Title:  soul at peace again; for the "indifference" was broken up. The boy could not
Title:  have shown a wilder, heartier interest, if she had built a fire under him.
Title:  
Title:     Tom felt that it was time to wake up; this sort of life might be romantic
Title:  enough, in his blighted condition, but it was getting to have too little
Title:  sentiment and too much distracting variety about it. So he thought over
Title:  various plans for relief, and finally hit pon that of professing to be fond
Title:  of Pain-killer. He asked for it so often that he became a nuisance, and his
Title:  aunt ended by telling him to help himself and quit bothering her. If it had
Title:  been Sid, she would have had no misgivings to alloy her delight;
Title:  but since it was Tom, she watched the bottle clandestinely. She found that
Title:  the medicine did really diminish, but it did not occur to her that the boy
Title:  was mending the health of a crack in the sitting-room floor with it.
Title:  
Title:     One day Tom was in the act of dosing the crack when his aunt's yellow cat
Title:  came along, purring, eying the teaspoon avariciously, and begging for a
Title:  taste. Tom said:
Title:  
Title:     "Don't ask for it unless you want it, Peter."
Title:  
Title:     But Peter signified that he did want it.
Title:  
Title:     "You better make sure."
Title:  
Title:     Peter was sure.
Title:  
Title:     "Now you've asked for it, and I'll give it to you, because there ain't
Title:  anything mean about me; but if you find you don't like it, you mustn't blame
Title:  anybody but your own self."
Title:  
Title:     Peter was agreeable. So Tom pried his mouth open and poured down the
Title:  Pain-killer. Peter sprang a couple of yards in the air, and then delivered a
Title:  war-whoop and set off round and round the room, banging against furniture,
Title:  upsetting flower-pots, and making general havoc. Next he rose on his hind
Title:  feet and pranced around, in a frenzy of enjoyment, with his head over his
Title:  shoulder and his voice proclaiming his unappeasable happiness. Then he went
Title:  tearing around the house again spreading chaos and destruction in his path.
Title:  Aunt Polly entered in time to see him throw a few double summersets, deliver
Title:  a final mighty hurrah, and sail through the open
Title:  window, carrying the rest of the flower-pots with him. The old lady stood
Title:  petrified with astonishment, peering over her glasses; Tom lay on the floor
Title:  expiring with laughter.
Title:  
Title:     "Tom, what on earth ails that cat?"
Title:  
Title:     "I don't know, aunt," gasped the boy.
Title:  
Title:     "Why, I never see anything like it. What did make him act so?"
Title:  
Title:     "Deed I don't know, Aunt Polly; cats always act so when they're having a
Title:  good time."
Title:  
Title:     "They do, do they?" There was something in the tone that made Tom
Title:  apprehensive.
Title:  
Title:     "Yes'm. That is, I believe they do."
Title:  
Title:     "You do?"
Title:  
Title:     "Yes'm."
Title:  
Title:     The old lady was bending down, Tom watching, with interest emphasized by
Title:  anxiety. Too late he divined her "drift." The handle of the telltale
Title:  teaspoon was visible under the bed-valance. Aunt Polly took it, held it up.
Title:  Tom winced, and dropped his eyes. Aunt Polly raised him by the usual handle
Title:  -- his ear -- and cracked his head soundly with her thimble.
Title:  
Title:     "Now, sir, what did you want to treat that poor dumb beast so, for?"
Title:  
Title:     "I done it out of pity for him -- because he hadn't any aunt."
Title:  
Title:     "Hadn't any aunt! -- you numskull. What has that got to do with it?"
Title:  
Title:     "Heaps. Because if he'd had one she'd a burnt
Title:  him out herself! She'd a roasted his bowels out of him 'thout any more
Title:  feeling than if he was a human!"
Title:  
Title:     Aunt Polly felt a sudden pang of remorse. This was putting the thing in a
Title:  new light; what was cruelty to a cat might be cruelty to a boy, too. She
Title:  began to soften; she felt sorry. Her eyes watered a little, and she put her
Title:  hand on Tom's head and said gently:
Title:  
Title:     "I was meaning for the best, Tom. And, Tom, it did do you good."
Title:  
Title:     Tom looked up in her face with just a perceptible twinkle peeping through
Title:  his gravity.
Title:  
Title:     "I know you was meaning for the best, aunty, and so was I with Peter. It
Title:  done him good, too. I never see him get around so since -- "
Title:  
Title:     "Oh, go 'long with you, Tom, before you aggravate me again. And you try
Title:  and see if you can't be a good boy, for once, and you needn't take any more
Title:  medicine."
Title:  
Title:     Tom reached school ahead of time. It was noticed that this strange thing
Title:  had been occurring every day latterly. And now, as usual of late, he hung
Title:  about the gate of the schoolyard instead of playing with his comrades. He
Title:  was sick, he said, and he looked it. He tried to seem to be looking
Title:  everywhere but whither he really was looking -- down the road. Presently
Title:  Jeff Thatcher hove in sight, and Tom's face lighted; he gazed a moment, and
Title:  then turned sorrowfully away. When Jeff arrived, Tom accosted him; and "led
Title:  up" warily to opportunities for remark
Title:  about Becky, but the giddy lad never could see the bait. Tom watched and
Title:  watched, hoping whenever a frisking frock came in sight, and hating the
Title:  owner of it as soon as he saw she was not the right one. At last frocks
Title:  ceased to appear, and he dropped hopelessly into the dumps; he entered the
Title:  empty schoolhouse and sat down to suffer. Then one more frock passed in at
Title:  the gate, and Tom's heart gave a great bound. The next instant he was out,
Title:  and "going on" like an Indian; yelling, laughing, chasing boys, jumping over
Title:  the fence at risk of life and limb, throwing handsprings, standing on his
Title:  head -- doing all the heroic things he could conceive of, and keeping a
Title:  furtive eye out, all the while, to see if Becky Thatcher was noticing. But
Title:  she seemed to be unconscious of it all; she never looked. Could it be
Title:  possible that she was not aware that he was there? He carried his exploits
Title:  to her immediate vicinity; came war-whooping around, snatched a boy's cap,
Title:  hurled it to the roof of the schoolhouse, broke through a group of boys,
Title:  tumbling them in every direction, and fell sprawling, himself, under Becky's
Title:  nose, almost upsetting her -- and she turned, with her nose in the air, and
Title:  he heard her say: "Mf! some people think they're mighty smart -- always
Title:  showing off!"
Title:  
Title:     Tom's cheeks burned. He gathered himself up and sneaked off, crushed and
Title:  crestfallen.
Title:  
Title:    ------------------------------------------------------------------------
Title:  
Title:                                  Chapter XIII
Title:  
Title:     TOM'S mind was made up now. He was gloomy and desperate. He was a
Title:  forsaken, friendless boy, he said; nobody loved him; when they found out
Title:  what they had driven him to, perhaps they would be sorry; he had tried to do
Title:  right and get along, but they would not let him; since nothing would do them
Title:  but to be rid of him, let it be so; and let them blame him for the
Title:  consequences -- why shouldn't they? What right had the friendless to
Title:  complain? Yes, they had forced him to it at last: he would lead a life of
Title:  crime. There was no choice.
Title:  
Title:     By this time he was far down Meadow Lane, and the bell for school to
Title:  "take up" tinkled faintly upon his ear. He sobbed, now, to think he should
Title:  never, never hear that old familiar sound any more -- it was very hard, but
Title:  it was forced on him; since he was driven out into the cold world, he must
Title:  submit -- but he forgave them. Then the sobs came thick and fast.
Title:  
Title:     Just at this point he met his soul's sworn comrade, Joe Harper --
Title:  hard-eyed, and with evidently a great and dismal purpose in his heart.
Title:  Plainly here were
Title:  "two souls with but a single thought." Tom, wiping his eyes with his sleeve,
Title:  began to blubber out something about a resolution to escape from hard usage
Title:  and lack of sympathy at home by roaming abroad into the great world never to
Title:  return; and ended by hoping that Joe would not forget him.
Title:  
Title:     But it transpired that this was a request which Joe had just been going
Title:  to make of Tom, and had come to hunt him up for that purpose. His mother had
Title:  whipped him for drinking some cream which he had never tasted and knew
Title:  nothing about; it was plain that she was tired of him and wished him to go;
Title:  if she felt that way, there was nothing for him to do but succumb; he hoped
Title:  she would be happy, and never regret having driven her poor boy out into the
Title:  unfeeling world to suffer and die.
Title:  
Title:     As the two boys walked sorrowing along, they made a new compact to stand
Title:  by each other and be brothers and never separate till death relieved them of
Title:  their troubles. Then they began to lay their plans. Joe was for being a
Title:  hermit, and living on crusts in a remote cave, and dying, some time, of cold
Title:  and want and grief; but after listening to Tom, he conceded that there were
Title:  some conspicuous advantages about a life of crime, and so he consented to be
Title:  a pirate.
Title:  
Title:     Three miles below St. Petersburg, at a point where the Mississippi River
Title:  was a trifle over a mile wide, there was a long, narrow, wooded island, with
Title:  a shallow bar at the head of it, and this offered well
Title:  as a rendezvous. It was not inhabited; it lay far over toward the further
Title:  shore, abreast a dense and almost wholly unpeopled forest. So Jackson's
Title:  Island was chosen. Who were to be the subjects of their piracies was a
Title:  matter that did not occur to them. Then they hunted up Huckleberry Finn, and
Title:  he joined them promptly, for all careers were one to him; he was
Title:  indifferent. They presently separated to meet at a lonely spot on the
Title:  river-bank two miles above the village at the favorite hour -- which was
Title:  midnight. There was a small log raft there which they meant to capture. Each
Title:  would bring hooks and lines, and such provision as he could steal in the
Title:  most dark and mysterious way -- as became outlaws. And before the afternoon
Title:  was done, they had all managed to enjoy the sweet glory of spreading the
Title:  fact that pretty soon the town would "hear something." All who got this
Title:  vague hint were cautioned to "be mum and wait."
Title:  
Title:     About midnight Tom arrived with a boiled ham and a few trifles, and
Title:  stopped in a dense undergrowth on a small bluff overlooking the
Title:  meeting-place. It was starlight, and very still. The mighty river lay like
Title:  an ocean at rest. Tom listened a moment, but no sound disturbed the quiet.
Title:  Then he gave a low, distinct whistle. It was answered from under the bluff.
Title:  Tom whistled twice more; these signals were answered in the same way. Then a
Title:  guarded voice said:
Title:  
Title:     "Who goes there?"
Title:  
Title:     "Tom Sawyer, the Black Avenger of the Spanish Main. Name your names."
Title:  
Title:     "Huck Finn the Red-Handed, and Joe Harper the Terror of the Seas." Tom
Title:  had furnished these titles, from his favorite literature.
Title:  
Title:     "'Tis well. Give the countersign."
Title:  
Title:     Two hoarse whispers delivered the same awful word simultaneously to the
Title:  brooding night:
Title:  
Title:     "BLOOD!"
Title:  
Title:     Then Tom tumbled his ham over the bluff and let himself down after it,
Title:  tearing both skin and clothes to some extent in the effort. There was an
Title:  easy, comfortable path along the shore under the bluff, but it lacked the
Title:  advantages of difficulty and danger so valued by a pirate.
Title:  
Title:     The Terror of the Seas had brought a side of bacon, and had about worn
Title:  himself out with getting it there. Finn the Red-Handed had stolen a skillet
Title:  and a quantity of half-cured leaf tobacco, and had also brought a few
Title:  corn-cobs to make pipes with. But none of the pirates smoked or "chewed" but
Title:  himself. The Black Avenger of the Spanish Main said it would never do to
Title:  start without some fire. That was a wise thought; matches were hardly known
Title:  there in that day. They saw a fire smouldering upon a great raft a hundred
Title:  yards above, and they went stealthily thither and helped themselves to a
Title:  chunk. They made an imposing adventure of it, saying, "Hist!" every now and
Title:  then, and suddenly halting with finger on lip; moving with hands on
Title:  imaginary dagger-hilts; and giving orders in dismal whispers that if "the
Title:  foe" stirred, to "let him have it to the hilt," because "dead men tell no
Title:  tales." They knew well enough that the raftsmen were all down at the village
Title:  laying in stores or having a spree, but still that was no excuse for their
Title:  conducting this thing in an unpiratical way.
Title:  
Title:     They shoved off, presently, Tom in command, Huck at the after oar and Joe
Title:  at the forward. Tom stood amidships, gloomy-browed, and with folded arms,
Title:  and gave his orders in a low, stern whisper:
Title:  
Title:     "Luff, and bring her to the wind!"
Title:  
Title:     "Aye-aye, sir!"
Title:  
Title:     "Steady, steady-y-y-y!"
Title:  
Title:     "Steady it is, sir!"
Title:  
Title:     "Let her go off a point!"
Title:  
Title:     "Point it is, sir!"
Title:  
Title:     As the boys steadily and monotonously drove the raft toward mid-stream it
Title:  was no doubt understood that these orders were given only for "style," and
Title:  were not intended to mean anything in particular.
Title:  
Title:     "What sail's she carrying?"
Title:  
Title:     "Courses, tops'ls, and flying-jib, sir."
Title:  
Title:     "Send the r'yals up! Lay out aloft, there, half a dozen of ye --
Title:  foretopmaststuns'l! Lively, now!"
Title:  
Title:     "Aye-aye, sir!"
Title:  
Title:     "Shake out that maintogalans'l! Sheets and braces! Now my hearties!"
Title:  
Title:     "Aye-aye, sir!"
Title:  
Title:     "Hellum-a-lee -- hard a port! Stand by to meet
Title:  her when she comes! Port, port! Now, men! With a will! Stead-y-y-y!"
Title:  
Title:     "Steady it is, sir!"
Title:  
Title:     The raft drew beyond the middle of the river; the boys pointed her head
Title:  right, and then lay on their oars. The river was not high, so there was not
Title:  more than a two or three mile current. Hardly a word was said during the
Title:  next three-quarters of an hour. Now the raft was passing before the distant
Title:  town. Two or three glimmering lights showed where it lay, peacefully
Title:  sleeping, beyond the vague vast sweep of star-gemmed water, unconscious of
Title:  the tremendous event that was happening. The Black Avenger stood still with
Title:  folded arms, "looking his last" upon the scene of his former joys and his
Title:  later sufferings, and wishing "she" could see him now, abroad on the wild
Title:  sea, facing peril and death with dauntless heart, going to his doom with a
Title:  grim smile on his lips. It was but a small strain on his imagination to
Title:  remove Jackson's Island beyond eye-shot of the village, and so he "looked
Title:  his last" with a broken and satisfied heart. The other pirates were looking
Title:  their last, too; and they all looked so long that they came near letting the
Title:  current drift them out of the range of the island. But they discovered the
Title:  danger in time, and made shift to avert it. About two o'clock in the morning
Title:  the raft grounded on the bar two hundred yards above the head of the island,
Title:  and they waded back and forth until they had landed their freight. Part of
Title:  the little
Title:  raft's belongings consisted of an old sail, and this they spread over a nook
Title:  in the bushes for a tent to shelter their provisions; but they themselves
Title:  would sleep in the open air in good weather, as became outlaws.
Title:  
Title:     They built a fire against the side of a great log twenty or thirty steps
Title:  within the sombre depths of the forest, and then cooked some bacon in the
Title:  frying-pan for supper, and used up half of the corn "pone" stock they had
Title:  brought. It seemed glorious sport to be feasting in that wild, free way in
Title:  the virgin forest of an unexplored and uninhabited island, far from the
Title:  haunts of men, and they said they never would return to civilization. The
Title:  climbing fire lit up their faces and threw its ruddy glare upon the pillared
Title:  tree-trunks of their forest temple, and upon the varnished foliage and
Title:  festooning vines.
Title:  
Title:     When the last crisp slice of bacon was gone, and the last allowance of
Title:  corn pone devoured, the boys stretched themselves out on the grass, filled
Title:  with contentment. They could have found a cooler place, but they would not
Title:  deny themselves such a romantic feature as the roasting camp-fire.
Title:  
Title:     "AIN'T it gay?" said Joe.
Title:  
Title:     "It's NUTS!" said Tom. "What would the boys say if they could see us?"
Title:  
Title:     "Say? Well, they'd just die to be here -- hey, Hucky!"
Title:  
Title:     "I reckon so," said Huckleberry; "anyways,
Title:  I'm suited. I don't want nothing better'n this. I don't ever get enough to
Title:  eat, gen'ally -- and here they can't come and pick at a feller and bullyrag
Title:  him so."
Title:  
Title:     "It's just the life for me," said Tom. "You don't have to get up,
Title:  mornings, and you don't have to go to school, and wash, and all that blame
Title:  foolishness. You see a pirate don't have to do anything, Joe, when he's
Title:  ashore, but a hermit he has to be praying considerable, and then he don't
Title:  have any fun, anyway, all by himself that way."
Title:  
Title:     "Oh yes, that's so," said Joe, "but I hadn't thought much about it, you
Title:  know. I'd a good deal rather be a pirate, now that I've tried it."
Title:  
Title:     "You see," said Tom, "people don't go much on hermits, nowadays, like
Title:  they used to in old times, but a pirate's always respected. And a hermit's
Title:  got to sleep on the hardest place he can find, and put sackcloth and ashes
Title:  on his head, and stand out in the rain, and -- "
Title:  
Title:     "What does he put sackcloth and ashes on his head for?" inquired Huck.
Title:  
Title:     " I dono. But they've got to do it. Hermits always do. You'd have to do
Title:  that if you was a hermit."
Title:  
Title:     "Dern'd if I would," said Huck.
Title:  
Title:     "Well, what would you do?"
Title:  
Title:     "I dono. But I wouldn't do that."
Title:  
Title:     "Why, Huck, you'd have to. How'd you get around it?"
Title:  
Title:     "Why, I just wouldn't stand it. I'd run away."
Title:  
Title:     "Run away! Well, you would be a nice old slouch of a hermit. You'd be a
Title:  disgrace."
Title:  
Title:     The Red-Handed made no response, being better employed. He had finished
Title:  gouging out a cob, and now he fitted a weed stem to it, loaded it with
Title:  tobacco, and was pressing a coal to the charge and blowing a cloud of
Title:  fragrant smoke -- he was in the full bloom of luxurious contentment. The
Title:  other pirates envied him this majestic vice, and secretly resolved to
Title:  acquire it shortly. Presently Huck said:
Title:  
Title:     "What does pirates have to do?"
Title:  
Title:     Tom said:
Title:  
Title:     "Oh, they have just a bully time -- take ships and burn them, and get the
Title:  money and bury it in awful places in their island where there's ghosts and
Title:  things to watch it, and kill everybody in the ships -- make 'em walk a
Title:  plank."
Title:  
Title:     "And they carry the women to the island," said Joe; "they don't kill the
Title:  women."
Title:  
Title:     "No," assented Tom, "they don't kill the women -- they're too noble. And
Title:  the women's always beautiful, too.
Title:  
Title:     "And don't they wear the bulliest clothes! Oh no! All gold and silver and
Title:  di'monds," said Joe, with enthusiasm.
Title:  
Title:     "Who?" said Huck.
Title:  
Title:     "Why, the pirates."
Title:  
Title:     Huck scanned his own clothing forlornly.
Title:  
Title:     "I reckon I ain't dressed fitten for a pirate," said
Title:  he, with a regretful pathos in his voice; "but I ain't got none but these."
Title:  
Title:     But the other boys told him the fine clothes would come fast enough,
Title:  after they should have begun their adventures. They made him understand that
Title:  his poor rags would do to begin with, though it was customary for wealthy
Title:  pirates to start with a proper wardrobe.
Title:  
Title:     Gradually their talk died out and drowsiness began to steal upon the
Title:  eyelids of the little waifs. The pipe dropped from the fingers of the
Title:  Red-Handed, and he slept the sleep of the conscience-free and the weary. The
Title:  Terror of the Seas and the Black Avenger of the Spanish Main had more
Title:  difficulty in getting to sleep. They said their prayers inwardly, and lying
Title:  down, since there was nobody there with authority to make them kneel and
Title:  recite aloud; in truth, they had a mind not to say them at all, but they
Title:  were afraid to proceed to such lengths as that, lest they might call down a
Title:  sudden and special thunderbolt from heaven. Then at once they reached and
Title:  hovered upon the imminent verge of sleep -- but an intruder came, now, that
Title:  would not "down." It was conscience. They began to feel a vague fear that
Title:  they had been doing wrong to run away; and next they thought of the stolen
Title:  meat, and then the real torture came. They tried to argue it away by
Title:  reminding conscience that they had purloined sweetmeats and apples scores of
Title:  times; but conscience was not to be appeased by such thin
Title:  plausibilities; it seemed to them, in the end, that there was no getting
Title:  around the stubborn fact that taking sweetmeats was only "hooking," while
Title:  taking bacon and hams and such valuables was plain simple stealing -- and
Title:  there was a command against that in the Bible. So they inwardly resolved
Title:  that so long as they remained in the business, their piracies should not
Title:  again be sullied with the crime of stealing. Then conscience granted a
Title:  truce, and these curiously inconsistent pirates fell peacefully to sleep.
Title:  
Title:    ------------------------------------------------------------------------
Title:  
Title:                                   Chapter XIV
Title:  
Title:     WHEN Tom awoke in the morning, he wondered where he was. He sat up and
Title:  rubbed his eyes and looked around. Then he comprehended. It was the cool
Title:  gray dawn, and there was a delicious sense of repose and peace in the deep
Title:  pervading calm and silence of the woods. Not a leaf stirred; not a sound
Title:  obtruded upon great Nature's meditation. Beaded dewdrops stood upon the
Title:  leaves and grasses. A white layer of ashes covered the fire, and a thin blue
Title:  breath of smoke rose straight into the air. Joe and Huck still slept.
Title:  
Title:     Now, far away in the woods a bird called; another answered; presently the
Title:  hammering of a woodpecker was heard. Gradually the cool dim gray of the
Title:  morning whitened, and as gradually sounds multiplied and life manifested
Title:  itself. The marvel of Nature shaking off sleep and going to work unfolded
Title:  itself to the musing boy. A little green worm came crawling over a dewy
Title:  leaf, lifting two-thirds of his body into the air from time to time and
Title:  "sniffing around," then proceeding again -- for he was measuring, Tom said;
Title:  and when the worm approached
Title:  him, of its own accord, he sat as still as a stone, with his hopes rising
Title:  and falling, by turns, as the creature still came toward him or seemed
Title:  inclined to go elsewhere; and when at last it considered a painful moment
Title:  with its curved body in the air and then came decisively down upon Tom's leg
Title:  and began a journey over him, his whole heart was glad -- for that meant
Title:  that he was going to have a new suit of clothes -- without the shadow of a
Title:  doubt a gaudy piratical uniform. Now a procession of ants appeared, from
Title:  nowhere in particular, and went about their labors; one struggled manfully
Title:  by with a dead spider five times as big as itself in its arms, and lugged it
Title:  straight up a tree-trunk. A brown spotted lady-bug climbed the dizzy height
Title:  of a grass blade, and Tom bent down close to it and said, "Lady-bug,
Title:  lady-bug, fly away home, your house is on fire, your children's alone," and
Title:  she took wing and went off to see about it -- which did not surprise the
Title:  boy, for he knew of old that this insect was credulous about conflagrations,
Title:  and he had practised upon its simplicity more than once. A tumblebug came
Title:  next, heaving sturdily at its ball, and Tom touched the creature, to see it
Title:  shut its legs against its body and pretend to be dead. The birds were fairly
Title:  rioting by this time. A catbird, the Northern mocker, lit in a tree over
Title:  Tom's head, and trilled out her imitations of her neighbors in a rapture of
Title:  enjoyment; then a shrill jay swept down, a flash of blue flame, and stopped
Title:  on a twig almost within the boy's
Title:  reach, cocked his head to one side and eyed the strangers with a consuming
Title:  curiosity; a gray squirrel and a big fellow of the "fox" kind came skurrying
Title:  along, sitting up at intervals to inspect and chatter at the boys, for the
Title:  wild things had probably never seen a human being before and scarcely knew
Title:  whether to be afraid or not. All Nature was wide awake and stirring, now;
Title:  long lances of sunlight pierced down through the dense foliage far and near,
Title:  and a few butterflies came fluttering upon the scene.
Title:  
Title:     Tom stirred up the other pirates and they all clattered away with a
Title:  shout, and in a minute or two were stripped and chasing after and tumbling
Title:  over each other in the shallow limpid water of the white sandbar. They felt
Title:  no longing for the little village sleeping in the distance beyond the
Title:  majestic waste of water. A vagrant current or a slight rise in the river had
Title:  carried off their raft, but this only gratified them, since its going was
Title:  something like burning the bridge between them and civilization.
Title:  
Title:     They came back to camp wonderfully refreshed, glad-hearted, and ravenous;
Title:  and they soon had the camp-fire blazing up again. Huck found a spring of
Title:  clear cold water close by, and the boys made cups of broad oak or hickory
Title:  leaves, and felt that water, sweetened with such a wildwood charm as that,
Title:  would be a good enough substitute for coffee. While Joe was slicing bacon
Title:  for breakfast, Tom and Huck asked him to hold on a minute; they stepped to a
Title:  promising nook in the river-bank and threw in their
Title:  lines; almost immediately they had reward. Joe had not had time to get
Title:  impatient before they were back again with some handsome bass, a couple of
Title:  sun-perch and a small catfish -- provisions enough for quite a family. They
Title:  fried the fish with the bacon, and were astonished; for no fish had ever
Title:  seemed so delicious before. They did not know that the quicker a fresh-water
Title:  fish is on the fire after he is caught the better he is; and they reflected
Title:  little upon what a sauce open-air sleeping, open-air exercise, bathing, and
Title:  a large ingredient of hunger make, too.
Title:  
Title:     They lay around in the shade, after breakfast, while Huck had a smoke,
Title:  and then went off through the woods on an exploring expedition. They tramped
Title:  gayly along, over decaying logs, through tangled underbrush, among solemn
Title:  monarchs of the forest, hung from their crowns to the ground with a drooping
Title:  regalia of grape-vines. Now and then they came upon snug nooks carpeted with
Title:  grass and jeweled with flowers.
Title:  
Title:     They found plenty of things to be delighted with, but nothing to be
Title:  astonished at. They discovered that the island was about three miles long
Title:  and a quarter of a mile wide, and that the shore it lay closest to was only
Title:  separated from it by a narrow channel hardly two hundred yards wide. They
Title:  took a swim about every hour, so it was close upon the middle of the
Title:  afternoon when they got back to camp. They were too hungry to stop to fish,
Title:  but they fared sumptuously upon cold ham, and then threw themselves down in the
Title:  shade to talk. But the talk soon began to drag, and then died. The
Title:  stillness, the solemnity that brooded in the woods, and the sense of
Title:  loneliness, began to tell upon the spirits of the boys. They fell to
Title:  thinking. A sort of undefined longing crept upon them. This took dim shape,
Title:  presently -- it was budding homesickness. Even Finn the Red-Handed was
Title:  dreaming of his doorsteps and empty hogsheads. But they were all ashamed of
Title:  their weakness, and none was brave enough to speak his thought.
Title:  
Title:     For some time, now, the boys had been dully conscious of a peculiar sound
Title:  in the distance, just as one sometimes is of the ticking of a clock which he
Title:  takes no distinct note of. But now this mysterious sound became more
Title:  pronounced, and forced a recognition. The boys started, glanced at each
Title:  other, and then each assumed a listening attitude. There was a long silence,
Title:  profound and unbroken; then a deep, sullen boom came floating down out of
Title:  the distance.
Title:  
Title:     "What is it!" exclaimed Joe, under his breath.
Title:  
Title:     "I wonder," said Tom in a whisper.
Title:  
Title:     "'Tain't thunder," said Huckleberry, in an awed tone, "becuz thunder -- "
Title:  
Title:     "Hark!" said Tom. "Listen -- don't talk."
Title:  
Title:     They waited a time that seemed an age, and then the same muffled boom
Title:  troubled the solemn hush.
Title:  
Title:     "Let's go and see."
Title:  
Title:     They sprang to their feet and hurried to the shore toward the town. They
Title:  parted the bushes on the bank and peered out over the water. The little
Title:  steam ferry-boat was about a mile below the village, drifting with the
Title:  current. Her broad deck seemed crowded with people. There were a great many
Title:  skiffs rowing about or floating with the stream in the neighborhood of the
Title:  ferryboat, but the boys could not determine what the men in them were doing.
Title:  Presently a great jet of white smoke burst from the ferryboat's side, and as
Title:  it expanded and rose in a lazy cloud, that same dull throb of sound was
Title:  borne to the listeners again.
Title:  
Title:     "I know now!" exclaimed Tom; "somebody's drownded!"
Title:  
Title:     "That's it!" said Huck; "they done that last summer, when Bill Turner got
Title:  drownded; they shoot a cannon over the water, and that makes him come up to
Title:  the top. Yes, and they take loaves of bread and put quicksilver in 'em and
Title:  set 'em afloat, and wherever there's anybody that's drownded, they'll float
Title:  right there and stop."
Title:  
Title:     "Yes, I've heard about that," said Joe. "I wonder what makes the bread do
Title:  that."
Title:  
Title:     "Oh, it ain't the bread, so much," said Tom; "I reckon it's mostly what
Title:  they SAY over it before they start it out."
Title:  
Title:     "But they don't say anything over it," said Huck. "I've seen 'em and they
Title:  don't."
Title:  
Title:     "Well, that's funny," said Tom. "But maybe
Title:  they say it to themselves. Of course they do. Anybody might know that."
Title:  
Title:     The other boys agreed that there was reason in what Tom said, because an
Title:  ignorant lump of bread, uninstructed by an incantation, could not be
Title:  expected to act very intelligently when set upon an errand of such gravity.
Title:  
Title:     "By jings, I wish I was over there, now," said Joe.
Title:  
Title:     "I do too" said Huck "I'd give heaps to know who it is."
Title:  
Title:     The boys still listened and watched. Presently a revealing thought
Title:  flashed through Tom's mind, and he exclaimed:
Title:  
Title:     "Boys, I know who's drownded -- it's us!"
Title:  
Title:     They felt like heroes in an instant. Here was a gorgeous triumph; they
Title:  were missed; they were mourned; hearts were breaking on their account; tears
Title:  were being shed; accusing memories of unkindness to these poor lost lads
Title:  were rising up, and unavailing regrets and remorse were being indulged; and
Title:  best of all, the departed were the talk of the whole town, and the envy of
Title:  all the boys, as far as this dazzling notoriety was concerned. This was
Title:  fine. It was worth while to be a pirate, after all.
Title:  
Title:     As twilight drew on, the ferryboat went back to her accustomed business
Title:  and the skiffs disappeared. The pirates returned to camp. They were jubilant
Title:  with vanity over their new grandeur and the illustrious trouble they were
Title:  making. They caught fish,
Title:  cooked supper and ate it, and then fell to guessing at what the village was
Title:  thinking and saying about them; and the pictures they drew of the public
Title:  distress on their account were gratifying to look upon -- from their point
Title:  of view. But when the shadows of night closed them in, they gradually ceased
Title:  to talk, and sat gazing into the fire, with their minds evidently wandering
Title:  elsewhere. The excitement was gone, now, and Tom and Joe could not keep back
Title:  thoughts of certain persons at home who were not enjoying this fine frolic
Title:  as much as they were. Misgivings came; they grew troubled and unhappy; a
Title:  sigh or two escaped, unawares. By and by Joe timidly ventured upon a
Title:  roundabout "feeler" as to how the others might look upon a return to
Title:  civilization -- not right now, but --
Title:  
Title:     Tom withered him with derision! Huck, being uncommitted as yet, joined in
Title:  with Tom, and the waverer quickly "explained," and was glad to get out of
Title:  the scrape with as little taint of chicken-hearted home-sickness clinging to
Title:  his garments as he could. Mutiny was effectually laid to rest for the
Title:  moment.
Title:  
Title:     As the night deepened, Huck began to nod, and presently to snore. Joe
Title:  followed next. Tom lay upon his elbow motionless, for some time, watching
Title:  the two intently. At last he got up cautiously, on his knees, and went
Title:  searching among the grass and the flickering reflections flung by the
Title:  camp-fire. He picked up and inspected several large semi-cylinders
Title:  of the thin white bark of a sycamore, and finally chose two which seemed to
Title:  suit him. Then he knelt by the fire and painfully wrote something upon each
Title:  of these with his "red keel"; one he rolled up and put in his jacket pocket,
Title:  and the other he put in Joe's hat and removed it to a little distance from
Title:  the owner. And he also put into the hat certain schoolboy treasures of
Title:  almost inestimable value -- among them a lump of chalk, an India-rubber
Title:  ball, three fishhooks, and one of that kind of marbles known as a "sure
Title:  'nough crystal." Then he tiptoed his way cautiously among the trees till he
Title:  felt that he was out of hearing, and straightway broke into a keen run in
Title:  the direction of the sandbar.
Title:  
Title:    ------------------------------------------------------------------------
Title:  
Title:                                   Chapter XV
Title:  
Title:     A FEW minutes later Tom was in the shoal water of the bar, wading toward
Title:  the Illinois shore. Before the depth reached his middle he was half-way
Title:  over; the current would permit no more wading, now, so he struck out
Title:  confidently to swim the remaining hundred yards. He swam quartering
Title:  upstream, but still was swept downward rather faster than he had expected.
Title:  However, he reached the shore finally, and drifted along till he found a low
Title:  place and drew himself out. He put his hand on his jacket pocket, found his
Title:  piece of bark safe, and then struck through the woods, following the shore,
Title:  with streaming garments. Shortly before ten o'clock he came out into an open
Title:  place opposite the village, and saw the ferryboat lying in the shadow of the
Title:  trees and the high bank. Everything was quiet under the blinking stars. He
Title:  crept down the bank, watching with all his eyes, slipped into the water,
Title:  swam three or four strokes and climbed into the skiff that did "yawl" duty
Title:  at the boat's stern. He laid himself down under the thwarts and waited,
Title:  panting.
Title:  
Title:     Presently the cracked bell tapped and a voice gave the order to "cast
Title:  off." A minute or two later the skiff's head was standing high up, against
Title:  the boat's swell, and the voyage was begun. Tom felt happy in his success,
Title:  for he knew it was the boat's last trip for the night. At the end of a long
Title:  twelve or fifteen minutes the wheels stopped, and Tom slipped overboard and
Title:  swam ashore in the dusk, landing fifty yards downstream, out of danger of
Title:  possible stragglers.
Title:  
Title:     He flew along unfrequented alleys, and shortly found himself at his
Title:  aunt's back fence. He climbed over, approached the "ell," and looked in at
Title:  the sitting-room window, for a light was burning there. There sat Aunt
Title:  Polly, Sid, Mary, and Joe Harper's mother, grouped together, talking. They
Title:  were by the bed, and the bed was between them and the door. Tom went to the
Title:  door and began to softly lift the latch; then he pressed gently and the door
Title:  yielded a crack; he continued pushing cautiously, and quaking every time it
Title:  creaked, till he judged he might squeeze through on his knees; so he put his
Title:  head through and began, warily.
Title:  
Title:     "What makes the candle blow so?" said Aunt Polly. Tom hurried up. "Why,
Title:  that door's open, I believe. Why, of course it is. No end of strange things
Title:  now. Go 'long and shut it, Sid."
Title:  
Title:     Tom disappeared under the bed just in time. He lay and "breathed" himself
Title:  for a time, and then crept to where he could almost touch his aunt's foot.
Title:  
Title:     "But as I was saying," said Aunt Polly, "he warn't bad, so to say -- only
Title:  mischeevous. Only just giddy, and harum-scarum, you know. He warn't any more
Title:  responsible than a colt. He never meant any harm, and he was the
Title:  best-hearted boy that ever was" -- and she began to cry.
Title:  
Title:     "It was just so with my Joe -- always full of his devilment, and up to
Title:  every kind of mischief, but he was just as unselfish and kind as he could be
Title:  -- and laws bless me, to think I went and whipped him for taking that cream,
Title:  never once recollecting that I throwed it out myself because it was sour,
Title:  and I never to see him again in this world, never, never, never, poor abused
Title:  boy!" And Mrs. Harper sobbed as if her heart would break.
Title:  
Title:     "I hope Tom's better off where he is," said Sid, "but if he'd been better
Title:  in some ways -- "
Title:  
Title:     "Sid !" Tom felt the glare of the old lady's eye, though he could not see
Title:  it. "Not a word against my Tom, now that he's gone! God'll take care of him
Title:  -- never you trouble yourself, sir! Oh, Mrs. Harper, I don't know how to
Title:  give him up! I don't know how to give him up! He was such a comfort to me,
Title:  although he tormented my old heart out of me, 'most."
Title:  
Title:     "The Lord giveth and the Lord hath taken away -- Blessed be the name of
Title:  the Lord! But it's so hard -- Oh, it's so hard! Only last Saturday my Joe
Title:  busted a firecracker right under my nose and I knocked him sprawling. Little
Title:  did I know then,
Title:  how soon -- Oh, if it was to do over again I'd hug him and bless him for
Title:  it."
Title:  
Title:     "Yes, yes, yes, I know just how you feel, Mrs. Harper, I know just
Title:  exactly how you feel. No longer ago than yesterday noon, my Tom took and
Title:  filled the cat full of Pain-killer, and I did think the cretur would tear
Title:  the house down. And God forgive me, I cracked Tom's head with my thimble,
Title:  poor boy, poor dead boy. But he's out of all his troubles now. And the last
Title:  words I ever heard him say was to reproach -- "
Title:  
Title:     But this memory was too much for the old lady, and she broke entirely
Title:  down. Tom was snuffling, now, himself -- and more in pity of himself than
Title:  anybody else. He could hear Mary crying, and putting in a kindly word for
Title:  him from time to time. He began to have a nobler opinion of himself than
Title:  ever before. Still, he was sufficiently touched by his aunt's grief to long
Title:  to rush out from under the bed and overwhelm her with joy -- and the
Title:  theatrical gorgeousness of the thing appealed strongly to his nature, too,
Title:  but he resisted and lay still.
Title:  
Title:     He went on listening, and gathered by odds and ends that it was
Title:  conjectured at first that the boys had got drowned while taking a swim; then
Title:  the small raft had been missed; next, certain boys said the missing lads had
Title:  promised that the village should "hear something" soon; the wise-heads had
Title:  "put this and that together" and decided that the lads had gone off on that
Title:  raft and would turn up at the
Title:  next town below, presently; but toward noon the raft had been found, lodged
Title:  against the Missouri shore some five or six miles below the village -- and
Title:  then hope perished; they must be drowned, else hunger would have driven them
Title:  home by nightfall if not sooner. It was believed that the search for the
Title:  bodies had been a fruitless effort merely because the drowning must have
Title:  occurred in mid-channel, since the boys, being good swimmers, would
Title:  otherwise have escaped to shore. This was Wednesday night. If the bodies
Title:  continued missing until Sunday, all hope would be given over, and the
Title:  funerals would be preached on that morning. Tom shuddered.
Title:  
Title:     Mrs. Harper gave a sobbing good-night and turned to go. Then with a
Title:  mutual impulse the two bereaved women flung themselves into each other's
Title:  arms and had a good, consoling cry, and then parted. Aunt Polly was tender
Title:  far beyond her wont, in her good-night to Sid and Mary. Sid snuffled a bit
Title:  and Mary went off crying with all her heart.
Title:  
Title:     Aunt Polly knelt down and prayed for Tom so touchingly, so appealingly,
Title:  and with such measureless love in her words and her old trembling voice,
Title:  that he was weltering in tears again, long before she was through.
Title:  
Title:     He had to keep still long after she went to bed, for she kept making
Title:  broken-hearted ejaculations from time to time, tossing unrestfully, and
Title:  turning over. But at last she was still, only moaning a
Title:  little in her sleep. Now the boy stole out, rose gradually by the bedside,
Title:  shaded the candle-light with his hand, and stood regarding her. His heart
Title:  was full of pity for her. He took out his sycamore scroll and placed it by
Title:  the candle. But something occurred to him, and he lingered considering. His
Title:  face lighted with a happy solution of his thought; he put the bark hastily
Title:  in his pocket. Then he bent over and kissed the faded lips, and straightway
Title:  made his stealthy exit, latching the door behind him.
Title:  
Title:     He threaded his way back to the ferry landing, found nobody at large
Title:  there, and walked boldly on board the boat, for he knew she was tenantless
Title:  except that there was a watchman, who always turned in and slept like a
Title:  graven image. He untied the skiff at the stern, slipped into it, and was
Title:  soon rowing cautiously upstream. When he had pulled a mile above the
Title:  village, he started quartering across and bent himself stoutly to his work.
Title:  He hit the landing on the other side neatly, for this was a familiar bit of
Title:  work to him. He was moved to capture the skiff, arguing that it might be
Title:  considered a ship and therefore legitimate prey for a pirate, but he knew a
Title:  thorough search would be made for it and that might end in revelations. So
Title:  he stepped ashore and entered the woods.
Title:  
Title:     He sat down and took a long rest, torturing himself meanwhile to keep
Title:  awake, and then started warily down the home-stretch. The night was far
Title:  spent. It was broad daylight before he found himself fairly
Title:  abreast the island bar. He rested again until the sun was well up and
Title:  gilding the great river with its splendor, and then he plunged into the
Title:  stream. A little later he paused, dripping, upon the threshold of the camp,
Title:  and heard Joe say:
Title:  
Title:     "No, Tom's true-blue, Huck, and he'll come back. He won't desert. He
Title:  knows that would be a disgrace to a pirate, and Tom's too proud for that
Title:  sort of thing. He's up to something or other. Now I wonder what?"
Title:  
Title:     "Well, the things is ours, anyway, ain't they?"
Title:  
Title:     "Pretty near, but not yet, Huck. The writing says they are if he ain't
Title:  back here to breakfast."
Title:  
Title:     "Which he is!" exclaimed Tom, with fine dramatic effect, stepping grandly
Title:  into camp.
Title:  
Title:     A sumptuous breakfast of bacon and fish was shortly provided, and as the
Title:  boys set to work upon it, Tom recounted (and adorned) his adventures. They
Title:  were a vain and boastful company of heroes when the tale was done. Then Tom
Title:  hid himself away in a shady nook to sleep till noon, and the other pirates
Title:  got ready to fish and explore.
Title:  
Title:    ------------------------------------------------------------------------
Title:  
Title:                                   Chapter XVI
Title:  
Title:     AFTER dinner all the gang turned out to hunt for turtle eggs on the bar.
Title:  They went about poking sticks into the sand, and when they found a soft
Title:  place they went down on their knees and dug with their hands. Sometimes they
Title:  would take fifty or sixty eggs out of one hole. They were perfectly round
Title:  white things a trifle smaller than an English walnut. They had a famous
Title:  fried-egg feast that night, and another on Friday morning.
Title:  
Title:     After breakfast they went whooping and prancing out on the bar, and
Title:  chased each other round and round, shedding clothes as they went, until they
Title:  were naked, and then continued the frolic far away up the shoal water of the
Title:  bar, against the stiff current, which latter tripped their legs from under
Title:  them from time to time and greatly increased the fun. And now and then they
Title:  stooped in a group and splashed water in each other's faces with their
Title:  palms, gradually approaching each other, with averted faces to avoid the
Title:  strangling sprays, and finally gripping and struggling till the best man
Title:  ducked his neighbor, and then they all went under
Title:  in a tangle of white legs and arms and came up blowing, sputtering,
Title:  laughing, and gasping for breath at one and the same time.
Title:  
Title:     When they were well exhausted, they would run out and sprawl on the dry,
Title:  hot sand, and lie there and cover themselves up with it, and by and by break
Title:  for the water again and go through the original performance once more.
Title:  Finally it occurred to them that their naked skin represented flesh-colored
Title:  "tights" very fairly; so they drew a ring in the sand and had a circus --
Title:  with three clowns in it, for none would yield this proudest post to his
Title:  neighbor.
Title:  
Title:     Next they got their marbles and played "knucks" and "ring-taw" and
Title:  "keeps" till that amusement grew stale. Then Joe and Huck had another swim,
Title:  but Tom would not venture, because he found that in kicking off his trousers
Title:  he had kicked his string of rattlesnake rattles off his ankle, and he
Title:  wondered how he had escaped cramp so long without the protection of this
Title:  mysterious charm. He did not venture again until he had found it, and by
Title:  that time the other boys were tired and ready to rest. They gradually
Title:  wandered apart, dropped into the "dumps," and fell to gazing longingly
Title:  across the wide river to where the village lay drowsing in the sun. Tom
Title:  found himself writing "BECKY" in the sand with his big toe; he scratched it
Title:  out, and was angry with himself for his weakness. But he wrote it again,
Title:  nevertheless; he could not help it. He erased it once more and then took
Title:  himself out of
Title:  temptation by driving the other boys together and joining them.
Title:  
Title:     But Joe's spirits had gone down almost beyond resurrection. He was so
Title:  homesick that he could hardly endure the misery of it. The tears lay very
Title:  near the surface. Huck was melancholy, too. Tom was down-hearted, but tried
Title:  hard not to show it. He had a secret which he was not ready to tell, yet,
Title:  but if this mutinous depression was not broken up soon, he would have to
Title:  bring it out. He said, with a great show of cheerfulness:
Title:  
Title:     "I bet there's been pirates on this island before, boys. We'll explore it
Title:  again. They've hid treasures here somewhere. How'd you feel to light on a
Title:  rotten chest full of gold and silver -- hey?"
Title:  
Title:     But it roused only faint enthusiasm, which faded out, with no reply. Tom
Title:  tried one or two other seductions; but they failed, too. It was discouraging
Title:  work. Joe sat poking up the sand with a stick and looking very gloomy.
Title:  Finally he said:
Title:  
Title:     "Oh, boys, let's give it up. I want to go home. It's so lonesome."
Title:  
Title:     "Oh no, Joe, you'll feel better by and by," said Tom. "Just think of the
Title:  fishing that's here."
Title:  
Title:     "I don't care for fishing. I want to go home."
Title:  
Title:     "But, Joe, there ain't such another swimming-place anywhere."
Title:  
Title:     "Swimming's no good. I don't seem to care for it, somehow, when there
Title:  ain't anybody to say I sha'n't go in. I mean to go home."
Title:  
Title:     "Oh, shucks! Baby! You want to see your mother, I reckon."
Title:  
Title:     "Yes, I do want to see my mother -- and you would, too, if you had one. I
Title:  ain't any more baby than you are." And Joe snuffled a little.
Title:  
Title:     "Well, we'll let the cry-baby go home to his mother, won't we, Huck? Poor
Title:  thing -- does it want to see its mother? And so it shall. You like it here,
Title:  don't you, Huck? We'll stay, won't we?"
Title:  
Title:     Huck said, "Y-e-s" -- without any heart in it.
Title:  
Title:     "I'll never speak to you again as long as I live," said Joe, rising.
Title:  "There now!" And he moved moodily away and began to dress himself.
Title:  
Title:     "Who cares!" said Tom. "Nobody wants you to. Go 'long home and get
Title:  laughed at. Oh, you're a nice pirate. Huck and me ain't cry-babies. We'll
Title:  stay, won't we, Huck? Let him go if he wants to. I reckon we can get along
Title:  without him, per'aps."
Title:  
Title:     But Tom was uneasy, nevertheless, and was alarmed to see Joe go sullenly
Title:  on with his dressing. And then it was discomforting to see Huck eying Joe's
Title:  preparations so wistfully, and keeping up such an ominous silence.
Title:  Presently, without a parting word, Joe began to wade off toward the Illinois
Title:  shore. Tom's heart began to sink. He glanced at Huck. Huck could not bear
Title:  the look, and dropped his eyes. Then he said:
Title:  
Title:     "I want to go, too, Tom. It was getting so lonesome anyway, and now it'll
Title:  be worse. Let's us go, too, Tom."
Title:  
Title:     "I won't! You can all go, if you want to. I mean to stay."
Title:  
Title:     "Tom, I better go."
Title:  
Title:     "Well, go 'long -- who's hendering you."
Title:  
Title:     Huck began to pick up his scattered clothes. He said:
Title:  
Title:     "Tom, I wisht you'd come, too. Now you think it over. We'll wait for you
Title:  when we get to shore."
Title:  
Title:     "Well, you'll wait a blame long time, that's all."
Title:  
Title:     Huck started sorrowfully away, and Tom stood looking after him, with a
Title:  strong desire tugging at his heart to yield his pride and go along too. He
Title:  hoped the boys would stop, but they still waded slowly on. It suddenly
Title:  dawned on Tom that it was become very lonely and still. He made one final
Title:  struggle with his pride, and then darted after his comrades, yelling:
Title:  
Title:     "Wait! Wait! I want to tell you something!"
Title:  
Title:     They presently stopped and turned around. When he got to where they were,
Title:  he began unfolding his secret, and they listened moodily till at last they
Title:  saw the "point" he was driving at, and then they set up a war-whoop of
Title:  applause and said it was "splendid!" and said if he had told them at first,
Title:  they wouldn't have started away. He made a plausible excuse; but his real
Title:  reason had been the fear that not even the secret would keep them with him
Title:  any very great length of time, and so he had meant to hold it in reserve as
Title:  a last seduction.
Title:  
Title:     The lads came gayly back and went at their sports
Title:  again with a will, chattering all the time about Tom's stupendous plan and
Title:  admiring the genius of it. After a dainty egg and fish dinner, Tom said he
Title:  wanted to learn to smoke, now. Joe caught at the idea and said he would like
Title:  to try, too. So Huck made pipes and filled them. These novices had never
Title:  smoked anything before but cigars made of grape-vine, and they "bit" the
Title:  tongue, and were not considered manly anyway.
Title:  
Title:     Now they stretched themselves out on their elbows and began to puff,
Title:  charily, and with slender confidence. The smoke had an unpleasant taste, and
Title:  they gagged a little, but Tom said:
Title:  
Title:     "Why, it's just as easy! If I'd a knowed this was all, I'd a learnt long
Title:  ago."
Title:  
Title:     "So would I," said Joe. "It's just nothing."
Title:  
Title:     "Why, many a time I've looked at people smoking, and thought well I wish
Title:  I could do that; but I never thought I could," said Tom.
Title:  
Title:     "That's just the way with me, hain't it, Huck? You've heard me talk just
Title:  that way -- haven't you, Huck? I'll leave it to Huck if I haven't."
Title:  
Title:     "Yes -- heaps of times," said Huck.
Title:  
Title:     "Well, I have too," said Tom; "oh, hundreds of times. Once down by the
Title:  slaughter-house. Don't you remember, Huck? Bob Tanner was there, and Johnny
Title:  Miller, and Jeff Thatcher, when I said it. Don't you remember, Huck, 'bout
Title:  me saying that?"
Title:  
Title:     "Yes, that's so," said Huck. "That was the
Title:  day after I lost a white alley. No, 'twas the day before."
Title:  
Title:     "There -- I told you so," said Tom. "Huck recollects it."
Title:  
Title:     "I bleeve I could smoke this pipe all day," said Joe. "I don't feel
Title:  sick."
Title:  
Title:     "Neither do I," said Tom. " I could smoke it all day. But I bet you Jeff
Title:  Thatcher couldn't."
Title:  
Title:     "Jeff Thatcher! Why, he'd keel over just with two draws. Just let him try
Title:  it once. He'd see!"
Title:  
Title:     "I bet he would. And Johnny Miller -- I wish could see Johnny Miller
Title:  tackle it once."
Title:  
Title:     "Oh, don't I!" said Joe. "Why, I bet you Johnny Miller couldn't any more
Title:  do this than nothing. Just one little snifter would fetch him ."
Title:  
Title:     "'Deed it would, Joe. Say -- I wish the boys could see us now."
Title:  
Title:     "So do I."
Title:  
Title:     "Say -- boys, don't say anything about it, and some time when they're
Title:  around, I'll come up to you and say, 'Joe, got a pipe? I want a smoke.' And
Title:  you'll say, kind of careless like, as if it warn't anything, you'll say,
Title:  'Yes, I got my old pipe, and another one, but my tobacker ain't very good.'
Title:  And I'll say, 'Oh, that's all right, if it's strong enough.' And then you'll
Title:  out with the pipes, and we'll light up just as ca'm, and then just see 'em
Title:  look!"
Title:  
Title:     "By jings, that'll be gay, Tom! I wish it was now!"
Title:  
Title:     "So do I! And when we tell 'em we learned when we was off pirating, won't
Title:  they wish they'd been along?"
Title:  
Title:     "Oh, I reckon not! I'll just bet they will!"
Title:  
Title:     So the talk ran on. But presently it began to flag a trifle, and grow
Title:  disjointed. The silences widened; the expectoration marvellously increased.
Title:  Every pore inside the boys' cheeks became a spouting fountain; they could
Title:  scarcely bail out the cellars under their tongues fast enough to prevent an
Title:  inundation; little overflowings down their throats occurred in spite of all
Title:  they could do, and sudden retchings followed every time. Both boys were
Title:  looking very pale and miserable, now. Joe's pipe dropped from his nerveless
Title:  fingers. Tom's followed. Both fountains were going furiously and both pumps
Title:  bailing with might and main. Joe said feebly:
Title:  
Title:     "I've lost my knife. I reckon I better go and find it."
Title:  
Title:     Tom said, with quivering lips and halting utterance:
Title:  
Title:     "I'll help you. You go over that way and I'll hunt around by the spring.
Title:  No, you needn't come, Huck -- we can find it."
Title:  
Title:     So Huck sat down again, and waited an hour. Then he found it lonesome,
Title:  and went to find his comrades. They were wide apart in the woods, both very
Title:  pale, both fast asleep. But something informed him that if they had had any
Title:  trouble they had got rid of it.
Title:  
Title:     They were not talkative at supper that night.
Title:  They had a humble look, and when Huck prepared his pipe after the meal and
Title:  was going to prepare theirs, they said no, they were not feeling very well
Title:  -- something they ate at dinner had disagreed with them.
Title:  
Title:     About midnight Joe awoke, and called the boys. There was a brooding
Title:  oppressiveness in the air that seemed to bode something. The boys huddled
Title:  themselves together and sought the friendly companionship of the fire,
Title:  though the dull dead heat of the breathless atmosphere was stifling. They
Title:  sat still, intent and waiting. The solemn hush continued. Beyond the light
Title:  of the fire everything was swallowed up in the blackness of darkness.
Title:  Presently there came a quivering glow that vaguely revealed the foliage for
Title:  a moment and then vanished. By and by another came, a little stronger. Then
Title:  another. Then a faint moan came sighing through the branches of the forest
Title:  and the boys felt a fleeting breath upon their cheeks, and shuddered with
Title:  the fancy that the Spirit of the Night had gone by. There was a pause. Now a
Title:  weird flash turned night into day and showed every little grass-blade,
Title:  separate and distinct, that grew about their feet. And it showed three
Title:  white, startled faces, too. A deep peal of thunder went rolling and tumbling
Title:  down the heavens and lost itself in sullen rumblings in the distance. A
Title:  sweep of chilly air passed by, rustling all the leaves and snowing the flaky
Title:  ashes broadcast about the fire. Another fierce glare lit up the forest and
Title:  an instant crash followed that seemed to rend
Title:  the tree-tops right over the boys' heads. They clung together in terror, in
Title:  the thick gloom that followed. A few big rain-drops fell pattering upon the
Title:  leaves.
Title:  
Title:     "Quick! boys, go for the tent!" exclaimed Tom.
Title:  
Title:     They sprang away, stumbling over roots and among vines in the dark, no
Title:  two plunging in the same direction. A furious blast roared through the
Title:  trees, making everything sing as it went. One blinding flash after another
Title:  came, and peal on peal of deafening thunder. And now a drenching rain poured
Title:  down and the rising hurricane drove it in sheets along the ground. The boys
Title:  cried out to each other, but the roaring wind and the booming thunder-blasts
Title:  drowned their voices utterly. However, one by one they straggled in at last
Title:  and took shelter under the tent, cold, scared, and streaming with water; but
Title:  to have company in misery seemed something to be grateful for. They could
Title:  not talk, the old sail flapped so furiously, even if the other noises would
Title:  have allowed them. The tempest rose higher and higher, and presently the
Title:  sail tore loose from its fastenings and went winging away on the blast. The
Title:  boys seized each others' hands and fled, with many tumblings and bruises, to
Title:  the shelter of a great oak that stood upon the river-bank. Now the battle
Title:  was at its highest. Under the ceaseless conflagration of lightning that
Title:  flamed in the skies, everything below stood out in clean-cut and shadowless
Title:  distinctness: the bending trees, the billowy
Title:  river, white with foam, the driving spray of spume-flakes, the dim outlines
Title:  of the high bluffs on the other side, glimpsed through the drifting
Title:  cloud-rack and the slanting veil of rain. Every little while some giant tree
Title:  yielded the fight and fell crashing through the younger growth; and the
Title:  unflagging thunder-peals came now in ear-splitting explosive bursts, keen
Title:  and sharp, and unspeakably appalling. The storm culminated in one matchless
Title:  effort that seemed likely to tear the island to pieces, burn it up, drown it
Title:  to the tree-tops, blow it away, and deafen every creature in it, all at one
Title:  and the same moment. It was a wild night for homeless young heads to be out
Title:  in.
Title:  
Title:     But at last the battle was done, and the forces retired with weaker and
Title:  weaker threatenings and grumblings, and peace resumed her sway. The boys
Title:  went back to camp, a good deal awed; but they found there was still
Title:  something to be thankful for, because the great sycamore, the shelter of
Title:  their beds, was a ruin, now, blasted by the lightnings, and they were not
Title:  under it when the catastrophe happened.
Title:  
Title:     Everything in camp was drenched, the camp-fire as well; for they were but
Title:  heedless lads, like their generation, and had made no provision against
Title:  rain. Here was matter for dismay, for they were soaked through and chilled.
Title:  They were eloquent in their distress; but they presently discovered that the
Title:  fire had eaten so far up under the great log it had been
Title:  built against (where it curved upward and separated itself from the ground),
Title:  that a handbreadth or so of it had escaped wetting; so they patiently
Title:  wrought until, with shreds and bark gathered from the under sides of
Title:  sheltered logs, they coaxed the fire to burn again. Then they piled on great
Title:  dead boughs till they had a roaring furnace, and were glad-hearted once
Title:  more. They dried their boiled ham and had a feast, and after that they sat
Title:  by the fire and expanded and glorified their midnight adventure until
Title:  morning, for there was not a dry spot to sleep on, anywhere around.
Title:  
Title:     As the sun began to steal in upon the boys, drowsiness came over them,
Title:  and they went out on the sandbar and lay down to sleep. They got scorched
Title:  out by and by, and drearily set about getting breakfast. After the meal they
Title:  felt rusty, and stiff-jointed, and a little home-sick once more. Tom saw the
Title:  signs, and fell to cheering up the pirates as well as he could. But they
Title:  cared nothing for marbles, or circus, or swimming, or anything. He reminded
Title:  them of the imposing secret, and raised a ray of cheer. While it lasted, he
Title:  got them interested in a new device. This was to knock off being pirates,
Title:  for a while, and be Indians for a change. They were attracted by this idea;
Title:  so it was not long before they were stripped, and striped from head to heel
Title:  with black mud, like so many zebras -- all of them chiefs, of course -- and
Title:  then they went tearing through the woods to attack an English settlement.
Title:  
Title:     By and by they separated into three hostile tribes, and darted upon each
Title:  other from ambush with dreadful war-whoops, and killed and scalped each
Title:  other by thousands. It was a gory day. Consequently it was an extremely
Title:  satisfactory one.
Title:  
Title:     They assembled in camp toward supper-time, hungry and happy; but now a
Title:  difficulty arose -- hostile Indians could not break the bread of hospitality
Title:  together without first making peace, and this was a simple impossibility
Title:  without smoking a pipe of peace. There was no other process that ever they
Title:  had heard of. Two of the savages almost wished they had remained pirates.
Title:  However, there was no other way; so with such show of cheerfulness as they
Title:  could muster they called for the pipe and took their whiff as it passed, in
Title:  due form.
Title:  
Title:     And behold, they were glad they had gone into savagery, for they had
Title:  gained something; they found that they could now smoke a little without
Title:  having to go and hunt for a lost knife; they did not get sick enough to be
Title:  seriously uncomfortable. They were not likely to fool away this high promise
Title:  for lack of effort. No, they practised cautiously, after supper, with right
Title:  fair success, and so they spent a jubilant evening. They were prouder and
Title:  happier in their new acquirement than they would have been in the scalping
Title:  and skinning of the Six Nations. We will leave them to smoke and chatter and
Title:  brag, since we have no further use for them at present.
Title:  
Title:    ------------------------------------------------------------------------
Title:  
Title:                                  Chapter XVII
Title:  
Title:     BUT there was no hilarity in the little town that same tranquil Saturday
Title:  afternoon. The Harpers, and Aunt Polly's family, were being put into
Title:  mourning, with great grief and many tears. An unusual quiet possessed the
Title:  village, although it was ordinarily quiet enough, in all conscience. The
Title:  villagers conducted their concerns with an absent air, and talked little;
Title:  but they sighed often. The Saturday holiday seemed a burden to the children.
Title:  They had no heart in their sports, and gradually gave them up.
Title:  
Title:     In the afternoon Becky Thatcher found herself moping about the deserted
Title:  schoolhouse yard, and feeling very melancholy. But she found nothing there
Title:  to comfort her. She soliloquized:
Title:  
Title:     "Oh, if I only had a brass andiron-knob again! But I haven't got anything
Title:  now to remember him by." And she choked back a little sob.
Title:  
Title:     Presently she stopped, and said to herself:
Title:  
Title:     "It was right here. Oh, if it was to do over again, I wouldn't say that
Title:  -- I wouldn't say it for the whole world. But he's gone now; I'll never,
Title:  never, never see him any more."
Title:  
Title:     This thought broke her down, and she wandered away, with tears rolling
Title:  down her cheeks. Then quite a group of boys and girls -- playmates of Tom's
Title:  and Joe's -- came by, and stood looking over the paling fence and talking in
Title:  reverent tones of how Tom did so-and-so the last time they saw him, and how
Title:  Joe said this and that small trifle (pregnant with awful prophecy, as they
Title:  could easily see now!) -- and each speaker pointed out the exact spot where
Title:  the lost lads stood at the time, and then added something like "and I was
Title:  a-standing just so -- just as I am now, and as if you was him -- I was as
Title:  close as that -- and he smiled, just this way -- and then something seemed
Title:  to go all over me, like -- awful, you know -- and I never thought what it
Title:  meant, of course, but I can see now!"
Title:  
Title:     Then there was a dispute about who saw the dead boys last in life, and
Title:  many claimed that dismal distinction, and offered evidences, more or less
Title:  tampered with by the witness; and when it was ultimately decided who DID see
Title:  the departed last, and exchanged the last words with them, the lucky parties
Title:  took upon themselves a sort of sacred importance, and were gaped at and
Title:  envied by all the rest. One poor chap, who had no other grandeur to offer,
Title:  said with tolerably manifest pride in the remembrance:
Title:  
Title:     "Well, Tom Sawyer he licked me once."
Title:  
Title:     But that bid for glory was a failure. Most of the boys could say that,
Title:  and so that cheapened the
Title:  distinction too much. The group loitered away, still recalling memories of
Title:  the lost heroes, in awed voices.
Title:  
Title:     When the Sunday-school hour was finished, the next morning, the bell
Title:  began to toll, instead of ringing in the usual way. It was a very still
Title:  Sabbath, and the mournful sound seemed in keeping with the musing hush that
Title:  lay upon nature. The villagers began to gather, loitering a moment in the
Title:  vestibule to converse in whispers about the sad event. But there was no
