Title:  whispering in the house; only the funereal rustling of dresses as the women
Title:  gathered to their seats disturbed the silence there. None could remember
Title:  when the little church had been so full before. There was finally a waiting
Title:  pause, an expectant dumbness, and then Aunt Polly entered, followed by Sid
Title:  and Mary, and they by the Harper family, all in deep black, and the whole
Title:  congregation, the old minister as well, rose reverently and stood until the
Title:  mourners were seated in the front pew. There was another communing silence,
Title:  broken at intervals by muffled sobs, and then the minister spread his hands
Title:  abroad and prayed. A moving hymn was sung, and the text followed: "I am the
Title:  Resurrection and the Life."
Title:  
Title:     As the service proceeded, the clergyman drew such pictures of the graces,
Title:  the winning ways, and the rare promise of the lost lads that every soul
Title:  there, thinking he recognized these pictures, felt a pang in remembering
Title:  that he had persistently blinded
Title:  himself to them always before, and had as persistently seen only faults and
Title:  flaws in the poor boys. The minister related many a touching incident in the
Title:  lives of the departed, too, which illustrated their sweet, generous natures,
Title:  and the people could easily see, now, how noble and beautiful those episodes
Title:  were, and remembered with grief that at the time they occurred they had
Title:  seemed rank rascalities, well deserving of the cowhide. The congregation
Title:  became more and more moved, as the pathetic tale went on, till at last the
Title:  whole company broke down and joined the weeping mourners in a chorus of
Title:  anguished sobs, the preacher himself giving way to his feelings, and crying
Title:  in the pulpit.
Title:  
Title:     There was a rustle in the gallery, which nobody noticed; a moment later
Title:  the church door creaked; the minister raised his streaming eyes above his
Title:  handkerchief, and stood transfixed! First one and then another pair of eyes
Title:  followed the minister's, and then almost with one impulse the congregation
Title:  rose and stared while the three dead boys came marching up the aisle, Tom in
Title:  the lead, Joe next, and Huck, a ruin of drooping rags, sneaking sheepishly
Title:  in the rear! They had been hid in the unused gallery listening to their own
Title:  funeral sermon!
Title:  
Title:     Aunt Polly, Mary, and the Harpers threw themselves upon their restored
Title:  ones, smothered them with kisses and poured out thanksgivings, while poor
Title:  Huck stood abashed and uncomfortable, not knowing exactly what to do or
Title:  where to hide from so many
Title:  unwelcoming eyes. He wavered, and started to slink away, but Tom seized him
Title:  and said:
Title:  
Title:     "Aunt Polly, it ain't fair. Somebody's got to be glad to see Huck."
Title:  
Title:     "And so they shall. I'm glad to see him, poor motherless thing!" And the
Title:  loving attentions Aunt Polly lavished upon him were the one thing capable of
Title:  making him more uncomfortable than he was before.
Title:  
Title:     Suddenly the minister shouted at the top of his voice: "Praise God from
Title:  whom all blessings flow -- SING! -- and put your hearts in it!"
Title:  
Title:     And they did. Old Hundred swelled up with a triumphant burst, and while
Title:  it shook the rafters Tom Sawyer the Pirate looked around upon the envying
Title:  juveniles about him and confessed in his heart that this was the proudest
Title:  moment of his life.
Title:  
Title:     As the "sold" congregation trooped out they said they would almost be
Title:  willing to be made ridiculous again to hear Old Hundred sung like that once
Title:  more.
Title:  
Title:     Tom got more cuffs and kisses that day -- according to Aunt Polly's
Title:  varying moods -- than he had earned before in a year; and he hardly knew
Title:  which expressed the most gratefulness to God and affection for himself.
Title:  
Title:    ------------------------------------------------------------------------
Title:  
Title:                                  Chapter XVIII
Title:  
Title:     THAT was Tom's great secret -- the scheme to return home with his brother
Title:  pirates and attend their own funerals. They had paddled over to the Missouri
Title:  shore on a log, at dusk on Saturday, landing five or six miles below the
Title:  village; they had slept in the woods at the edge of the town till nearly
Title:  daylight, and had then crept through back lanes and alleys and finished
Title:  their sleep in the gallery of the church among a chaos of invalided benches.
Title:  
Title:     At breakfast, Monday morning, Aunt Polly and Mary were very loving to
Title:  Tom, and very attentive to his wants. There was an unusual amount of talk.
Title:  In the course of it Aunt Polly said:
Title:  
Title:     "Well, I don't say it wasn't a fine joke, Tom, to keep everybody
Title:  suffering 'most a week so you boys had a good time, but it is a pity you
Title:  could be so hard-hearted as to let me suffer so. If you could come over on a
Title:  log to go to your funeral, you could have come over and give me a hint some
Title:  way that you warn't dead, but only run off."
Title:  
Title:     "Yes, you could have done that, Tom," said Mary; "and I believe you would
Title:  if you had thought of it."
Title:  
Title:     "Would you, Tom?" said Aunt Polly, her face lighting wistfully. "Say, now,
Title:  would you, if you'd thought of it?"
Title:  
Title:     "I -- well, I don't know. 'Twould 'a' spoiled everything."
Title:  
Title:     "Tom, I hoped you loved me that much," said Aunt Polly, with a grieved
Title:  tone that discomforted the boy. "It would have been something if you'd cared
Title:  enough to think of it, even if you didn't do it."
Title:  
Title:     "Now, auntie, that ain't any harm," pleaded Mary; "it's only Tom's giddy
Title:  way -- he is always in such a rush that he never thinks of anything."
Title:  
Title:     "More's the pity. Sid would have thought. And Sid would have come and
Title:  done it, too. Tom, you'll look back, some day, when it's too late, and wish
Title:  you'd cared a little more for me when it would have cost you so little."
Title:  
Title:     "Now, auntie, you know I do care for you," said Tom.
Title:  
Title:     "I'd know it better if you acted more like it."
Title:  
Title:     "I wish now I'd thought," said Tom, with a repentant tone; "but I dreamt
Title:  about you, anyway. That's something, ain't it?"
Title:  
Title:     "It ain't much -- a cat does that much -- but it's better than nothing.
Title:  What did you dream?"
Title:  
Title:     "Why, Wednesday night I dreamt that you was sitting over there by the
Title:  bed, and Sid was sitting by the woodbox, and Mary next to him."
Title:  
Title:     "Well, so we did. So we always do. I'm glad
Title:  your dreams could take even that much trouble about us."
Title:  
Title:     "And I dreamt that Joe Harper's mother was here."
Title:  
Title:     "Why, she was here! Did you dream any more?"
Title:  
Title:     "Oh, lots. But it's so dim, now."
Title:  
Title:     "Well, try to recollect -- can't you?"
Title:  
Title:     "Somehow it seems to me that the wind -- the wind blowed the -- the -- "
Title:  
Title:     "Try harder, Tom! The wind did blow something. Come!"
Title:  
Title:     Tom pressed his fingers on his forehead an anxious minute, and then said:
Title:  
Title:     "I've got it now! I've got it now! It blowed the candle!"
Title:  
Title:     "Mercy on us! Go on, Tom -- go on!"
Title:  
Title:     "And it seems to me that you said, 'Why, I believe that that door -- '"
Title:  
Title:     "Go on, Tom!"
Title:  
Title:     "Just let me study a moment -- just a moment. Oh, yes -- you said you
Title:  believed the door was open."
Title:  
Title:     "As I'm sitting here, I did! Didn't I, Mary! Go on!"
Title:  
Title:     "And then -- and then -- well I won't be certain, but it seems like as if
Title:  you made Sid go and -- and -- "
Title:  
Title:     "Well? Well? What did I make him do, Tom? What did I make him do?"
Title:  
Title:     "You made him -- you -- Oh, you made him shut it."
Title:  
Title:     "Well, for the land's sake! I never heard the beat of that in all my
Title:  days! Don't tell me there ain't anything in dreams, any more. Sereny Harper
Title:  shall know of this before I'm an hour older. I'd like to see her get around
Title:  this with her rubbage 'bout superstition. Go on, Tom!"
Title:  
Title:     "Oh, it's all getting just as bright as day, now. Next you said I warn't
Title:  bad, only mischeevous and harum-scarum, and not any more responsible than --
Title:  than -- I think it was a colt, or something."
Title:  
Title:     "And so it was! Well, goodness gracious! Go on, Tom!"
Title:  
Title:     "And then you began to cry."
Title:  
Title:     "So I did. So I did. Not the first time, neither. And then -- "
Title:  
Title:     "Then Mrs. Harper she began to cry, and said Joe was just the same, and
Title:  she wished she hadn't whipped him for taking cream when she'd throwed it out
Title:  her own self -- "
Title:  
Title:     "Tom! The sperrit was upon you! You was a prophesying -- that's what you
Title:  was doing! Land alive, go on, Tom!"
Title:  
Title:     "Then Sid he said -- he said -- "
Title:  
Title:     "I don't think I said anything," said Sid.
Title:  
Title:     "Yes you did, Sid," said Mary.
Title:  
Title:     "Shut your heads and let Tom go on! What did he say, Tom?"
Title:  
Title:     "He said -- I think he said he hoped I was better off where I was gone
Title:  to, but if I'd been better sometimes -- "
Title:  
Title:     "There, d'you hear that! It was his very words!"
Title:  
Title:     "And you shut him up sharp."
Title:  
Title:     "I lay I did! There must 'a' been an angel there. There was an angel
Title:  there, somewheres!"
Title:  
Title:     "And Mrs. Harper told about Joe scaring her with a firecracker, and you
Title:  told about Peter and the Painkiller -- "
Title:  
Title:     "Just as true as I live!"
Title:  
Title:     "And then there was a whole lot of talk 'bout dragging the river for us,
Title:  and 'bout having the funeral Sunday, and then you and old Miss Harper hugged
Title:  and cried, and she went."
Title:  
Title:     "It happened just so! It happened just so, as sure as I'm a-sitting in
Title:  these very tracks. Tom, you couldn't told it more like if you'd 'a' seen it!
Title:  And then what? Go on, Tom!"
Title:  
Title:     "Then I thought you prayed for me -- and I could see you and hear every
Title:  word you said. And you went to bed, and I was so sorry that I took and wrote
Title:  on a piece of sycamore bark, 'We ain't dead -- we are only off being
Title:  pirates,' and put it on the table by the candle; and then you looked so
Title:  good, laying there asleep, that I thought I went and leaned over and kissed
Title:  you on the lips."
Title:  
Title:     "Did you, Tom, did you! I just forgive you everything for that!" And she
Title:  seized the boy in a crushing embrace that made him feel like the guiltiest
Title:  of villains.
Title:  
Title:     "It was very kind, even though it was only a -- dream," Sid soliloquized
Title:  just audibly.
Title:  
Title:     "Shut up, Sid! A body does just the same in a dream as he'd do if he was
Title:  awake. Here's a big Milum apple I've been saving for you, Tom, if you was
Title:  ever found again -- now go 'long to school. I'm thankful to the good God and
Title:  Father of us all I've got you back, that's long-suffering and merciful to
Title:  them that believe on Him and keep His word, though goodness knows I'm
Title:  unworthy of it, but if only the worthy ones got His blessings and had His
Title:  hand to help them over the rough places, there's few enough would smile here
Title:  or ever enter into His rest when the long night comes. Go 'long Sid, Mary,
Title:  Tom -- take yourselves off -- you've hendered me long enough."
Title:  
Title:     The children left for school, and the old lady to call on Mrs. Harper and
Title:  vanquish her realism with Tom's marvellous dream. Sid had better judgment
Title:  than to utter the thought that was in his mind as he left the house. It was
Title:  this: "Pretty thin -- as long a dream as that, without any mistakes in it!"
Title:  
Title:     What a hero Tom was become, now! He did not go skipping and prancing, but
Title:  moved with a dignified swagger as became a pirate who felt that the public
Title:  eye was on him. And indeed it was; he tried not to seem to see the looks or
Title:  hear the remarks as he passed along, but they were food and drink to him.
Title:  Smaller boys than himself flocked at his heels, as proud to be seen with
Title:  him, and tolerated by him, as
Title:  if he had been the drummer at the head of a procession or the elephant
Title:  leading a menagerie into town. Boys of his own size pretended not to know he
Title:  had been away at all; but they were consuming with envy, nevertheless. They
Title:  would have given anything to have that swarthy suntanned skin of his, and
Title:  his glittering notoriety; and Tom would not have parted with either for a
Title:  circus.
Title:  
Title:     At school the children made so much of him and of Joe, and delivered such
Title:  eloquent admiration from their eyes, that the two heroes were not long in
Title:  becoming insufferably "stuck-up." They began to tell their adventures to
Title:  hungry listeners -- but they only began; it was not a thing likely to have
Title:  an end, with imaginations like theirs to furnish material. And finally, when
Title:  they got out their pipes and went serenely puffing around, the very summit
Title:  of glory was reached.
Title:  
Title:     Tom decided that he could be independent of Becky Thatcher now. Glory was
Title:  sufficient. He would live for glory. Now that he was distinguished, maybe
Title:  she would be wanting to "make up." Well, let her -- she should see that he
Title:  could be as indifferent as some other people. Presently she arrived. Tom
Title:  pretended not to see her. He moved away and joined a group of boys and girls
Title:  and began to talk. Soon he observed that she was tripping gayly back and
Title:  forth with flushed face and dancing eyes, pretending to be busy chasing
Title:  schoolmates, and screaming with laughter when she made a capture;
Title:  but he noticed that she always made her captures in his vicinity, and that
Title:  she seemed to cast a conscious eye in his direction at such times, too. It
Title:  gratified all the vicious vanity that was in him; and so, instead of winning
Title:  him, it only "set him up" the more and made him the more diligent to avoid
Title:  betraying that he knew she was about. Presently she gave over skylarking,
Title:  and moved irresolutely about, sighing once or twice and glancing furtively
Title:  and wistfully toward Tom. Then she observed that now Tom was talking more
Title:  particularly to Amy Lawrence than to any one else. She felt a sharp pang and
Title:  grew disturbed and uneasy at once. She tried to go away, but her feet were
Title:  treacherous, and carried her to the group instead. She said to a girl almost
Title:  at Tom's elbow -- with sham vivacity:
Title:  
Title:     "Why, Mary Austin! you bad girl, why didn't you come to Sunday-school?"
Title:  
Title:     "I did come -- didn't you see me?"
Title:  
Title:     "Why, no! Did you? Where did you sit?"
Title:  
Title:     "I was in Miss Peters' class, where I always go. I saw you."
Title:  
Title:     "Did you? Why, it's funny I didn't see you. I wanted to tell you about
Title:  the picnic."
Title:  
Title:     "Oh, that's jolly. Who's going to give it?"
Title:  
Title:     "My ma's going to let me have one."
Title:  
Title:     "Oh, goody; I hope she'll let me come."
Title:  
Title:     "Well, she will. The picnic's for me. She'll let anybody come that I
Title:  want, and I want you."
Title:  
Title:     "That's ever so nice. When is it going to be?"
Title:  
Title:     "By and by. Maybe about vacation."
Title:  
Title:     "Oh, won't it be fun! You going to have all the girls and boys?"
Title:  
Title:     "Yes, every one that's friends to me -- or wants to be"; and she glanced
Title:  ever so furtively at Tom, but he talked right along to Amy Lawrence about
Title:  the terrible storm on the island, and how the lightning tore the great
Title:  sycamore tree "all to flinders" while he was "standing within three feet of
Title:  it."
Title:  
Title:     "Oh, may I come?" said Grace Miller.
Title:  
Title:     "Yes."
Title:  
Title:     "And me?" said Sally Rogers.
Title:  
Title:     "Yes."
Title:  
Title:     "And me, too?" said Susy Harper. "And Joe?"
Title:  
Title:     "Yes."
Title:  
Title:     And so on, with clapping of joyful hands till all the group had begged
Title:  for invitations but Tom and Amy. Then Tom turned coolly away, still talking,
Title:  and took Amy with him. Becky's lips trembled and the tears came to her eyes;
Title:  she hid these signs with a forced gayety and went on chattering, but the
Title:  life had gone out of the picnic, now, and out of everything else; she got
Title:  away as soon as she could and hid herself and had what her sex call "a good
Title:  cry." Then she sat moody, with wounded pride, till the bell rang. She roused
Title:  up, now, with a vindictive cast in her eye, and gave her plaited tails a
Title:  shake and said she knew what she'd do.
Title:  
Title:     At recess Tom continued his flirtation with Amy with jubilant
Title:  self-satisfaction. And he kept drifting
Title:  about to find Becky and lacerate her with the performance. At last he spied
Title:  her, but there was a sudden falling of his mercury. She was sitting cosily
Title:  on a little bench behind the schoolhouse looking at a picture-book with
Title:  Alfred Temple -- and so absorbed were they, and their heads so close
Title:  together over the book, that they did not seem to be conscious of anything
Title:  in the world besides. Jealousy ran red-hot through Tom's veins. He began to
Title:  hate himself for throwing away the chance Becky had offered for a
Title:  reconciliation. He called himself a fool, and all the hard names he could
Title:  think of. He wanted to cry with vexation. Amy chatted happily along, as they
Title:  walked, for her heart was singing, but Tom's tongue had lost its function.
Title:  He did not hear what Amy was saying, and whenever she paused expectantly he
Title:  could only stammer an awkward assent, which was as often misplaced as
Title:  otherwise. He kept drifting to the rear of the school-house, again and
Title:  again, to sear his eyeballs with the hateful spectacle there. He could not
Title:  help it. And it maddened him to see, as he thought he saw, that Becky
Title:  Thatcher never once suspected that he was even in the land of the living.
Title:  But she did see, nevertheless; and she knew she was winning her fight, too,
Title:  and was glad to see him suffer as she had suffered.
Title:  
Title:     Amy's happy prattle became intolerable. Tom hinted at things he had to
Title:  attend to; things that must be done; and time was fleeting. But in vain
Title:  -- the girl chirped on. Tom thought, "Oh, hang her, ain't I ever going to
Title:  get rid of her?" At last he must be attending to those things -- and she
Title:  said artlessly that she would be "around" when school let out. And he
Title:  hastened away, hating her for it.
Title:  
Title:     "Any other boy!" Tom thought, grating his teeth. "Any boy in the whole
Title:  town but that Saint Louis smarty that thinks he dresses so fine and is
Title:  aristocracy! Oh, all right, I licked you the first day you ever saw this
Title:  town, mister, and I'll lick you again! You just wait till I catch you out!
Title:  I'll just take and -- "
Title:  
Title:     And he went through the motions of thrashing an imaginary boy --
Title:  pummelling the air, and kicking and gouging. "Oh, you do, do you? You holler
Title:  'nough, do you? Now, then, let that learn you!" And so the imaginary
Title:  flogging was finished to his satisfaction.
Title:  
Title:     Tom fled home at noon. His conscience could not endure any more of Amy's
Title:  grateful happiness, and his jealousy could bear no more of the other
Title:  distress. Becky resumed her picture inspections with Alfred, but as the
Title:  minutes dragged along and no Tom came to suffer, her triumph began to cloud
Title:  and she lost interest; gravity and absent-mindedness followed, and then
Title:  melancholy; two or three times she pricked up her ear at a footstep, but it
Title:  was a false hope; no Tom came. At last she grew entirely miserable and
Title:  wished she hadn't carried it so far. When poor Alfred, seeing that he was
Title:  losing her,
Title:  he did not know how, kept exclaiming: "Oh,here's a jolly one! look at this!"
Title:  she lost patience at last, and said, "Oh, don't bother me! I don't care for
Title:  them!" and burst into tears, and got up and walked away.
Title:  
Title:     Alfred dropped alongside and was going to try to comfort her, but she
Title:  said:
Title:  
Title:     "Go away and leave me alone, can't you! I hate you!"
Title:  
Title:     So the boy halted, wondering what he could have done -- for she had said
Title:  she would look at pictures all through the nooning -- and she walked on,
Title:  crying. Then Alfred went musing into the deserted school-house. He was
Title:  humiliated and angry. He easily guessed his way to the truth -- the girl had
Title:  simply made a convenience of him to vent her spite upon Tom Sawyer. He was
Title:  far from hating Tom the less when this thought occurred to him. He wished
Title:  there was some way to get that boy into trouble without much risk to
Title:  himself. Tom's spelling-book fell under his eye. Here was his opportunity.
Title:  He gratefully opened to the lesson for the afternoon and poured ink upon the
Title:  page.
Title:  
Title:     Becky, glancing in at a window behind him at the moment, saw the act, and
Title:  moved on, without discovering herself. She started homeward, now, intending
Title:  to find Tom and tell him; Tom would be thankful and their troubles would be
Title:  healed. Before she was half way home, however, she had changed her mind. The
Title:  thought of Tom's treatment of her
Title:  when she was talking about her picnic came scorching back and filled her
Title:  with shame. She resolved to let him get whipped on the damaged
Title:  spelling-book's account, and to hate him forever, into the bargain.
Title:  
Title:    ------------------------------------------------------------------------
Title:  
Title:                                   Chapter XIX
Title:  
Title:     TOM arrived at home in a dreary mood, and the first thing his aunt said
Title:  to him showed him that he had brought his sorrows to an unpromising market:
Title:  
Title:     "Tom, I've a notion to skin you alive!"
Title:  
Title:     "Auntie, what have I done?"
Title:  
Title:     "Well, you've done enough. Here I go over to Sereny Harper, like an old
Title:  softy, expecting I'm going to make her believe all that rubbage about that
Title:  dream, when lo and behold you she'd found out from Joe that you was over
Title:  here and heard all the talk we had that night. Tom, I don't know what is to
Title:  become of a boy that will act like that. It makes me feel so bad to think
Title:  you could let me go to Sereny Harper and make such a fool of myself and
Title:  never say a word."
Title:  
Title:     This was a new aspect of the thing. His smartness of the morning had
Title:  seemed to Tom a good joke before, and very ingenious. It merely looked mean
Title:  and shabby now. He hung his head and could not think of anything to say for
Title:  a moment. Then he said:
Title:  
Title:     "Auntie, I wish I hadn't done it -- but I didn't think."
Title:  
Title:     "Oh, child, you never think. You never think of anything but your own
Title:  selfishness. You could think to come all the way over here from Jackson's
Title:  Island in the night to laugh at our troubles, and you could think to fool me
Title:  with a lie about a dream; but you couldn't ever think to pity us and save us
Title:  from sorrow."
Title:  
Title:     "Auntie, I know now it was mean, but I didn't mean to be mean. I didn't,
Title:  honest. And besides, I didn't come over here to laugh at you that night."
Title:  
Title:     "What did you come for, then?"
Title:  
Title:     "It was to tell you not to be uneasy about us, because we hadn't got
Title:  drownded."
Title:  
Title:     "Tom, Tom, I would be the thankfullest soul in this world if I could
Title:  believe you ever had as good a thought as that, but you know you never did
Title:  -- and I know it, Tom."
Title:  
Title:     "Indeed and 'deed I did, auntie -- I wish I may never stir if I didn't."
Title:  
Title:     "Oh, Tom, don't lie -- don't do it. It only makes things a hundred times
Title:  worse."
Title:  
Title:     "It ain't a lie, auntie; it's the truth. I wanted to keep you from
Title:  grieving -- that was all that made me come."
Title:  
Title:     "I'd give the whole world to believe that -- it would cover up a power of
Title:  sins, Tom. I'd 'most be glad you'd run off and acted so bad. But it ain't
Title:  reasonable; because, why didn't you tell me, child?"
Title:  
Title:     "Why, you see, when you got to talking about the funeral, I just got all
Title:  full of the idea of our coming and hiding in the church, and I couldn't
Title:  somehow bear to spoil it. So I just put the bark back in my pocket and kept
Title:  mum."
Title:  
Title:     "What bark?"
Title:  
Title:     "The bark I had wrote on to tell you we'd gone pirating. I wish, now,
Title:  you'd waked up when I kissed you -- I do, honest."
Title:  
Title:     The hard lines in his aunt's face relaxed and a sudden tenderness dawned
Title:  in her eyes.
Title:  
Title:     " Did you kiss me, Tom?"
Title:  
Title:     "Why, yes, I did."
Title:  
Title:     "Are you sure you did, Tom?"
Title:  
Title:     "Why, yes, I did, auntie -- certain sure."
Title:  
Title:     "What did you kiss me for, Tom?"
Title:  
Title:     "Because I loved you so, and you laid there moaning and I was so sorry."
Title:  
Title:     The words sounded like truth. The old lady could not hide a tremor in her
Title:  voice when she said:
Title:  
Title:     "Kiss me again, Tom! -- and be off with you to school, now, and don't
Title:  bother me any more."
Title:  
Title:     The moment he was gone, she ran to a closet and got out the ruin of a
Title:  jacket which Tom had gone pirating in. Then she stopped, with it in her
Title:  hand, and said to herself:
Title:  
Title:     "No, I don't dare. Poor boy, I reckon he's lied about it -- but it's a
Title:  blessed, blessed lie, there's such a comfort come from it. I hope the Lord
Title:  -- I know the Lord will forgive him, because it was such
Title:  goodheartedness in him to tell it. But I don't want to find out it's a lie.
Title:  I won't look."
Title:  
Title:     She put the jacket away, and stood by musing a minute. Twice she put out
Title:  her hand to take the garment again, and twice she refrained. Once more she
Title:  ventured, and this time she fortified herself with the thought: "It's a good
Title:  lie -- it's a good lie -- I won't let it grieve me." So she sought the
Title:  jacket pocket. A moment later she was reading Tom's piece of bark through
Title:  flowing tears and saying: "I could forgive the boy, now, if he'd committed a
Title:  million sins!"
Title:  
Title:    ------------------------------------------------------------------------
Title:  
Title:                                   Chapter XX
Title:  
Title:     THERE was something about Aunt Polly's manner, when she kissed Tom, that
Title:  swept away his low spirits and made him light-hearted and happy again. He
Title:  started to school and had the luck of coming upon Becky Thatcher at the head
Title:  of Meadow Lane. His mood always determined his manner. Without a moment's
Title:  hesitation he ran to her and said:
Title:  
Title:     "I acted mighty mean to-day, Becky, and I'm so sorry. I won't ever, ever
Title:  do that way again, as long as ever I live -- please make up, won't you?"
Title:  
Title:     The girl stopped and looked him scornfully in the face:
Title:  
Title:     "I'll thank you to keep yourself to yourself, Mr. Thomas Sawyer. I'll
Title:  never speak to you again."
Title:  
Title:     She tossed her head and passed on. Tom was so stunned that he had not
Title:  even presence of mind enough to say "Who cares, Miss Smarty?" until the
Title:  right time to say it had gone by. So he said nothing. But he was in a fine
Title:  rage, nevertheless. He moped into the schoolyard wishing she were a boy, and
Title:  imagining how he would trounce her if she
Title:  were. He presently encountered her and delivered a stinging remark as he
Title:  passed. She hurled one in return, and the angry breach was complete. It
Title:  seemed to Becky, in her hot resentment, that she could hardly wait for
Title:  school to "take in," she was so impatient to see Tom flogged for the injured
Title:  spelling-book. If she had had any lingering notion of exposing Alfred
Title:  Temple, Tom's offensive fling had driven it entirely away.
Title:  
Title:     Poor girl, she did not know how fast she was nearing trouble herself. The
Title:  master, Mr. Dobbins, had reached middle age with an unsatisfied ambition.
Title:  The darling of his desires was, to be a doctor, but poverty had decreed that
Title:  he should be nothing higher than a village schoolmaster. Every day he took a
Title:  mysterious book out of his desk and absorbed himself in it at times when no
Title:  classes were reciting. He kept that book under lock and key. There was not
Title:  an urchin in school but was perishing to have a glimpse of it, but the
Title:  chance never came. Every boy and girl had a theory about the nature of that
Title:  book; but no two theories were alike, and there was no way of getting at the
Title:  facts in the case. Now, as Becky was passing by the desk, which stood near
Title:  the door, she noticed that the key was in the lock! It was a precious
Title:  moment. She glanced around; found herself alone, and the next instant she
Title:  had the book in her hands. The title-page -- Professor Somebody's ANATOMY --
Title:  carried no information to her mind; so she began to turn the leaves. She
Title:  came at once upon a handsomely engraved and colored frontispiece -- a human
Title:  figure, stark naked. At that moment a shadow fell on the page and Tom Sawyer
Title:  stepped in at the door and caught a glimpse of the picture. Becky snatched
Title:  at the book to close it, and had the hard luck to tear the pictured page
Title:  half down the middle. She thrust the volume into the desk, turned the key,
Title:  and burst out crying with shame and vexation.
Title:  
Title:     "Tom Sawyer, you are just as mean as you can be, to sneak up on a person
Title:  and look at what they're looking at."
Title:  
Title:     "How could I know you was looking at anything?"
Title:  
Title:     "You ought to be ashamed of yourself, Tom Sawyer; you know you're going
Title:  to tell on me, and oh, what shall I do, what shall I do! I'll be whipped,
Title:  and I never was whipped in school."
Title:  
Title:     Then she stamped her little foot and said:
Title:  
Title:     " Be so mean if you want to! I know something that's going to happen. You
Title:  just wait and you'll see! Hateful, hateful, hateful!" -- and she flung out
Title:  of the house with a new explosion of crying.
Title:  
Title:     Tom stood still, rather flustered by this onslaught. Presently he said to
Title:  himself:
Title:  
Title:     "What a curious kind of a fool a girl is! Never been licked in school!
Title:  Shucks! What's a licking! That's just like a girl -- they're so thin-skinned
Title:  and chicken-hearted. Well, of course I ain't going to tell old Dobbins on
Title:  this little fool, because there's
Title:  other ways of getting even on her, that ain't so mean; but what of it? Old
Title:  Dobbins will ask who it was tore his book. Nobody'll answer. Then he'll do
Title:  just the way he always does -- ask first one and then t'other, and when he
Title:  comes to the right girl he'll know it, without any telling. Girls' faces
Title:  always tell on them. They ain't got any backbone. She'll get licked. Well,
Title:  it's a kind of a tight place for Becky Thatcher, because there ain't any way
Title:  out of it." Tom conned the thing a moment longer, and then added: "All
Title:  right, though; she'd like to see me in just such a fix -- let her sweat it
Title:  out!"
Title:  
Title:     Tom joined the mob of skylarking scholars outside. In a few moments the
Title:  master arrived and school "took in." Tom did not feel a strong interest in
Title:  his studies. Every time he stole a glance at the girls' side of the room
Title:  Becky's face troubled him. Considering all things, he did not want to pity
Title:  her, and yet it was all he could do to help it. He could get up no
Title:  exultation that was really worthy the name. Presently the spelling-book
Title:  discovery was made, and Tom's mind was entirely full of his own matters for
Title:  a while after that. Becky roused up from her lethargy of distress and showed
Title:  good interest in the proceedings. She did not expect that Tom could get out
Title:  of his trouble by denying that he spilt the ink on the book himself; and she
Title:  was right. The denial only seemed to make the thing worse for Tom. Becky
Title:  supposed she would be glad of that, and she tried to believe she was glad
Title:  of it, but she found she was not certain. When the worst came to the worst,
Title:  she had an impulse to get up and tell on Alfred Temple, but she made an
Title:  effort and forced herself to keep still -- because, said she to herself,
Title:  "he'll tell about me tearing the picture sure. I wouldn't say a word, not to
Title:  save his life!"
Title:  
Title:     Tom took his whipping and went back to his seat not at all
Title:  broken-hearted, for he thought it was possible that he had unknowingly upset
Title:  the ink on the spelling-book himself, in some skylarking bout -- he had
Title:  denied it for form's sake and because it was custom, and had stuck to the
Title:  denial from principle.
Title:  
Title:     A whole hour drifted by, the master sat nodding in his throne, the air
Title:  was drowsy with the hum of study. By and by, Mr. Dobbins straightened
Title:  himself up, yawned, then unlocked his desk, and reached for his book, but
Title:  seemed undecided whether to take it out or leave it. Most of the pupils
Title:  glanced up languidly, but there were two among them that watched his
Title:  movements with intent eyes. Mr. Dobbins fingered his book absently for a
Title:  while, then took it out and settled himself in his chair to read! Tom shot a
Title:  glance at Becky. He had seen a hunted and helpless rabbit look as she did,
Title:  with a gun levelled at its head. Instantly he forgot his quarrel with her.
Title:  Quick -- something must be done! done in a flash, too! But the very
Title:  imminence of the emergency paralyzed his invention. Good! -- he had an
Title:  inspiration! He would run and snatch the
Title:  book, spring through the door and fly. But his resolution shook for one
Title:  little instant, and the chance was lost -- the master opened the volume. If
Title:  Tom only had the wasted opportunity back again! Too late. There was no help
Title:  for Becky now, he said. The next moment the master faced the school. Every
Title:  eye sank under his gaze. There was that in it which smote even the innocent
Title:  with fear. There was silence while one might count ten -- the master was
Title:  gathering his wrath. Then he spoke: "Who tore this book?"
Title:  
Title:     There was not a sound. One could have heard a pin drop. The stillness
Title:  continued; the master searched face after face for signs of guilt.
Title:  
Title:     "Benjamin Rogers, did you tear this book?"
Title:  
Title:     A denial. Another pause.
Title:  
Title:     "Joseph Harper, did you?"
Title:  
Title:     Another denial. Tom's uneasiness grew more and more intense under the
Title:  slow torture of these proceedings. The master scanned the ranks of boys --
Title:  considered a while, then turned to the girls:
Title:  
Title:     "Amy Lawrence?"
Title:  
Title:     A shake of the head.
Title:  
Title:     "Gracie Miller?"
Title:  
Title:     The same sign.
Title:  
Title:     "Susan Harper, did you do this?"
Title:  
Title:     Another negative. The next girl was Becky Thatcher. Tom was trembling
Title:  from head to foot with excitement and a sense of the hopelessness of the
Title:  situation.
Title:  
Title:     "Rebecca Thatcher" [Tom glanced at her face -- it was white with terror]
Title:  -- "did you tear -- no, look me in the face" [her hands rose in appeal] --
Title:  "did you tear this book?"
Title:  
Title:     A thought shot like lightning through Tom's brain. He sprang to his feet
Title:  and shouted -- " I done it!"
Title:  
Title:     The school stared in perplexity at this incredible folly. Tom stood a
Title:  moment, to gather his dismembered faculties; and when he stepped forward to
Title:  go to his punishment the surprise, the gratitude, the adoration that shone
Title:  upon him out of poor Becky's eyes seemed pay enough for a hundred floggings.
Title:  Inspired by the splendor of his own act, he took without an outcry the most
Title:  merciless flaying that even Mr. Dobbins had ever administered; and also
Title:  received with indifference the added cruelty of a command to remain two
Title:  hours after school should be dismissed -- for he knew who would wait for him
Title:  outside till his captivity was done, and not count the tedious time as loss,
Title:  either.
Title:  
Title:     Tom went to bed that night planning vengeance against Alfred Temple; for
Title:  with shame and repentance Becky had told him all, not forgetting her own
Title:  treachery; but even the longing for vengeance had to give way, soon, to
Title:  pleasanter musings, and he fell asleep at last with Becky's latest words
Title:  lingering dreamily in his ear --
Title:  
Title:     "Tom, how could you be so noble!"
Title:  
Title:    ------------------------------------------------------------------------
Title:  
Title:                                   Chapter XXI
Title:  
Title:     VACATION was approaching. The school-master, always severe, grew severer
Title:  and more exacting than ever, for he wanted the school to make a good showing
Title:  on "Examination" day. His rod and his ferule were seldom idle now -- at
Title:  least among the smaller pupils. Only the biggest boys, and young ladies of
Title:  eighteen and twenty, escaped lashing. Mr. Dobbins' lashings were very
Title:  vigorous ones, too; for although he carried, under his wig, a perfectly bald
Title:  and shiny head, he had only reached middle age, and there was no sign of
Title:  feebleness in his muscle. As the great day approached, all the tyranny that
Title:  was in him came to the surface; he seemed to take a vindictive pleasure in
Title:  punishing the least shortcomings. The consequence was, that the smaller boys
Title:  spent their days in terror and suffering and their nights in plotting
Title:  revenge. They threw away no opportunity to do the master a mischief. But he
Title:  kept ahead all the time. The retribution that followed every vengeful
Title:  success was so sweeping and majestic that the boys always retired from the
Title:  field badly worsted. At last they conspired together
Title:  and hit upon a plan that promised a dazzling victory. They swore in the
Title:  sign-painter's boy, told him the scheme, and asked his help. He had his own
Title:  reasons for being delighted, for the master boarded in his father's family
Title:  and had given the boy ample cause to hate him. The master's wife would go on
Title:  a visit to the country in a few days, and there would be nothing to
Title:  interfere with the plan; the master always prepared himself for great
Title:  occasions by getting pretty well fuddled, and the sign-painter's boy said
Title:  that when the dominie had reached the proper condition on Examination
Title:  Evening he would "manage the thing" while he napped in his chair; then he
Title:  would have him awakened at the right time and hurried away to school.
Title:  
Title:     In the fulness of time the interesting occasion arrived. At eight in the
Title:  evening the schoolhouse was brilliantly lighted, and adorned with wreaths
Title:  and festoons of foliage and flowers. The master sat throned in his great
Title:  chair upon a raised platform, with his blackboard behind him. He was looking
Title:  tolerably mellow. Three rows of benches on each side and six rows in front
Title:  of him were occupied by the dignitaries of the town and by the parents of
Title:  the pupils. To his left, back of the rows of citizens, was a spacious
Title:  temporary platform upon which were seated the scholars who were to take part
Title:  in the exercises of the evening; rows of small boys, washed and dressed to
Title:  an intolerable state of discomfort; rows of gawky big boys; snowbanks of
Title:  girls and young ladies clad in lawn and muslin and conspicuously conscious
Title:  of their bare arms, their grandmothers' ancient trinkets, their bits of pink
Title:  and blue ribbon and the flowers in their hair. All the rest of the house was
Title:  filled with non-participating scholars.
Title:  
Title:     The exercises began. A very little boy stood up and sheepishly recited,
Title:  "You'd scarce expect one of my age to speak in public on the stage," etc. --
Title:  accompanying himself with the painfully exact and spasmodic gestures which a
Title:  machine might have used -- supposing the machine to be a trifle out of
Title:  order. But he got through safely, though cruelly scared, and got a fine
Title:  round of applause when he made his manufactured bow and retired.
Title:  
Title:     A little shamefaced girl lisped, "Mary had a little lamb," etc.,
Title:  performed a compassion-inspiring curtsy, got her meed of applause, and sat
Title:  down flushed and happy.
Title:  
Title:     Tom Sawyer stepped forward with conceited confidence and soared into the
Title:  unquenchable and indestructible "Give me liberty or give me death" speech,
Title:  with fine fury and frantic gesticulation, and broke down in the middle of
Title:  it. A ghastly stage-fright seized him, his legs quaked under him and he was
Title:  like to choke. True, he had the manifest sympathy of the house but he had
Title:  the house's silence, too, which was even worse than its sympathy. The master
Title:  frowned, and this completed the disaster. Tom struggled awhile and then
Title:  retired, utterly
Title:  defeated. There was a weak attempt at applause, but it died early.
Title:  
Title:     "The Boy Stood on the Burning Deck" followed; also "The Assyrian Came
Title:  Down," and other declamatory gems. Then there were reading exercises, and a
Title:  spelling fight. The meagre Latin class recited with honor. The prime feature
Title:  of the evening was in order, now -- original "compositions" by the young
Title:  ladies. Each in her turn stepped forward to the edge of the platform,
Title:  cleared her throat, held up her manuscript (tied with dainty ribbon), and
Title:  proceeded to read, with labored attention to "expression" and punctuation.
Title:  The themes were the same that had been illuminated upon similar occasions by
Title:  their mothers before them, their grandmothers, and doubtless all their
Title:  ancestors in the female line clear back to the Crusades. "Friendship" was
Title:  one; "Memories of Other Days"; "Religion in History"; "Dream Land"; "The
Title:  Advantages of Culture"; "Forms of Political Government Compared and
Title:  Contrasted"; "Melancholy"; "Filial Love"; "Heart Longings," etc., etc.
Title:  
Title:     A prevalent feature in these compositions was a nursed and petted
Title:  melancholy; another was a wasteful and opulent gush of "fine language";
Title:  another was a tendency to lug in by the ears particularly prized words and
Title:  phrases until they were worn entirely out; and a peculiarity that
Title:  conspicuously marked and marred them was the inveterate
Title:  and intolerable sermon that wagged its crippled tail at the end of each and
Title:  every one of them. No matter what the subject might be, a brain-racking
Title:  effort was made to squirm it into some aspect or other that the moral and
Title:  religious mind could contemplate with edification. The glaring insincerity
Title:  of these sermons was not sufficient to compass the banishment of the fashion
Title:  from the schools, and it is not sufficient to-day; it never will be
Title:  sufficient while the world stands, perhaps. There is no school in all our
Title:  land where the young ladies do not feel obliged to close their compositions
Title:  with a sermon; and you will find that the sermon of the most frivolous and
Title:  the least religious girl in the school is always the longest and the most
Title:  relentlessly pious. But enough of this. Homely truth is unpalatable.
Title:  
Title:     Let us return to the "Examination." The first composition that was read
Title:  was one entitled "Is this, then, Life?" Perhaps the reader can endure an
Title:  extract from it:
Title:  
Title:  
Title:  
Title:       "In the common walks of life, with what delightful emotions does
Title:       the youthful mind look forward to some anticipated scene of
Title:       festivity! Imagination is busy sketching rose-tinted pictures of
Title:       joy. In fancy, the voluptuous votary of fashion sees herself amid
Title:       the festive throng, 'the observed of all observers.' Her graceful
Title:       form, arrayed in snowy robes, is whirling through the mazes of the
Title:       joyous dance; her eye is brightest, her step is lightest in the
Title:       gay assembly.
Title:  
Title:  
Title:  
Title:       "In such delicious fancies time quickly glides by, and the welcome
Title:       hour arrives for her entrance into the Elysian world, of which she
Title:       has had such bright dreams. How fairy-like does everything appear
Title:       to her enchanted vision! Each new scene is more charming than the
Title:       last. But after a while she finds that beneath this goodly
Title:       exterior, all is vanity:
Title:       the flattery which once charmed her soul, now grates harshly upon
Title:       her ear; the ball-room has lost its charms; and with wasted health
Title:       and imbittered heart, she turns away with the conviction that
Title:       earthly pleasures cannot satisfy the longings of the soul!"
Title:  
Title:     And so forth and so on. There was a buzz of gratification from time to
Title:  time during the reading, accompanied by whispered ejaculations of "How
Title:  sweet!" "How eloquent!" "So true!" etc., and after the thing had closed with
Title:  a peculiarly afflicting sermon the applause was enthusiastic.
Title:  
Title:     Then arose a slim, melancholy girl, whose face had the "interesting"
Title:  paleness that comes of pills and indigestion, and read a "poem." Two stanzas
Title:  of it will do:
Title:  
Title:  
Title:  
Title:                     A MISSOURI MAIDEN'S FAREWELL TO ALABAMA
Title:  
Title:       "Alabama, good-bye! I love thee well!
Title:       But yet for a while do I leave thee now!
Title:       Sad, yes, sad thoughts of thee my heart doth swell,
Title:       And burning recollections throng my brow!
Title:       For I have wandered through thy flowery woods;
Title:       Have roamed and read near Tallapoosa's stream;
Title:       Have listened to Tallassee's warring floods,
Title:       And wooed on Coosa's side Aurora's beam.
Title:  
Title:       "Yet shame I not to bear an o'er-full heart,
Title:       Nor blush to turn behind my tearful eyes;
Title:       'Tis from no stranger land I now must part,
Title:       'Tis to no strangers left I yield these sighs.
Title:       Welcome and home were mine within this State,
Title:       Whose vales I leave -- whose spires fade fast from me
Title:       And cold must be mine eyes, and heart, and tete,
Title:       When, dear Alabama! they turn cold on thee!"
Title:  
Title:     There were very few there who knew what "tete"
Title:  meant, but the poem was very satisfactory, nevertheless.
Title:  
Title:     Next appeared a dark-complexioned, black-eyed, black-haired young lady,
Title:  who paused an impressive moment, assumed a tragic expression, and began to
Title:  read in a measured, solemn tone:
Title:  
Title:  
Title:  
Title:                                    A VISION
Title:  
Title:       Dark and tempestuous was night. Around the throne on high not a
Title:       single star quivered; but the deep intonations of the heavy
Title:       thunder constantly vibrated upon the ear; whilst the terrific
Title:       lightning revelled in angry mood through the cloudy chambers of
Title:       heaven, seeming to scorn the power exerted over its terror by the
Title:       illustrious Franklin! Even the boisterous winds unanimously came
Title:       forth from their mystic homes, and blustered about as if to
Title:       enhance by their aid the wildness of the scene.
Title:  
Title:  
Title:  
Title:       At such a time, so dark, so dreary, for human sympathy my very
Title:       spirit sighed; but instead thereof,
Title:  
Title:      "My dearest friend, my counsellor, my comforter and guide --
Title:  
Title:     My joy in grief, my second bliss in joy,' came to my side. She moved like
Title:  one of those bright beings pictured in the sunny walks of fancy's Eden by
Title:  the romantic and young, a queen of beauty unadorned save by her own
Title:  transcendent loveliness. So soft was her step, it failed to make even a
Title:  sound, and but for the magical thrill imparted by her genial touch, as other
Title:  unobtrusive beauties, she would have glided away un-perceived -- unsought. A
Title:  strange sadness rested upon her features, like icy tears upon the robe of
Title:  December, as she pointed to the contending elements without, and bade me
Title:  contemplate the two beings presented."
Title:  
Title:     This nightmare occupied some ten pages of manuscript and wound up with a
Title:  sermon so destructive of all hope to non-Presbyterians that it took the
Title:  first prize. This composition was considered to be the very finest effort of
Title:  the evening. The mayor of the village, in delivering the prize to the author
Title:  of it,
Title:  made a warm speech in which he said that it was by far the most "eloquent"
Title:  thing he had ever listened to, and that Daniel Webster himself might well be
Title:  proud of it.
Title:  
Title:     It may be remarked, in passing, that the number of compositions in which
Title:  the word "beauteous" was over-fondled, and human experience referred to as
Title:  "life's page," was up to the usual average.
Title:  
Title:     Now the master, mellow almost to the verge of geniality, put his chair
Title:  aside, turned his back to the audience, and began to draw a map of America
Title:  on the blackboard, to exercise the geography class upon. But he made a sad
Title:  business of it with his unsteady hand, and a smothered titter rippled over
Title:  the house. He knew what the matter was, and set himself to right it. He
Title:  sponged out lines and remade them; but he only distorted them more than
Title:  ever, and the tittering was more pronounced. He threw his entire attention
Title:  upon his work, now, as if determined not to be put down by the mirth. He
Title:  felt that all eyes were fastened upon him; he imagined he was succeeding,
Title:  and yet the tittering continued; it even manifestly increased. And well it
Title:  might. There was a garret above, pierced with a scuttle over his head; and
Title:  down through this scuttle came a cat, suspended around the haunches by a
Title:  string; she had a rag tied about her head and jaws to keep her from mewing;
Title:  as she slowly descended she curved upward and clawed at the string, she
Title:  swung downward and clawed at the intangible air.
Title:  The tittering rose higher and higher -- the cat was within six inches of the
Title:  absorbed teacher's head -- down, down, a little lower, and she grabbed his
Title:  wig with her desperate claws, clung to it, and was snatched up into the
Title:  garret in an instant with her trophy still in her possession! And how the
Title:  light did blaze abroad from the master's bald pate -- for the sign-painter's
Title:  boy had gilded it!
Title:  
Title:     That broke up the meeting. The boys were avenged. Vacation had come.
Title:  
Title:  Note: NOTE. -- The pretended "compositions" quoted in this chapter are taken
Title:  without alteration from a volume entitled "Prose and Poetry, by a Western
Title:  Lady" -- but they are exactly and precisely after the schoolgirl pattern,
Title:  and hence are much happier than any mere imitations could be.
Title:  
Title:    ------------------------------------------------------------------------
Title:  
Title:                                  Chapter XXII
Title:  
Title:     TOM joined the new order of Cadets of Temperance, being attracted by the
Title:  showy character of their "regalia." He promised to abstain from smoking,
Title:  chewing, and profanity as long as he remained a member. Now he found out a
Title:  new thing -- namely, that to promise not to do a thing is the surest way in
Title:  the world to make a body want to go and do that very thing. Tom soon found
Title:  himself tormented with a desire to drink and swear; the desire grew to be so
Title:  intense that nothing but the hope of a chance to display himself in his red
Title:  sash kept him from withdrawing from the order. Fourth of July was coming;
Title:  but he soon gave that up -- gave it up before he had worn his shackles over
Title:  forty-eight hours -- and fixed his hopes upon old Judge Frazer, justice of
Title:  the peace, who was apparently on his deathbed and would have a big public
Title:  funeral, since he was so high an official. During three days Tom was deeply
Title:  concerned about the Judge's condition and hungry for news of it. Sometimes
Title:  his hopes ran high -- so high that he would venture to get out his regalia
Title:  and practise before the looking-glass. But the Judge had a most
Title:  discouraging way of fluctuating. At last he was pronounced upon the mend --
Title:  and then convalescent. Tom was disgusted; and felt a sense of injury, too.
Title:  He handed in his resignation at once -- and that night the Judge suffered a
Title:  relapse and died. Tom resolved that he would never trust a man like that
Title:  again.
Title:  
Title:     The funeral was a fine thing. The Cadets paraded in a style calculated to
Title:  kill the late member with envy. Tom was a free boy again, however -- there
Title:  was something in that. He could drink and swear, now -- but found to his
Title:  surprise that he did not want to. The simple fact that he could, took the
Title:  desire away, and the charm of it.
Title:  
Title:     Tom presently wondered to find that his coveted vacation was beginning to
Title:  hang a little heavily on his hands.
Title:  
Title:     He attempted a diary -- but nothing happened during three days, and so he
Title:  abandoned it.
Title:  
Title:     The first of all the negro minstrel shows came to town, and made a
Title:  sensation. Tom and Joe Harper got up a band of performers and were happy for
Title:  two days.
Title:  
Title:     Even the Glorious Fourth was in some sense a failure, for it rained hard,
Title:  there was no procession in consequence, and the greatest man in the world
Title:  (as Tom supposed), Mr. Benton, an actual United States Senator, proved an
Title:  overwhelming disappointment -- for he was not twenty-five feet high, nor
Title:  even anywhere in the neighborhood of it.
Title:  
Title:     A circus came. The boys played circus for three days afterward in tents
Title:  made of rag carpeting -- admission, three pins for boys, two for girls --
Title:  and then circusing was abandoned.
Title:  
Title:     A phrenologist and a mesmerizer came -- and went again and left the
Title:  village duller and drearier than ever.
Title:  
Title:     There were some boys-and-girls' parties, but they were so few and so
Title:  delightful that they only made the aching voids between ache the harder.
Title:  
Title:     Becky Thatcher was gone to her Constantinople home to stay with her
Title:  parents during vacation -- so there was no bright side to life anywhere.
Title:  
Title:     The dreadful secret of the murder was a chronic misery. It was a very
Title:  cancer for permanency and pain.
Title:  
Title:     Then came the measles.
Title:  
Title:     During two long weeks Tom lay a prisoner, dead to the world and its
Title:  happenings. He was very ill, he was interested in nothing. When he got upon
Title:  his feet at last and moved feebly down-town, a melancholy change had come
Title:  over everything and every creature. There had been a "revival," and
Title:  everybody had "got religion," not only the adults, but even the boys and
Title:  girls. Tom went about, hoping against hope for the sight of one blessed
Title:  sinful face, but disappointment crossed him everywhere. He found Joe Harper
Title:  studying a Testament, and turned sadly away from the depressing spectacle.
Title:  He sought Ben Rogers, and found him visiting the
Title:  poor with a basket of tracts. He hunted up Jim Hollis, who called his
Title:  attention to the precious blessing of his late measles as a warning. Every
Title:  boy he encountered added another ton to his depression; and when, in
Title:  desperation, he flew for refuge at last to the bosom of Huckleberry Finn and
Title:  was received with a Scriptural quotation, his heart broke and he crept home
Title:  and to bed realizing that he alone of all the town was lost, forever and
Title:  forever.
Title:  
Title:     And that night there came on a terrific storm, with driving rain, awful
Title:  claps of thunder and blinding sheets of lightning. He covered his head with
Title:  the bedclothes and waited in a horror of suspense for his doom; for he had
Title:  not the shadow of a doubt that all this hubbub was about him. He believed he
Title:  had taxed the forbearance of the powers above to the extremity of endurance
Title:  and that this was the result. It might have seemed to him a waste of pomp
Title:  and ammunition to kill a bug with a battery of artillery, but there seemed
Title:  nothing incongruous about the getting up such an expensive thunder-storm as
Title:  this to knock the turf from under an insect like himself.
Title:  
Title:     By and by the tempest spent itself and died without accomplishing its
Title:  object. The boy's first impulse was to be grateful, and reform. His second
Title:  was to wait -- for there might not be any more storms.
Title:  
Title:     The next day the doctors were back; Tom had relapsed. The three weeks he
Title:  spent on his back
Title:  this time seemed an entire age. When he got abroad at last he was hardly
Title:  grateful that he had been spared, remembering how lonely was his estate, how
Title:  companionless and forlorn he was. He drifted listlessly down the street and
Title:  found Jim Hollis acting as judge in a juvenile court that was trying a cat
Title:  for murder, in the presence of her victim, a bird. He found Joe Harper and
Title:  Huck Finn up an alley eating a stolen melon. Poor lads! they -- like Tom --
Title:  had suffered a relapse.
Title:  
Title:    ------------------------------------------------------------------------
Title:  
Title:                                  Chapter XXIII
Title:  
Title:     AT last the sleepy atmosphere was stirred -- and vigorously: the murder
Title:  trial came on in the court. It became the absorbing topic of village talk
Title:  immediately. Tom could not get away from it. Every reference to the murder
Title:  sent a shudder to his heart, for his troubled conscience and fears almost
Title:  persuaded him that these remarks were put forth in his hearing as "feelers";
Title:  he did not see how he could be suspected of knowing anything about the
Title:  murder, but still he could not be comfortable in the midst of this gossip.
Title:  It kept him in a cold shiver all the time. He took Huck to a lonely place to
Title:  have a talk with him. It would be some relief to unseal his tongue for a
Title:  little while; to divide his burden of distress with another sufferer.
Title:  Moreover, he wanted to assure himself that Huck had remained discreet.
Title:  
Title:     "Huck, have you ever told anybody about -- that?"
Title:  
Title:     "'Bout what?"
Title:  
Title:     "You know what."
Title:  
Title:     "Oh -- 'course I haven't."
Title:  
Title:     "Never a word?"
Title:  
Title:     "Never a solitary word, so help me. What makes you ask?"
Title:  
Title:     "Well, I was afeard."
Title:  
Title:     "Why, Tom Sawyer, we wouldn't be alive two days if that got found out.
Title:  You know that."
Title:  
Title:     Tom felt more comfortable. After a pause:
Title:  
Title:     "Huck, they couldn't anybody get you to tell, could they?"
Title:  
Title:     "Get me to tell? Why, if I wanted that half-breed devil to drownd me they
Title:  could get me to tell. They ain't no different way."
Title:  
Title:     "Well, that's all right, then. I reckon we're safe as long as we keep
Title:  mum. But let's swear again, anyway. It's more surer."
Title:  
Title:     "I'm agreed."
Title:  
Title:     So they swore again with dread solemnities.
Title:  
Title:     "What is the talk around, Huck? I've heard a power of it."
Title:  
Title:     "Talk? Well, it's just Muff Potter, Muff Potter, Muff Potter all the
Title:  time. It keeps me in a sweat, constant, so's I want to hide som'ers."
Title:  
Title:     "That's just the same way they go on round me. I reckon he's a goner.
Title:  Don't you feel sorry for him, sometimes?"
Title:  
Title:     "Most always -- most always. He ain't no account; but then he hain't ever
Title:  done anything to hurt anybody. Just fishes a little, to get money to get
Title:  drunk on -- and loafs around considerable; but lord, we all do that --
Title:  leastways most of us --
Title:  preachers and such like. But he's kind of good -- he give me half a fish,
Title:  once, when there warn't enough for two; and lots of times he's kind of stood
Title:  by me when I was out of luck."
Title:  
Title:     "Well, he's mended kites for me, Huck, and knitted hooks on to my line. I
Title:  wish we could get him out of there."
Title:  
Title:     "My! we couldn't get him out, Tom. And besides, 'twouldn't do any good;
Title:  they'd ketch him again."
Title:  
Title:     "Yes -- so they would. But I hate to hear 'em abuse him so like the
Title:  dickens when he never done -- that."
Title:  
Title:     "I do too, Tom. Lord, I hear 'em say he's the bloodiest looking villain
Title:  in this country, and they wonder he wasn't ever hung before."
Title:  
Title:     "Yes, they talk like that, all the time. I've heard 'em say that if he
Title:  was to get free they'd lynch him."
Title:  
Title:     "And they'd do it, too."
Title:  
Title:     The boys had a long talk, but it brought them little comfort. As the
Title:  twilight drew on, they found themselves hanging about the neighborhood of
Title:  the little isolated jail, perhaps with an undefined hope that something
Title:  would happen that might clear away their difficulties. But nothing happened;
Title:  there seemed to be no angels or fairies interested in this luckless captive.
Title:  
Title:     The boys did as they had often done before -- went to the cell grating
Title:  and gave Potter some tobacco
Title:  and matches. He was on the ground floor and there were no guards.
Title:  
Title:     His gratitude for their gifts had always smote their consciences before
Title:  -- it cut deeper than ever, this time. They felt cowardly and treacherous to
Title:  the last degree when Potter said:
Title:  
Title:     "You've been mighty good to me, boys -- better'n anybody else in this
Title:  town. And I don't forget it, I don't. Often I says to myself, says I, 'I
Title:  used to mend all the boys' kites and things, and show 'em where the good
Title:  fishin' places was, and befriend 'em what I could, and now they've all
Title:  forgot old Muff when he's in trouble; but Tom don't, and Huck don't -- they
Title:  don't forget him, says I, 'and I don't forget them.' Well, boys, I done an
Title:  awful thing -- drunk and crazy at the time -- that's the only way I account
Title:  for it -- and now I got to swing for it, and it's right. Right, and best,
Title:  too, I reckon -- hope so, anyway. Well, we won't talk about that. I don't
Title:  want to make you feel bad; you've befriended me. But what I want to say, is,
Title:  don't you ever get drunk -- then you won't ever get here. Stand a litter
Title:  furder west -- so -- that's it; it's a prime comfort to see faces that's
Title:  friendly when a body's in such a muck of trouble, and there don't none come
Title:  here but yourn. Good friendly faces -- good friendly faces. Git up on one
Title:  another's backs and let me touch 'em. That's it. Shake hands -- yourn'll
Title:  come through the bars, but mine's too big. Little hands, and weak -- but
Title:  they've helped Muff
Title:  Potter a power, and they'd help him more if they could."
Title:  
Title:     Tom went home miserable, and his dreams that night were full of horrors.
Title:  The next day and the day after, he hung about the court-room, drawn by an
Title:  almost irresistible impulse to go in, but forcing himself to stay out. Huck
Title:  was having the same experience. They studiously avoided each other. Each
Title:  wandered away, from time to time, but the same dismal fascination always
Title:  brought them back presently. Tom kept his ears open when idlers sauntered
Title:  out of the court-room, but invariably heard distressing news -- the toils
Title:  were closing more and more relentlessly around poor Potter. At the end of
Title:  the second day the village talk was to the effect that Injun Joe's evidence
Title:  stood firm and unshaken, and that there was not the slightest question as to
Title:  what the jury's verdict would be.
Title:  
Title:     Tom was out late, that night, and came to bed through the window. He was
Title:  in a tremendous state of excitement. It was hours before he got to sleep.
Title:  All the village flocked to the court-house the next morning, for this was to
Title:  be the great day. Both sexes were about equally represented in the packed
Title:  audience. After a long wait the jury filed in and took their places; shortly
Title:  afterward, Potter, pale and haggard, timid and hopeless, was brought in,
Title:  with chains upon him, and seated where all the curious eyes could stare at
Title:  him; no less conspicuous was Injun Joe, stolid as ever. There was another
Title:  pause, and then the judge arrived and the sheriff proclaimed the opening of
Title:  the court. The usual whisperings among the lawyers and gathering together of
Title:  papers followed. These details and accompanying delays worked up an
Title:  atmosphere of preparation that was as impressive as it was fascinating.
Title:  
Title:     Now a witness was called who testified that he found Muff Potter washing
Title:  in the brook, at an early hour of the morning that the murder was
Title:  discovered, and that he immediately sneaked away. After some further
Title:  questioning, counsel for the prosecution said:
Title:  
Title:     "Take the witness."
Title:  
Title:     The prisoner raised his eyes for a moment, but dropped them again when
Title:  his own counsel said:
Title:  
Title:     "I have no questions to ask him."
Title:  
Title:     The next witness proved the finding of the knife near the corpse. Counsel
Title:  for the prosecution said:
Title:  
Title:     "Take the witness."
Title:  
Title:     "I have no questions to ask him," Potter's lawyer replied.
Title:  
Title:     A third witness swore he had often seen the knife in Potter's possession.
Title:  
Title:     "Take the witness."
Title:  
Title:     Counsel for Potter declined to question him. The faces of the audience
Title:  began to betray annoyance. Did this attorney mean to throw away his client's
Title:  life without an effort?
Title:  
Title:     Several witnesses deposed concerning Potter's guilty behavior when
Title:  brought to the scene of the
Title:  murder. They were allowed to leave the stand without being cross-questioned.
Title:  
Title:     Every detail of the damaging circumstances that occurred in the graveyard
Title:  upon that morning which all present remembered so well was brought out by
Title:  credible witnesses, but none of them were cross-examined by Potter's lawyer.
Title:  The perplexity and dissatisfaction of the house expressed itself in murmurs
Title:  and provoked a reproof from the bench. Counsel for the prosecution now said:
Title:  
Title:     "By the oaths of citizens whose simple word is above suspicion, we have
Title:  fastened this awful crime, beyond all possibility of question, upon the
Title:  unhappy prisoner at the bar. We rest our case here."
Title:  
Title:     A groan escaped from poor Potter, and he put his face in his hands and
Title:  rocked his body softly to and fro, while a painful silence reigned in the
Title:  court-room. Many men were moved, and many women's compassion testified
Title:  itself in tears. Counsel for the defence rose and said:
Title:  
Title:     "Your honor, in our remarks at the opening of this trial, we foreshadowed
Title:  our purpose to prove that our client did this fearful deed while under the
Title:  influence of a blind and irresponsible delirium produced by drink. We have
Title:  changed our mind. We shall not offer that plea." [Then to the clerk:] "Call
Title:  Thomas Sawyer!"
Title:  
Title:     A puzzled amazement awoke in every face in the house, not even excepting
Title:  Potter's. Every eye fastened itself with wondering interest upon Tom as he
Title:  rose and took his place upon the stand. The boy looked wild enough, for he
Title:  was badly scared. The oath was administered.
Title:  
Title:     "Thomas Sawyer, where were you on the seventeenth of June, about the hour
Title:  of midnight?"
Title:  
Title:     Tom glanced at Injun Joe's iron face and his tongue failed him. The
Title:  audience listened breathless, but the words refused to come. After a few
Title:  moments, however, the boy got a little of his strength back, and managed to
Title:  put enough of it into his voice to make part of the house hear:
Title:  
Title:     "In the graveyard!"
Title:  
Title:     "A little bit louder, please. Don't be afraid. You were -- "
Title:  
Title:     "In the graveyard."
Title:  
Title:     A contemptuous smile flitted across Injun Joe's face.
Title:  
Title:     "Were you anywhere near Horse Williams' grave?"
Title:  
Title:     "Yes, sir."
Title:  
Title:     "Speak up -- just a trifle louder. How near were you?"
Title:  
Title:     "Near as I am to you."
Title:  
Title:     "Were you hidden, or not?"
Title:  
Title:     "I was hid."
Title:  
Title:     "Where?"
Title:  
Title:     "Behind the elms that's on the edge of the grave."
Title:  
Title:     Injun Joe gave a barely perceptible start.
Title:  
Title:     "Any one with you?"
Title:  
Title:     "Yes, sir. I went there with -- "
Title:  
Title:     "Wait -- wait a moment. Never mind mentioning your companion's name. We
Title:  will produce him at the proper time. Did you carry anything there with you."
Title:  
Title:     Tom hesitated and looked confused.
Title:  
Title:     "Speak out, my boy -- don't be diffident. The truth is always
Title:  respectable. What did you take there?"
Title:  
Title:     "Only a -- a -- dead cat."
Title:  
Title:     There was a ripple of mirth, which the court checked.
Title:  
Title:     "We will produce the skeleton of that cat. Now, my boy, tell us
Title:  everything that occurred -- tell it in your own way -- don't skip anything,
Title:  and don't be afraid."
Title:  
Title:     Tom began -- hesitatingly at first, but as he warmed to his subject his
Title:  words flowed more and more easily; in a little while every sound ceased but
Title:  his own voice; every eye fixed itself upon him; with parted lips and bated
Title:  breath the audience hung upon his words, taking no note of time, rapt in the
Title:  ghastly fascinations of the tale. The strain upon pent emotion reached its
Title:  climax when the boy said:
Title:  
Title:     " -- and as the doctor fetched the board around and Muff Potter fell,
Title:  Injun Joe jumped with the knife and -- "
Title:  
Title:     Crash! Quick as lightning the half-breed sprang for a window, tore his
Title:  way through all opposers, and was gone!
Title:  
Title:    ------------------------------------------------------------------------
Title:  
Title:                                  Chapter XXIV
Title:  
Title:     TOM was a glittering hero once more -- the pet of the old, the envy of
Title:  the young. His name even went into immortal print, for the village paper
Title:  magnified him. There were some that believed he would be President, yet, if
Title:  he escaped hanging.
Title:  
Title:     As usual, the fickle, unreasoning world took Muff Potter to its bosom and
Title:  fondled him as lavishly as it had abused him before. But that sort of
Title:  conduct is to the world's credit; therefore it is not well to find fault
Title:  with it.
Title:  
Title:     Tom's days were days of splendor and exultation to him, but his nights
Title:  were seasons of horror. Injun Joe infested all his dreams, and always with
Title:  doom in his eye. Hardly any temptation could persuade the boy to stir abroad
Title:  after nightfall. Poor Huck was in the same state of wretchedness and terror,
Title:  for Tom had told the whole story to the lawyer the night before the great
Title:  day of the trial, and Huck was sore afraid that his share in the business
Title:  might leak out, yet, notwithstanding Injun Joe's flight had saved him the
Title:  suffering of testifying in court. The poor fellow had got the attorney to
Title:  promise secrecy, but
Title:  what of that? Since Tom's harassed conscience had managed to drive him to
Title:  the lawyer's house by night and wring a dread tale from lips that had been
Title:  sealed with the dismalest and most formidable of oaths, Huck's confidence in
Title:  the human race was well-nigh obliterated.
Title:  
Title:     Daily Muff Potter's gratitude made Tom glad he had spoken; but nightly he
Title:  wished he had sealed up his tongue.
Title:  
Title:     Half the time Tom was afraid Injun Joe would never be captured; the other
Title:  half he was afraid he would be. He felt sure he never could draw a safe
Title:  breath again until that man was dead and he had seen the corpse.
Title:  
Title:     Rewards had been offered, the country had been scoured, but no Injun Joe
Title:  was found. One of those omniscient and awe-inspiring marvels, a detective,
Title:  came up from St. Louis, moused around, shook his head, looked wise, and made
Title:  that sort of astounding success which members of that craft usually achieve.
Title:  That is to say, he "found a clew." But you can't hang a "clew" for murder,
Title:  and so after that detective had got through and gone home, Tom felt just as
Title:  insecure as he was before.
Title:  
Title:     The slow days drifted on, and each left behind it a slightly lightened
Title:  weight of apprehension.
Title:  
Title:    ------------------------------------------------------------------------
Title:  
Title:                                   Chapter XXV
Title:  
Title:     THERE comes a time in every rightly-constructed boy's life when he has a
Title:  raging desire to go somewhere and dig for hidden treasure. This desire
Title:  suddenly came upon Tom one day. He sallied out to find Joe Harper, but
Title:  failed of success. Next he sought Ben Rogers; he had gone fishing. Presently
Title:  he stumbled upon Huck Finn the Red-Handed. Huck would answer. Tom took him
Title:  to a private place and opened the matter to him confidentially. Huck was
Title:  willing. Huck was always willing to take a hand in any enterprise that
Title:  offered entertainment and required no capital, for he had a troublesome
Title:  superabundance of that sort of time which is not money. "Where'll we dig?"
Title:  said Huck.
Title:  
Title:     "Oh, most anywhere."
Title:  
Title:     "Why, is it hid all around?"
Title:  
Title:     "No, indeed it ain't. It's hid in mighty particular places, Huck --
Title:  sometimes on islands, sometimes in rotten chests under the end of a limb of
Title:  an old dead tree, just where the shadow falls at midnight; but mostly under
Title:  the floor in ha'nted houses."
Title:  
Title:     "Who hides it?"
Title:  
Title:     "Why, robbers, of course -- who'd you reckon? Sunday-school
Title:  sup'rintendents?"
Title:  
Title:     "I don't know. If 'twas mine I wouldn't hide it; I'd spend it and have a
Title:  good time."
Title:  
Title:     "So would I. But robbers don't do that way. They always hide it and leave
Title:  it there."
Title:  
Title:     "Don't they come after it any more?"
Title:  
Title:     "No, they think they will, but they generally forget the marks, or else
Title:  they die. Anyway, it lays there a long time and gets rusty; and by and by
Title:  somebody finds an old yellow paper that tells how to find the marks -- a
Title:  paper that's got to be ciphered over about a week because it's mostly signs
Title:  and hy'roglyphics."
Title:  
Title:     "Hyro which?"
Title:  
Title:     "Hy'roglyphics -- pictures and things, you know, that don't seem to mean
Title:  anything."
Title:  
Title:     "Have you got one of them papers, Tom?"
Title:  
Title:     "No."
Title:  
Title:     "Well then, how you going to find the marks?"
Title:  
Title:     "I don't want any marks. They always bury it under a ha'nted house or on
Title:  an island, or under a dead tree that's got one limb sticking out. Well,
Title:  we've tried Jackson's Island a little, and we can try it again some time;
Title:  and there's the old ha'nted house up the Still-House branch, and there's
Title:  lots of deadlimb trees -- dead loads of 'em."
Title:  
Title:     "Is it under all of them?"
Title:  
Title:     "How you talk! No!"
Title:  
Title:     "Then how you going to know which one to go for?"
Title:  
Title:     "Go for all of 'em!"
Title:  
Title:     "Why, Tom, it'll take all summer."
Title:  
Title:     "Well, what of that? Suppose you find a brass pot with a hundred dollars
Title:  in it, all rusty and gray, or rotten chest full of di'monds. How's that?"
Title:  
Title:     Huck's eyes glowed.
Title:  
Title:     "That's bully. Plenty bully enough for me. Just you gimme the hundred
